والمتعارف في بعض البلاد الآن كالشام والحجاز ليس ذلك بل وزن ربع وقيراط الدرهم . وأما في عرف مصر لفظ الدرهم ينصرف الآن إلى زنة أربعة دراهم بوزن سبعة من الفلوس إلا أن يقيد بالفضة فينصرف إلى درهم بوزن سبعة فإن ما دونه ثقل أو خفة يسمونه نصف فضة اهـ . وعلى هذا إذا شرط بعض الواقفين بمصر للمستحق دراهم ولم يقيدها تنصرف إلى الفلوس النحاس، وأما إذا قيدها بالنقرة كواقف الشيخونية والصرغتمشية تنصرف إلى الفضة لما في المغرب : النقرة القطعة المذابة من الذهب أو الفضة، ويقال نقرة فضة على الإضافة للبيان ا هـ. وفي المصباح : النقرة القطعة المذابة من الفضة وقبل الذوب هي تبر ا هـ . قوله: (وعلى هذا إذا شرط بعض الواقفين بمصر (الخ قال في النهر : ولا يخفى أن كون الدراهم تنصرف إلى الفلوس في شروط الواقفين بمصر مطلقاً أخذاً مما في الفتح فيه نظر إذ غاية ما فيه الإحالة على زمنه ولا يلزم منه أن يكون في كل زمن كذلك، والذي ينبغي أن لا يعدل عنه اعتبار من الواقف إن عرف فإن لم يعرف صرف إلى الفضة لأنه الأصل. وأما قيمة كل درهم منها اهـ. ثم قال في النهر بعد كلام طويل فعلى هذا فقيمة الدرهم في الشيخونية والصرغتمشية ونحوهما نصفان وهذا النقل هو المعول عليه دون غيره والله تعالى أعلم. قوله: وفي الجوهرة من الرهن من كان له على رجل درهم فأعطاه درهمين صغيرين وزنهما درهم جاز ويجبر على قبض ذلك، ولو كان له دينار فأعطاه دينارين صغيرين وزنهما دينار فأبى لم يجبر على ذلك اهـ . وفي الواقعات الحسامية من كتاب الصلح وقال أبو يوسف : إذا اقتضى دراهم فأنفقها ثم ردت عليه بعيب الزيافة، فإن كان أنها زائفة فله أن يردها سواء قبلها بقضاء أو بغير قضاء. فرق بين هذا المبيع إذا قبله البائع بغير قضاء ليس له أن يرده، والفرق أن هناك الرد إذا كان بغير قضاء جعل عقداً جديداً في حق الثالث وهو البائع، أما هنا لا يمكن أن يجعل بيعاً جديداً لأنه لم يملك الرد على ما قدمناه وقال أبو يوسف من أقرض كر حنطة عفن وقبضها المستقرض حين أنفقها واستهلكها ثم قضاه كر حنطة جيدة، فإن كان قال له الطالب لي عليك حنطة طيبة وصدقه المطلوب ثم قضاه ثم تصادقا أن الكر القرض كان عفناً فللمستقرض أن يرجع فيما قضاه ويعطيه كراً عفناً مثل القرض، فإن لم يكن الطالب قال له كري جيد لكن المستقرض قضاه من غير شرط جاز وليس له أن يرجع . قلت : ويحتمل أن يكون جواب الوجه الأول به جيداً. فقال في البحر بعدما أعاد المسألة في الصرف قد وقع الاشتباه في أنها خالصة أو مغشوشة وكنت قد استفتيت بعض المالكية عنها يعني به علامة عصره ناصر الدين اللقاني فأفتى أنه ممن يوثق سمع الدرهم منها يساوي نصفاً وثلاثة من الفلوس قال : فليعول على ذلك ما لم يوجد خلافه اهـ. وقد اعتبر ذلك في زماننا لأن الأدنى متيقن به وما زاد عليه فهو مشكوك فيه، ولكن الأوفق بفروع مذهبنا وجوب درهم وسط لما في جامع الفصولين من دعوى النقرة: لو تزوجها على مائة درهم نقرة ولم يصفها صح العقد، ولو ادعت مائة درهم وجب لها مائة وسط اهـ. فينبغي أن يعول عليه اهـ. ثم قال في النهر بعد كلام طويل فعلى هذا فقيمة الدرهم في الشيخونية والصرغتمشية ونحوهما نصفان وهذا النقل هو المعول عليه دون غيره والله تعالى أعلم. قوله:
And the customary practice in some countries now, like Syria and the Hijaz, is not that, but rather a weight of a quarter and a carat of the dirham. And in the custom of Egypt, the word 'dirham' now applies to a weight of four dirhams by weight of seven from the copper coins (fulus), unless it is restricted by 'silver', then it applies to a dirham of weight seven; and what is less than that in weight or lightness they call 'half silver'. Based on this, if some endower in Egypt stipulates dirhams for the beneficiary and does not restrict it, it applies to copper coins (flus). And if he restricts it by 'nuqrah', like the endowment of al-Shaykhuniyya and al-Sarghatmishiyya, it applies to silver, because in al-Maghrib: al-nuqrah is a melted piece of gold or silver, and 'nuqrah silver' is said with the genitive for clarification. And in al-Misbah: al-nuqrah is a melted piece of silver, and before melting it is 'tibr'. His saying: (And based on this if some endower in Egypt (etc.) said in al-Nahr: It is not hidden that dirhams applying to copper coins in the conditions of endowers in Egypt absolutely, taking from what is in al-Fath, is open to consideration, because its utmost is reference to his time, and it does not necessitate that it is always like that. What is appropriate is not to deviate from considering the intent of the endower if known, and if unknown, it applies to silver because it is the default. And as for the value of each dirham of them, etc. Then he said in al-Nahr after lengthy speech: Based on this, the value of a dirham in al-Shaykhuniyya and al-Sarghatmishiyya and the like is half and half, and this report is the relied-upon without other, and Allah knows best. His saying: And in al-Jawhara from the book of Rahn: If someone has a dirham owed to him and he gives him two small dirhams whose weight is one dirham, it is valid and he is compelled to accept that. And if he owed a dinar and gave him two small dinars weighing one dinar, and he refused, he is not compelled to accept that. In al-Waqi'at al-Husamiyya from the book of Sulh, Abu Yusuf said: If a person collected dirhams and spent them, then they were returned to him due to a defect of being bad, and if they are bad, he has the right to return them whether he accepted them in settlement or without settlement. There is a distinction between this and a sale: if the seller accepts it without settlement, he does not have the right to return it. The difference is that there, the return without settlement is considered a new contract in relation to the third party, the seller. Here, it is not possible to make it a new sale because he did not own the return as we have presented. And Abu Yusuf said: If someone lent a quantity of rotten wheat, and the borrower took it, spent it, and consumed it, then repaid him with a quantity of good wheat: if the claimant said 'I have good wheat from you' and the defendant confirmed, then he repaid, then they both admitted that the loan was rotten, then the borrower has the right to take back what he repaid and give him a quantity like the rotten original loan. But if the claimant did not say 'my wheat is good' but the borrower repaid without any condition, it is valid and he has no right to take it back. I say: It is possible that the answer to the first aspect is good. Then he said in al-Bahr after repeating the issue in sarf: There was confusion about whether it is pure or mixed, and I had sought a fatwa from some Malikis, meaning by it the scholar of his time, Nasir al-Din al-Laqqani. He gave a fatwa that he is trustworthy: the dirham from it equals half and three from the copper coins. He said: So rely on that as long as no opposite is found. And that has been considered in our time because the lowest is certain, and what is above it is doubtful. But more consistent with the branches of our madhhab is the obligation of a medium dirham, because in Jami' al-Fusulayn about a claim of nuqrah: If he married her for one hundred dirhams of nuqrah without describing them, the contract is valid. If she claims one hundred dirhams, she is owed one hundred medium dirhams. So it is appropriate to rely on that. Then he said in al-Nahr after lengthy speech: Based on this, the value of a dirham in al-Shaykhuniyya and al-Sarghatmishiyya and the like is half and half, and this report is the relied-upon without other, and Allah knows best. His saying:
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage addresses the interpretation of 'dirham' in different regions and specifically in waqf (endowment) conditions in Egypt. The author first notes that in Syria and Hijaz, the term dirham refers to a specific weight, while in Egypt the common usage (urf) is that the unqualified word 'dirham' refers to a certain weight of copper coins (فلوس), specifically four dirhams by weight of seven copper coins. If qualified by 'silver' (فضة), it refers to a silver dirham of weight seven. This custom affects the interpretation of waqf conditions: if an endower in Egypt stipulates 'dirham' without qualification, it is understood as copper coins. However, if he qualifies it with 'nuqrah' (which means a piece of melted silver), as in the endowments of al-Shaykhuniyya and al-Sarghatmishiyya, it is understood as silver. The author then quotes al-Nahr, which critiques a blanket application of this rule from the book al-Fath, arguing that it depends on the time and the endower's intent. If the endower's intent is unknown, the default should be silver because that is the default currency. The passage then includes several subsidiary rulings: in al-Jawhara, a person owed one dirham can be compelled to accept two small dirhams totaling that weight, but not two small dinars for one dinar. From al-Waqi'at al-Husamiyya, if a creditor receives bad coins and spends them, then the debtor returns them, the creditor can return them to the debtor (whether the acceptance was in settlement or not), unlike the case of a sale where return without settlement creates a new contract. Then a ruling from Abu Yusuf on a loan of rotten wheat repaid with good: if the lender claimed the loan was good and the borrower agreed, then repaid good, then both admit the loan was rotten, the borrower can reclaim the good and give rotten; otherwise, if no condition, the repayment stands. Finally, the author discusses the value of a dirham in endowments, citing a fatwa from a Maliki scholar that the dirham equals half and three copper coins, but the preferred Hanafi view is to take a medium dirham, as per Jami' al-Fusulayn. The overall ruling is that the interpretation of dirham in waqf conditions follows the known intent of the endower or, failing that, defaults to silver.

Key Terms
نقرة (nuqrah): A piece of melted silver (or gold), used in waqf to specify silver dirhams as opposed to copper.
درهم (dirham): In Egyptian custom, when unqualified, refers to copper coins (فلوس) of a specific weight; when qualified with 'فضة' or 'نقرة', it refers to silver.
فلوس (fulus): Copper coins used in Egyptian custom as the default meaning of unqualified 'dirham'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Egyptian custom described, if a waqf in Egypt stipulates 'one hundred dirhams' for a beneficiary without qualification, what does it mean?
A) It means one hundred silver dirhams.
B) It means one hundred copper coins (fulus).
C) It is void due to ambiguity.
D) It must be interpreted by a judge as half silver, half copper.

Key Takeaway
The interpretation of ambiguous terms in waqf conditions depends on custom and the endower's intent; in Egypt, unqualified 'dirham' means copper, but silver is the default if intent unknown.

Classification of Defective Coins (Zuyūf, Sutūqah, Nubahrjah)
Defines three categories of defective coins and states the genus rule.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify coins as zuyūf, sutūqah, or nubahrjah and explain why the genus distinction affects liability in repayment.

Core Idea
Zuyūf are of the same genus as lawful currency; sutūqah and nubahrjah are not — this changes repayment rules.

In Hanafi commercial fiqh, not all defective coins are treated equally. The key distinction is whether the defective coin is of the same genus (jins) as the genuine currency or a different substance altogether. This lesson examines the three categories defined by classical Hanafi jurists: الزيوف (zuyūf), الستوقة (sutūqah), and النبهرجة (nubahrjah). Understanding these categories is essential for determining proper liability in transactions and debts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three coin types
Read the definitions provided by Abu al-Nasr and Abu Ja'far. Note the characteristics: zuyūf are adulterated but silver-based; sutūqah are copper coated with silver; nubahrjah are struck outside the official mint.
Pay attention to the material composition.
2
Determine the genus rule
The passage explicitly states that zuyūf are of the same genus (jins) as the creditor's right, while sutūqah and nubahrjah are not. This is the crucial legal distinction.
Think about why genus matters in Hanafi mu'āmalāt.
3
Understand the liability consequence
For coins of the same genus (zuyūf), the debtor must return the same type (mithl). For coins of a different genus, the debtor owes the value (qīmah) of the genuine coins.
This rule applies to destruction or loss.
4
Recognize practical identification
Note the lexicographical and customary descriptions: zuyūf are mercury-sulfur coated dirhams; sutūqah are silver-washed copper; nubahrjah are non-mint strike and often not accepted by merchants.
These descriptions help in real-world detection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العلم لأنه لو علم بها وأنفقها كان قضاء اتفاقاً وقيد بالزيوف لأنها لو كانت ستوقة أو نبهرجة فأتلفها فإنه يرد مثلها ويرجع بالجياد اتفاقاً وهما فرقا بأن الزيوف من جنس حقه والستوقة والنبهرجة لا . وفي المصباح : زافت الدراهم تزيف زيفاً من باب «سار» ردأت ثم وصف بالمصدر فقيل درهم زيف مثل فلس وفلوس وربما قيل زائف على الأصل ودراهم زيف مثل راكع وركع، وزيفتها تزييفاً أظهرت زيفها . قال بعضهم: الدراهم الزيوف هي المطلية بالزئبق المعقود بمزاوجة الكبريت وكانت معروفة قبل زمانا وقدرها مثل سنج الميزان وفي الواقعات الحسامية من البيع تكلموا في معرفة الزيوف والنبهرجة. قال أبو النصر : الزيوف دراهم مغشوشة، أما النبهرجة التي تضرب في غير دار السلطان والستوقة صفر مموه بالفضة. وقال الفقيه أبو جعفر : الزيوف ما زيفه بيت المال يقال في عرفنا غطريقي لا غير والنبهرجة ما لا يقبله التاجر ا هـ. وفي الجوهرة من الرهن من كان له على رجل درهم فأعطاه درهمين صغيرين وزنهما درهم جاز ويجبر على قبض ذلك، ولو كان له دينار فأعطاه دينارين صغيرين وزنهما دينار فأبى لم يجبر على ذلك اهـ . وفي الواقعات الحسامية من كتاب الصلح وقال أبو يوسف : إذا اقتضى دراهم فأنفقها ثم ردت عليه بعيب الزيافة، فإن كان أنها زائفة فله أن يردها سواء قبلها بقضاء أو بغير قضاء. فرق بين هذا المبيع إذا قبله البائع بغير قضاء ليس له أن يرده، والفرق أن هناك الرد إذا كان بغير قضاء جعل عقداً جديداً في حق الثالث وهو البائع، أما هنا لا يمكن أن يجعل بيعاً جديداً لأنه لم يملك الرد على ما قدمناه وقال أبو يوسف من أقرض كر حنطة عفن وقبضها المستقرض حين أنفقها يعلم وبين وواستهلكها ثم قضاه كر حنطة جيدة، فإن كان قال له الطالب لي عليك حنطة طيبة وصدقه المطلوب ثم قضاه ثم تصادقا أن الكر القرض كان عفناً فللمستقرض أن . فيما قضاه يرجع ويعطيه كراً عفناً مثل القرض، فإن لم يكن الطالب قال له كري حيد لكن المستقرض قضاه من غير شرط جاز وليس له أن يرجع . قلت : ويحتمل أن يكون جواب الوجه الأول جيداً. به 6 فقال في البحر بعدما أعاد المسألة في الصرف قد وقع الاشتباه في أنها خالصة أو مغشوشة وكنت قد استفتيت بعض المالكية عنها يعني به علامة عصره ناصر الدين اللقاني فأفتى أنه ممن يوثق سمع الدرهم منها يساوي نصفاً وثلاثة من الفلوس قال : فليعول على ذلك ما لم يوجد خلافه اهـ. وقد اعتبر ذلك في زماننا لأن الأدنى متيقن به وما زاد عليه فهو مشكوك فيه، ولكن الأوفق بفروع مذهبنا وجوب درهم وسط لما في جامع الفصولين من دعوى النقرة: لو تزوجها على مائة درهم نقرة ولم يصفها صح العقد، ولو ادعت مائة درهم وجب لها مائة وسط اهـ. فينبغي أن يعول عليه اهـ. ثم قال في النهر بعد كلام طويل فعلى هذا فقيمة الدرهم في الشيخونية والصرغتمشية ونحوهما نصفان وهذا النقل هو المعول عليه دون غيره والله تعالى أعلم.
Knowledge because if he knew about them [defective coins] and spent them, it was considered repayment by agreement. And it was restricted to الزيوف because if they were ستوقة or نبهرجة and he destroyed them, then he returns their like and recourse for good [coins] by agreement. And both [types] differ because الزيوف are of the same genus as his right, while الستوقة and النبهرجة are not. And in Al-Misbah: The dirhams became defective (zāfat) from the verb from the door of 'Sāra', meaning they became bad, then described by the infinitive, so it is said dirham zayf like fals and fulus, and sometimes zā'if is said on the original, and dirhams zuyūf like rāki' and ruku'. And you make them defective (zayyafatā) showing their defect. Some said: الزيوف dirhams are those coated with mercury mixed with sulfur, known in our time, and their weight is like the scale weight. And in Al-Waqi'at al-Husamiyya from the book of sales: they spoke about knowing الزيوف and النبهرجة. Abu al-Nasr said: الزيوف are adulterated dirhams, as for النبهرجة which are struck outside the sultan's mint, and الستوقة are copper coated with silver. And Faqih Abu Ja'far said: الزيوف are what the treasury rejects, in our custom only غطريقي [unknown], and النبهرجة is what the merchant does not accept. End. And in Al-Jawhara from the book of mortgage: whoever has a dirham owed to him and [the debtor] gives him two small dirhams weighing one dirham, it is permissible and he is forced to accept them. And if he had a dinar and [the debtor] gives him two small dinars weighing one dinar, and he refuses, he is not forced to accept that. End. And in Al-Waqi'at al-Husamiyya from the book of reconciliation: Abu Yusuf said: If he collected dirhams [as payment] and spent them, then they were returned to him due to the defect of being counterfeit, then if they are counterfeit, he has the right to return them whether he accepted them by judgment or without judgment. There is a difference between this and a sold [item] if the seller accepted it without judgment, he does not have the right to return it. And the difference is that there the return without judgment is made a new contract regarding the third party [seller], but here it cannot be made a new sale because he did not own the return based on what we have presented. And Abu Yusuf said: Whoever lends a karr of spoiled wheat, and the borrower took it and spent it knowingly and clearly and consumed it, then [the borrower] repaid him with a karr of good wheat. If the claimant said: I have good wheat on you, and the defendant confirmed him, then he repaid him, then they both discovered that the lent karr was spoiled, then the borrower has the right to take back what he repaid and give him a spoiled karr like the loan. If the claimant did not say to him: My karr is good, but the borrower repaid without condition, it is permissible and he has no right to take back. I say: It is possible that the answer of the first aspect is good. ... So he said in Al-Bahr after repeating the issue in exchange: confusion occurred whether it is pure or adulterated. I had sought a fatwa from some Malikis about it, meaning the scholar of his time Nasir al-Din al-Laqani, and he gave a fatwa that he is reliable: the dirham from it is worth half and three fils. He said: Reliance should be on that as long as no difference is found. End. And this was considered in our time because the lower bound is certain and above it is doubtful. But more consistent with the branches of our madhhab is the obligation of a medium dirham, as in Jami' al-Fusulayn from the claim of pure silver: if he marries her for one hundred dirhams of pure silver and does not describe it, the contract is valid, and if she claims one hundred dirhams, she is owed one hundred medium dirhams. End. So it is appropriate to rely on it. End. Then he said in Al-Nahr after lengthy speech: so on this, the value of the dirham in al-Shaykhuniyya and al-Sarghatmishiyya and similar is half and half, this transmission is the relied upon, not other. And Allah most high knows best.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling discussion from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, expanding on various types of defective coins and their legal implications. It begins by distinguishing between الزيوف (counterfeit coins of the same genus as the rightful currency) and types like الستوقة (copper plated with silver) and النبهرجة (coins struck outside official mints, often not accepted by merchants). The author cites lexicographical sources and definitions from scholars like Abu al-Nasr and Abu Ja'far, establishing that الزيوف are adulterated but still within the category of dirhams, while the other types are not of the same genus. This distinction affects liability: if someone destroys coins of the same genus, they must return similar coins; otherwise, they return the equivalent value. The passage then presents a ruling from Abu Yusuf regarding debt repayment: if a debtor pays with coins that are later found to be defective (الزيافة), the creditor can return them regardless of whether the payment was by judgment or voluntarily, unlike the sale of a defective item where return without judgment is not allowed. The key difference is that in sale, the return creates a new contract; in debt, the creditor never owned the right to return the defective coins as such. Another ruling from Abu Yusuf deals with a loan of spoiled wheat: if the borrower knowingly consumes it and later repays with good wheat, but had admitted to owing good wheat, the borrower can retract and give spoiled wheat like the original loan; if no such admission was made, the repayment is valid and cannot be retracted. The passage concludes with a fatwa from a Maliki scholar on determining the value of coins, and a recommendation to rely on a medium dirham standard consistent with Hanafi principles. The authority weight is from Fatawa later than Zahir al-Riwayah, as it cites later sources like Al-Nahr and Jami' al-Fusulayn.

Key Terms
زيوف (zuyūf): Counterfeit dirhams that are adulterated but made from the same material as genuine dirhams (silver), often coated with mercury and sulfur.
ستوقة (sutūqah): Copper coins coated with silver to appear as silver dirhams.
نبهرجة (nubahrjah): Coins struck outside the sultan's mint, often not accepted by merchants.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason that liability differs between zuyūf coins and sutūqah coins?
A) Zuyūf are more common than sutūqah.
B) Zuyūf are of the same genus as the lawful currency, while sutūqah are not.
C) Sutūqah are heavier than zuyūf.
D) Zuyūf are accepted by the treasury, sutūqah are not.

Key Takeaway
The genus of a defective coin determines whether replacement or value compensation applies.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
12 min
Debt Repayment with Defective Coins — Abu Yusuf's Rulings
Presents two rulings by Abu Yusuf on defective coin repayment and spoiled wheat loan, plus a valuation standard.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Abu Yusuf's rulings on returning defective coins and repaying loans of spoiled commodities.

Core Idea
A creditor can return defective coins even if accepted voluntarily; a borrower can retract repayment if the lender admitted to owing good quality.

The source passage presents two rulings from Imam Abu Yusuf that clarify the rights of parties in transactions involving defective items. The first ruling addresses when a creditor who accepted payment in dirhams later discovers they were counterfeit (zuyūf). The second ruling deals with a loan of spoiled wheat where the borrower repaid with good wheat after confirming the loan's quality. Both rulings hinge on the presence of a condition or admission. This lesson explores these cases and their underlying rationale, and also touches on the Hanafi preference for a medium dirham valuation standard.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Yusuf's first ruling
Read the passage: 'إذا اقتضى دراهم فأنفقها ثم ردت عليه بعيب الزيافة ... فله أن يردها سواء قبلها بقضاء أو بغير قضاء.' This means if a creditor accepts and spends dirhams, then later discovers they are counterfeit, he can return them and demand good dirhams, regardless of whether he accepted them by court judgment or voluntarily.
Note the phrase 'بقضاء أو بغير قضاء' – it covers both formal and informal acceptance.
2
Compare with the sale of a defective item
Abu Yusuf distinguishes this from a sale where the seller accepts the return of a defective item without a judgment; in that case, the return creates a new contract and is not allowed. Here, in debt repayment, the return does not create a new contract because the creditor never owned the right to return the defective coins.
This distinction is critical – understand how the legal nature of debt vs. sale affects the right to rescind.
3
State Abu Yusuf's second ruling on spoiled wheat
A borrower who knowingly consumed spoiled wheat and later repaid with good wheat. If the lender had claimed 'I lent you good wheat' and the borrower admitted, then the borrower can retract the repayment and give spoiled wheat like the original loan. If no such admission occurred, the repayment stands.
The condition is the lender's claim that the loan was of good quality, confirmed by the borrower.
4
Understand the medium dirham standard
The passage concludes with a fatwa that in cases of doubt about coin purity, the Hanafi school obligates a medium dirham (درهم وسط) rather than the lower bound used by some Malikis. This is derived from the principle that certainty (lower bound) cannot override obligation (medium standard).
This practical rule helps in calculating compensation when coins of unknown purity are involved.

Key Terms
نقرة (nuqrah): Pure silver; unadulterated silver used in minting.
وسط (wasat): Medium; average quality or weight, used as a benchmark for valuation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf, under what condition can a borrower who repaid good wheat retract his repayment and give spoiled wheat instead?
A) If the lender confirms that the original loan was spoiled.
B) If the borrower acted without any condition.
C) If the lender initially claimed the loan was of good quality and the borrower admitted.
D) If the borrower repays within one week.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the right to return defective payment exists regardless of judicial process, and a debtor may retract an overly generous repayment only if the lender admitted to the quality owed.

Ownership of Game Entering Private Land: The Two Conditions
Ruling on ownership of wild birds and animals entering private land

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who owns a bird's eggs or a deer entering land, and identify the two conditions that modify the default rule.

Core Idea
Wild game on private land belongs to the taker, unless the landowner prepared the land for hunting or is close enough to take it constructively.

A common assumption is that anything found on one's land automatically belongs to the landowner. However, Hanafi fiqh makes a careful distinction: wild animals and birds are mubah (permissible property) that become owned only through taking (ihraz). This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the default rule and then introduces two important conditions that shift ownership back to the landowner under specific circumstances.

Guided Path
1
State the default ruling
Identify the core ruling: if a bird lays eggs or a deer enters a lair on someone's land, the eggs or the deer belong to whoever takes them, not automatically to the landowner.
The default is based on the hadith 'Game belongs to whoever takes it.'
2
Recognize the first condition: land prepared for hunting
If the landowner has prepared his land for hunting (e.g., set traps or nets with the intention to catch), then game caught there belongs to the landowner, even if someone else physically takes it first.
Intention (niyyah) links the catch to the landowner's cause.
3
Recognize the second condition: proximity of the landowner
If the landowner is close enough to the game to take it by simply extending his hand, then he is considered to have constructively taken it, and the game belongs to him.
This is a constructive taking (ihraz hukmi).
4
Distinguish from items arising from the land itself
Note the exception: honey from bees, trees that grow, and soil accumulated by water belong to the landowner even without intention or proximity, because they arise from the land itself.
This is because they are considered part of the land (taba'an).
5
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Given a scenario (e.g., a deer enters land, landowner is far but another man takes it), determine ownership by checking the two conditions.
If neither condition is met, the taker owns it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وإن أفرخ طير أو باض أو تكنس ظبي في أرض رجل فهو لمن أخذه) لأنه مباح سبقت يده إليه فكان أولى به لقوله عليه السلام الصيد لمن أخذه والبيض صيد ولهذا يجب على المحرم الجزاء بكسره . أطلقه وهو مقيد بقيدين : الأول ذكره الشارح أن لا تكون أرضه مهيئة لذلك وإن كانت مهيئة للاصطياد فهو له لأن الحكم لا يضاف إلى السبب الصالح إلا بالقصد ألا تری أن من نصب شبكة للجفاف فتعلق بها صيد أو حفر بئراً للماء فوقع فيها صيد لا يملكه ولا يجب عليه الجزاء إن كان محرماً، وإن قصد به الاصطياد ملكه ووجب عليه الجزاء إن كان محرماً. وعلى هذا التفصيل لو دخل صيد داره أو وقع ما نثر من الدراهم في ثيابه بخلاف معسل النحل في أرضه حيث يملكه وإن لم تكن أرضه معدة لذلك لأنه من إنزال الأرض حتى يملكه تبعاً لها كالأشجار النابتة والتراب المجتمع فيها بجريان الماء وإن لم تكن معدة ولهذا يجب في العسل العشر إذا أخذه من أرض العشر. الثاني في الذخيرة من كتاب الصيد : وهذا إذا كان صاحب الأرض بعيداً من الصيد بحيث لا يقدر على أخذه لو مد يده، وأما إذا كان صاحب الأرض قريباً من الصيد بحيث يقدر على أخذه لو مد يده فالصيد لصاحب الأرض لأنه صار أخذاً له تقديراً لتمكنه من الأخذ حقيقة إن لم يكن آخذاً له بأرضه ا هـ. ومثله في شرح الطحاوي. وقوله تكنس ظبي أي دخل في كناسه وهو بالكسر بيته، وكنس الظبي كنوساً من باب نزل دخل كناسه ؛ كذا في المصباح. ولم يذكر تكنس. وفي المغرب : كنس الظبي دخل في الكناس كنوساً من باب طلب وتكنس مثله، ومنه الصيد إذا تكنس في أرض رجل أي استتر ويروى تكسر وانكسر ا هـ. وفي فتح القدير : وفي بعض النسخ تكسر أي وقع فيها فتكسر ويحترز به عما لو كسره رجل فيها فإنه لذلك الرجل لا (وإنما قيد بالتلف ليعم حكم ما إذا أنفقها بالأولى قال في النهر فيه نظر. قوله: (من باب طلب) قال الرملي صوابه من باب جلس. قوله ويحترز به عما لو كسره رجل) إنما يتم
(And if a bird produces chicks, or lays eggs, or a deer enters its lair (takanasa) in a man's land, then it belongs to whoever takes it) because it is permissible (mubah) over which his hand has preceded, so he is more entitled to it based on his statement, peace be upon him: 'Game belongs to whoever takes it.' And eggs are game, and for this reason a pilgrim (muhrim) must pay expiation for breaking them. He [the author] gave it unrestrictedly, but it is restricted by two conditions: The first, mentioned by the commentator, that his land should not be prepared for that [hunting]. If it is prepared for hunting, then it belongs to him [the landowner], because the ruling is not attributed to a suitable cause except by intention. Do you not see that whoever sets up a net for drying and game gets caught in it, or digs a well for water and game falls into it, he does not own it, and no expiation is required if he is a pilgrim; but if he intended by it to hunt, he owns it and expiation is required if he is a pilgrim. And based on this detail, if game enters his house, or scattered coins fall into his clothes, it is different from the honey of bees in his land; he owns it even if his land is not prepared for it, because it is from the deposition of the land so he owns it as a subsidiary to it, like trees that grow and soil that accumulates by water flow, even if not prepared. For this reason, 'ushr (tithe) is due on honey if he takes it from 'ushr land. The second [condition] is in al-Dhakhira from the book of hunting: This [ruling] applies when the landowner is far from the game such that he cannot take it if he extended his hand. If the landowner is close to the game such that he can take it if he extended his hand, then the game belongs to the landowner because he is considered to have taken it constructively due to his ability to actually take it, even if he did not take it in his land. End. And similar is in Sharh al-Tahawi. And his saying: 'takanasa dhabi' means it entered its lair (kinās), which is its home, and kanasa al-dhabī kanūsan from the door of nazala meaning enters its lair; so in al-Misbah. And he did not mention takanasa. And in al-Mughrib: kanasa al-dhabī entered the lair (kinās) kanūsan from the door of talaba, and takanasa is like it, and from it 'the game if it takanasa in a man's land' meaning it hides, and it is narrated tukassir and inkassar. End. And in Fath al-Qadir: In some versions 'tukassir' meaning it falls and breaks, and he guards by it against what if a man breaks it, then it is for that man. (And it is restricted by destruction to include the ruling of what if he spends it, primarily. He said in al-Nahr: there is consideration. His saying: (from the door of talaba) al-Ramli said: correct is from the door of jalasa. His saying: 'and he guards by it against what if a man breaks it' is only completed...
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, explaining the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq: 'If a bird produces chicks, or lays eggs, or a deer enters its lair in a man's land, then it belongs to whoever takes it.' The author provides the rationale that these are permissible (mubah) things, and the first person to take possession of them becomes the owner, citing the hadith: 'Game belongs to whoever takes it.' Eggs are also considered game, so a pilgrim must pay expiation for breaking them. However, this ruling is qualified by two conditions derived from the commentary. First, the land must not be prepared or set up for hunting. If the land is intentionally prepared for hunting (e.g., with nets or traps), then any game caught belongs to the landowner, because the landowner's intention links the catch to his land. The author illustrates this with a person who sets up a net for drying clothes or digs a well for water; if game gets trapped accidentally, the person does not own it, but if the net or well was set up specifically for hunting, the owner owns the catch. This principle also applies to honey from bees on one's land: it belongs to the landowner even if the land was not prepared for beekeeping, because it arises from the land itself, similar to trees and soil accumulation. The second condition, from Al-Dhakhira, is proximity: if the landowner is close enough to the game to reach out and take it, then the game constructively belongs to him, even if he did not physically take it. If he is far away, it belongs to whoever actually takes it. The passage also includes lexical clarifications: 'takanasa' means entering the lair (kinās), with variant readings including 'tukassir' (falls and breaks), which is distinguished from a case where a man deliberately breaks the eggs—then the bird/eggs belong to that man. The authority weight is from Fatawa of later Hanafi scholars (Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Al-Dhakhira, Sharh al-Tahawi).

Key Terms
تفريخ الطير (tafrīkh al-ṭayr): A bird producing chicks or laying eggs in a particular place.
تكنس الظبي (takanasa al-ẓabī): A deer entering its lair (kinās) in someone's land.
إحراز (iḥrāz): Taking possession of a permissible (mubah) item, which establishes ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the conditions in this passage, if a deer enters a man's land and hides in its lair, who owns the deer?
A) The landowner, because it is on his land.
B) The person who takes it, unless the landowner could have taken it by extending his hand.
C) The landowner always owns it because the lair is on his property.
D) No one owns it until it leaves the land.

Key Takeaway
Ownership of wild game on private land is established by physical taking (ihraz), subject to two exceptions: the landowner's prior intention to hunt (prepared land) or his constructive possession through proximity.

Corrupt Conditions and Conditional Sales: Two Invalidating Factors
Commentary on matn distinguishing corrupt conditions and conditional sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a corrupt condition (shart fasid) that invalidates a sale and a conditional sale (ta'liq) that is not valid, and state the Hanafi ruling for each.

Core Idea
A corrupt condition voids the sale; a suspended sale is also void — both destroy the immediate transfer required in contracts.

In Hanafi sales law, the presence of an improper condition or the use of conditional language can render a contract void. This lesson unpacks the matn's statement 'ما يبطل بالشرط الفاسد ولا يصح تعليقه بالشرط' (What is invalidated by a corrupt condition and what cannot be conditioned). We will explore two distinct categories: conditions that are foreign to the contract's purpose, and contracts that are made dependent on a future event. Understanding this distinction is essential for drafting valid sales.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Categories
Read the matn: 'ما يبطل بالشرط الفاسد ولا يصح تعليقه بالشرط'. The commentator explains that this covers two separate legal issues. Pinpoint each one: (1) what is invalidated by a corrupt condition, and (2) what cannot be made conditional.
The phrase 'الترجمة لشيئين' signals the division.
2
Define the First Category (Shart Fasid)
A corrupt condition is one that the contract does not require, e.g., 'I sell you the slave on condition that he serves me for a month.' Such a condition makes the sale batil (void).
The condition must be 'fāsid' — not merely invalid but corruptive.
3
Define the Second Category (Ta'liq)
If the contract itself is issued using a conditional particle (e.g., 'if' or 'when'), like 'I sell you this slave if my father arrives,' the sale is not valid. Hanafi law requires contracts to be immediate and unconditional.
The text here cuts off, but the principle is clear: ta'liq nullifies the aqd.
4
Distinguish from Valid Conditions
Not all conditions are corrupt. Valid conditions like khiyar al-shart (option stipulation) are allowed because they are recognized by the Shari'ah. The matn's ruling applies only to conditions not required by the contract and to contractual ta'liq.
Conditions that uphold the contract's purpose (e.g., payment terms) are valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ما يبطل بالشرط الفاسد ولا يصح تعليقه بالشرط البيع) فإذا باع عبداً وشرط الاحتراز[؟] إذا لم يكن للمطاوعة وإلا فهو من فعل غيره يقال كسرته بالتشديد فتكسر وكسرته بالتخفيف فانكسر أي قبل ذلك تأمل. قوله : (ما يبطل بالشرط الفاسد ولا يصح تعليقه الترجمة لشيئين : الأول ما يبطل بالشرط الفاسد أي إذا ذكر في العقد شرطاً فاسداً لا يقتضيه العقد كبعتك العبد على أن يخدمني شهراً مثلاً فإنه يبطل البيع. والثاني ما لا يصح تعليقه بالشرط بأن صدر العقد معلقاً بأداة الشرط كبعتك العبد
His statement: (What is invalidated by a corrupt condition and what cannot be conditioned is the sale). For example, if he sells a slave and stipulates precaution? if it was not for compliance? otherwise it is the action of someone else. It is said 'kasar'tuhu' with tashdid so it breaks, and 'kasartuhu' with takhfif so it broke, i.e., before that, reflect. His statement: (What is invalidated by a corrupt condition and what cannot be conditioned is a translation of two things: first, what is invalidated by a corrupt condition, i.e., if a corrupt condition that the contract does not require is mentioned in the contract, e.g., 'I sell you the slave on condition that he serves me for a month,' then the sale is invalidated. Second, what cannot be conditioned, i.e., the contract is issued suspended by a conditional tool, e.g., 'I sell you the slave'
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage begins the commentary on the matn phrase 'ما يبطل بالشرط الفاسد ولا يصح تعليقه بالشرط' (What is invalidated by a corrupt condition and what cannot be conditioned). The commentator explains that the matn covers two distinct legal categories. The first is a condition that invalidates the sale: if a party adds a condition to the contract that is not required by the nature of the contract (e.g., 'I sell you the slave on condition that he serves me for a month'), the sale itself becomes void (batil). The second category is a sale that is conditioned (mu'allaq) upon a future event using a conditional particle like 'if' (e.g., 'I sell you this slave if...'). Such a sale is not valid because contracts in Hanafi law cannot be suspended. The text then goes into a brief linguistic discussion about the verb 'kasara' and its forms, which seems to be an aside. Unfortunately, the passage cuts off before the second type is fully explained. The commentary overall introduces the key distinction between a condition that corrupts an otherwise valid contract (making it void) and a conditional contract that is itself invalid because it lacks immediate effect.

Key Terms
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): A condition that is not in accordance with the contract's requirements, such as a service condition that benefits the seller.
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspending the execution of a contract upon a future event using conditional words (e.g., 'if').
عقد (aqd): A legally binding contract, specifically a sale in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if someone says 'I sell you this slave on condition that he serves me for a month,' what is the ruling on the sale?
A) The sale is valid, and the condition is enforceable.
B) The sale is valid, but the condition is void.
C) The sale is invalidated (batil) because of the corrupt condition.
D) The sale is suspended until the condition is fulfilled.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi sales law, both a corrupt condition not required by the contract and a conditional suspension (ta'liq) render the sale void (batil).

The Two Principles: Invalid Conditions and Suspension in Sales
Sharh explaining the two foundational principles and their application to sales.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two foundational principles governing invalid conditions and suspension, and apply them to sales with conditions introduced by 'in' and 'ala'.

Core Idea
Invalid conditions and 'if' suspension invalidate exchange-of-property sales, except for third-party consent within three days.

This lesson unpacks the foundational rules of the Hanafi school regarding conditions and suspension in contracts. You will learn the critical distinction between exchanges of property (sale) and non-property (gifts, divorce) and understand when a condition invalidates the entire contract versus merely being void itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract category
Determine if the contract is an exchange of property for property (like sale) or not (like gift). This determines whether an invalid condition voids the whole contract or just the condition.
The dividing line is mubadala mal bi mal.
2
Apply the rule for suspension with 'in'
If the contract is proprietary, suspension with 'if' (in) generally invalidates it absolutely, unless it is a condition of a third party's consent within three days.
Exception: third-party option clause is valid.
3
Apply the rule for conditions with 'ala'
For conditions introduced with 'upon' (ala), check if the condition is inherent, suitable, customary, or beneficial. If yes, condition is valid; if no benefit for entitled parties, condition is invalid but sale remains valid; if benefit, sale invalid.
Key distinction from suspension.
4
Analyse the suspension of acceptance
If the offer is suspended on future payment, istihsan allows it if payment is made, but the correct view per zahir al-riwaya is that it is not permissible.
This is a point of intra-madhhab difference.
5
Synthesize the ruling
Given a scenario with a condition or suspension, apply the principles to derive the ruling: valid, fasid, or only condition invalid.
Practice with examples.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب المتفرقات

والأصل أن ما كان مبادلة مال بمال فإنه لا يصح تعليقه بالشرط الفاسد للنهي عن بيع وشرط، وما كان مبادلة مال بغير مال أو كان من التبرعات فإنه لا يبطل به لأن الشروط من باب الربا وهو مختص بالمعاوضات المالية دون غيرها من غير المالية والتبرعات فيبطل الشرط فقط. وأصل آخر أن التعليق بالشرط المحض لا يجوز في التمليكات ويجوز فيما كان من باب الإسقاط المحض كالطلاق والعتاق وكذا ما كان من باب الإطلاقات والولايات يجوز تعليقه بالشرط الملائم، وكذا التحريضات أطلق في عدم صحة تعليقه بالشرط وهو محمول على ما إذا علقه بكلمة «إن» بأن قال بعتك هذا إن كان كذا فيفسد البيع مطلقاً ضاراً كان أو نافعاً إلا في صورة واحدة وهو أن يقول بعت منك هذا إن رضي فلان به فإنه يجوز إذا وقته بثلاثة أيام لأنه اشتراط الخيار إلى أجنبي وهو جائز. وفي جامع الفصولين: ولو قال بعته بكذا إن رضي فلان جاز البيع والشرط جميعاً ولو قال بعته منك بكذا إن شئت فقال قبلت تم البيع ا.هـ. وإن كان الشرط بكلمة «على» فقد قدمنا أنه إن كان مما يقتضيه العقد أو يلائمه أو فيه أثر أو جرى التعامل فيه كشرط تسليم المبيع أو الثمن أو التأجيل أو الخيار لا يفسد ويصح الشرط، وكذا إذا اشترى نعلاً على أن يحذوها البائع وإن كان الشرط لا يقتضيه العقد ولا يلائمه ولا جرت العادة به فإن كان فيه منفعة لأهل الاستحقاق فسد وإلا فلا. وفي جامع الفصولين وتعليق القبول في البيع بعد ما أوجب الآخر هل يصح؟ ذكر أنه لو قال إن أديت ثمن هذا فقد بعت منك صح البيع استحساناً إن دفع الثمن إليه، وقيل هذا خلاف ظاهر الرواية والصحيح أنه لا يجوز ا هـ .

قوله : (والقسمة) بأن كان للميت دين على الناس فاقتسموا التركة من الدين والعين على أن يكون الدين لأحدهم والعين للباقين فهي فاسدة وصورة تعليقها أن يقتسموا داراً وشرطوا رضا فلان فسدت أيضاً لأن القسمة فيها معنى المبادلة فهي كالبيع؛ كذا ذكر العيني مع أن البيع يصح تعليقه برضا فلان ويكون شرط خيار إذا وقته ولكن شرط الخيار هل يدخلها قال في الولوالجية من القسمة وأما خيار الرؤية والشرط فيثبت في قسمة لا يجبر القسمة في الأجناس المختلفة، وأما في كل قسمة يجبر الآبي عليها كالقسمة وهو الآبي عليها في ذوات الأمثال في الجنس الواحد فإنه لا يثبت ا هـ. ومن صور فسادها بالشرط ما إذا اقتسم الشريكان على أن لأحدهما الصامت وللآخر العروض وقماش الحانوت والديون التي على الناس على أنه إن توى عليه شيء من الديون يرد عليه نصفه فالقسمة فاسدة، وعلى الذي أخذه الصامت أن يرد على شريكه نصف ما أخذه وعلى شريكه أن يرد نصف ما أخذه أيضاً. ومنها أيضاً ما إذا اقتسما داراً على أن يشتري أحدهما من الآخر داراً له خاصة بألف درهم فهي فاسدة وكذا كل قسمة على شرط هبة أو صدقة. وإن شرط أن يزیده شيئاً معلوماً فهو جائز كالبيع، وإن اقتسما داراً وأخذ كل واحد طائفة على أن یرد أحدهما على الآخر دراهم مسماة فهو جائز، وكذا إن كانت الدراهم إلى آجل فإن كان له حمل ومؤنة ولم مكان الإيفاء فعلى الخلاف المعروف في السلم . الكل في الولوالجية قوله : (والإجارة) أي كان أجر داره على أن يقرضه المستأجر أو يهدي إليه أو إن قدم زيد ؛ كذا ذكره العيني.
The Book of Sale, Chapter on Miscellaneous Matters. The principle is that whatever is an exchange of property for property, it is not valid to suspend it with an invalid condition, due to the prohibition of sale with a condition. And whatever is an exchange of property for non-property or is from voluntary gifts, it is not invalidated by it because conditions are from the category of usury, which is specific to financial exchanges, not other non-financial matters and voluntary gifts; so only the condition becomes invalid. Another principle: suspension with a pure condition is not permissible in proprietary rights, but is permissible in what is from the category of pure relinquishment, like divorce and manumission, and likewise what is from the category of releases and appointments, it is permissible to suspend it with a suitable condition. Likewise, incitements are left unrestricted regarding the invalidity of suspending them with a condition, and this is interpreted as when he suspends it with the word 'if', such that he says 'I sold you this if such and such' so the sale becomes invalid absolutely, whether harmful or beneficial, except in one case: that he says 'I sold you this if so-and-so is pleased', then it is permissible if he specifies it within three days because it is stipulating an option for a third party, which is permissible. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: If he said 'I sold it to you for such if so-and-so is pleased', the sale and condition are both valid. And if he said 'I sold it to you for such if you wish', and he said 'I accept', the sale is concluded. End quote. If the condition is with the word 'upon', we have already stated that if it is something required by the contract or suitable to it, or has an effect, or is customary practice, like the condition of delivering the sold item or the price, or deferment, or option, it does not invalidate and the condition is valid; similarly, if he bought sandals on the condition that the seller make them. And if the condition is not required by the contract nor suitable nor customary, then if there is benefit for the entitled parties, it invalidates; otherwise not. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: Is suspending acceptance in sale after the offer valid? It is mentioned that if he said 'If I pay the price of this, I have sold it to you', the sale is valid by istihsan if he pays the price to him. And it was said: this contradicts the apparent narration, and the correct view is that it is not permissible. End quote.

His saying: (and division) such as if the deceased had a debt upon people, so they divided the estate between debt and assets on condition that the debt belongs to one of them and the assets to the others – it is invalid. And its suspended form: they divide a house and condition the pleasure of so-and-so – it is also invalid because division involves the meaning of exchange, so it is like sale. Thus mentioned al-Ayni, even though sale can be suspended on the pleasure of so-and-so and be a conditional option if timed. But does the option clause enter division? He said in al-Walwaljiyyah: Regarding division, the option of inspection and condition are established in a division that is not compulsory in different types. But in every division that compels the unwilling, like division in homogeneous things of the same type, it is not established. End quote. Among its forms of corruption by condition: if the two partners divided on condition that one gets the non-speaking goods and the other gets the goods, shop furnishings, and debts owed by people, on condition that if anything from the debts is lost, he returns half of it to him – the division is invalid. And the one who took the non-speaking goods must return half of what he took to his partner, and his partner must return half of what he took as well. Also, if they divided a house on condition that one of them buys from the other a house of his own for one thousand dirhams – it is invalid, and likewise every division conditioned on a gift or charity. If he conditions that he give him something known, it is valid like sale. And if they divided a house and each took a portion on condition that one of them gives the other named dirhams, it is valid; likewise if the dirhams are deferred, then if there is burden and expense and possibility of fulfillment, then it follows the known difference of opinion in salam. All from al-Walwaljiyyah. His saying: (and lease) i.e., he leased his house on condition that the lessee lend him, or give him a gift, or if Zayd comes; thus mentioned by al-Ayni.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the effect of invalid conditions and suspension in contracts. The author begins by stating two foundational principles (aslan) governing contracts in the Hanafi school. The first principle: any contract that is an exchange of property for property (mubadala mal bi mal) is invalidated if an invalid condition is attached. The evidence is the hadith prohibiting a sale with a condition (nahy an bay' wa shart). In contrast, if the transaction is an exchange of property for non-property (e.g., Ijarah for service) or is a voluntary gift (tabarru'), the condition is invalid but the contract itself remains valid, because the prohibition of conditions is considered analogous to riba, which only applies to financial exchanges (mu'awadat maliyya). The second principle: suspending (ta'liq) a contract with a pure condition (shart mahd) using the word 'in' (if) is not valid in proprietary contracts (tamlikat) like sale, but is valid in non-proprietary acts like divorce (talaq) and manumission ('itq), as well as in releases (isqat) and appointments (wilaya). However, if the condition is suitable (mula'im) to the contract, suspension may be valid. The author then addresses the specific case of suspension with 'in' in sales: generally, such suspension invalidates the sale absolutely, regardless of whether the condition is beneficial or harmful, with one exception—if the seller says 'I sold you this if so-and-so is pleased,' and specifies a timeframe of three days, this is valid because it is considered a stipulation of option (khiyar) for a third party. This exception is supported by a quote from Jami' al-Fusulayn, which adds that if the buyer says 'if I wish' and then accepts, the sale is concluded. If the condition is introduced with the word 'ala' (upon), the ruling depends on whether the condition is inherent in the contract (yaqtadihi al-'aqd), suitable to it (yula'imuhu), beneficial (fihi athar), or customary (jara al-ta'amul fihi). Examples include conditions of delivery, payment, deferment, or option—if such conditions are present, they do not invalidate the sale. The passage also notes a difference of opinion regarding the suspension of acceptance after the offer, with istihsan allowing it if payment is made, but the correct view according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) is that it is not permissible. The commentary then applies these rules to division (qisma) and lease (ijara). Division, because it contains the meaning of exchange (ma'na al-mubadala), is treated like sale: if an invalid condition is attached or if it is suspended on a condition, the division becomes invalid (fasid). However, the option of inspection and condition are established only in divisions that are not compulsory (like different types of property), not in compulsory divisions of homogeneous goods. Several examples illustrate the invalidity: e.g., dividing a debt and assets unevenly with a condition of recourse, or a division conditional on a future purchase. If the condition is a known additional payment, it is valid like a sale. For leases (ijara), the author gives examples of invalid conditions: leasing a house on condition that the lessee lend money or give a gift, or suspending the lease on the coming of Zayd. These are invalid because they attach a non-inherent condition to the contract.

Key Terms
الشرط الفاسد (al-shart al-fasid): A condition that is not valid according to Shari'ah, such as a condition that contradicts the nature of the contract or is not customary.
التعليق (al-ta'liq): The act of making a contract contingent upon a future event, often expressed with the word 'in' (if).
مبادلة مال بمال (mubadala mal bi mal): An exchange of property for property, such as a sale or barter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a seller says 'I sold you this if so-and-so is pleased' without specifying a time period?
A) The sale is valid and the condition is valid.
B) The sale is invalid because it is a suspended sale.
C) The sale is valid only if so-and-so agrees within three days.
D) The sale is valid but the condition is invalid.

Key Takeaway
Invalid conditions and suspension generally invalidate sales, but exceptions exist for third-party option and customary conditions.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Invalid Conditions and Suspension in Division and Leases
Sharh applying the rules to qisma and ijara.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify invalid conditions in division and lease contracts and state the Hanafi ruling.

Core Idea
Division is treated like sale: invalid conditions void it; lease is void if conditioned on a loan or gift.

This lesson applies the general principles of invalid conditions to two specific contracts: division of joint property (qisma) and leases (ijara). You will see examples of conditions that invalidate these contracts and learn how the Hanafi school distinguishes between compulsory and optional divisions.

Guided Path
1
Classify division as sale-like
Recognize that division (qisma) contains the meaning of exchange (mubadala), so rules similar to sale apply. Suspension or invalid conditions can invalidate the division.
Exception: option of inspection and condition only apply in non-compulsory divisions.
2
Analyse division examples
Examine the given examples: dividing debts and assets with recourse, conditional future purchase, conditional gift. Each is invalid because the condition is not inherent or customary.
The condition of an additional known payment is valid like a sale.
3
Apply to lease
For leases, conditions that are not integral to the contract, such as a loan or gift from the lessee, invalidate the lease. Similarly, suspension on a future event (like Zayd's coming) is invalid.
Lease is an exchange of benefit for rent, so inherent conditions are those related to the subject matter.
4
Distinguish valid conditions
In division, if the condition is a known payment (like one party pays the other a sum) it is valid. In lease, conditions like the term of lease or rent amount are valid.
Conditions that are customary or have an effect are valid.
5
Synthesize a scenario
Given a division or lease scenario with a condition, apply the rules to determine validity and suggest correction if needed.
Practice with the examples from al-Walwaljiyyah.

والأصل أن ما كان مبادلة مال بمال فإنه لا يصح تعليقه بالشرط الفاسد للنهي عن بيع وشرط، وما كان مبادلة مال بغير مال أو كان من التبرعات فإنه لا يبطل به لأن الشروط من باب الربا وهو مختص بالمعاوضات المالية دون غيرها من غير المالية والتبرعات فيبطل الشرط فقط. وأصل آخر أن التعليق بالشرط المحض لا يجوز في التمليكات ويجوز فيما كان من باب الإسقاط المحض كالطلاق والعتاق وكذا ما كان من باب الإطلاقات والولايات يجوز تعليقه بالشرط الملائم، وكذا التحريضات أطلق في عدم صحة تعليقه بالشرط وهو محمول على ما إذا علقه بكلمة «إن» بأن قال بعتك هذا إن كان كذا فيفسد البيع مطلقاً ضاراً كان أو نافعاً إلا في صورة واحدة وهو أن يقول بعت منك هذا إن رضي فلان به فإنه يجوز إذا وقته بثلاثة أيام لأنه اشتراط الخيار إلى أجنبي وهو جائز. وفي جامع الفصولين: ولو قال بعته بكذا إن رضي فلان جاز البيع والشرط جميعاً ولو قال بعته منك بكذا إن شئت فقال قبلت تم البيع ا.هـ. وإن كان الشرط بكلمة «على» فقد قدمنا أنه إن كان مما يقتضيه العقد أو يلائمه أو فيه أثر أو جرى التعامل فيه كشرط تسليم المبيع أو الثمن أو التأجيل أو الخيار لا يفسد ويصح الشرط، وكذا إذا اشترى نعلاً على أن يحذوها البائع وإن كان الشرط لا يقتضيه العقد ولا يلائمه ولا جرت العادة به فإن كان فيه منفعة لأهل الاستحقاق فسد وإلا فلا. وفي جامع الفصولين وتعليق القبول في البيع بعد ما أوجب الآخر هل يصح؟ ذكر أنه لو قال إن أديت ثمن هذا فقد بعت منك صح البيع استحساناً إن دفع الثمن إليه، وقيل هذا خلاف ظاهر الرواية والصحيح أنه لا يجوز ا هـ .

قوله : (والقسمة) بأن كان للميت دين على الناس فاقتسموا التركة من الدين والعين على أن يكون الدين لأحدهم والعين للباقين فهي فاسدة وصورة تعليقها أن يقتسموا داراً وشرطوا رضا فلان فسدت أيضاً لأن القسمة فيها معنى المبادلة فهي كالبيع؛ كذا ذكر العيني مع أن البيع يصح تعليقه برضا فلان ويكون شرط خيار إذا وقته ولكن شرط الخيار هل يدخلها قال في الولوالجية من القسمة وأما خيار الرؤية والشرط فيثبت في قسمة لا يجبر القسمة في الأجناس المختلفة، وأما في كل قسمة يجبر الآبي عليها كالقسمة وهو الآبي عليها في ذوات الأمثال في الجنس الواحد فإنه لا يثبت ا هـ. ومن صور فسادها بالشرط ما إذا اقتسم الشريكان على أن لأحدهما الصامت وللآخر العروض وقماش الحانوت والديون التي على الناس على أنه إن توى عليه شيء من الديون يرد عليه نصفه فالقسمة فاسدة، وعلى الذي أخذه الصامت أن يرد على شريكه نصف ما أخذه وعلى شريكه أن يرد نصف ما أخذه أيضاً. ومنها أيضاً ما إذا اقتسما داراً على أن يشتري أحدهما من الآخر داراً له خاصة بألف درهم فهي فاسدة وكذا كل قسمة على شرط هبة أو صدقة. وإن شرط أن يزیده شيئاً معلوماً فهو جائز كالبيع، وإن اقتسما داراً وأخذ كل واحد طائفة على أن یرد أحدهما على الآخر دراهم مسماة فهو جائز، وكذا إن كانت الدراهم إلى آجل فإن كان له حمل ومؤنة ولم مكان الإيفاء فعلى الخلاف المعروف في السلم . الكل في الولوالجية قوله : (والإجارة) أي كان أجر داره على أن يقرضه المستأجر أو يهدي إليه أو إن قدم زيد ؛ كذا ذكره العيني.
The Book of Sale, Chapter on Miscellaneous Matters. Buyu — Sales and Trade

Rulings on Conditions in Sales with 'In' and 'Ala'
Rules for conditions in sales with 'in' and 'ala'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify conditions in a sale as valid or invalid according to the Hanafi school, based on the particle used and the nature of the condition.

Core Idea
Conditions inherent to the contract or customary are valid; conditions that benefit only one party may invalidate the sale.

In Hanafi fiqh, not every condition added to a sale contract renders it invalid. The scholars distinguish between conditions expressed with 'in' (if) and those with 'ala' (on condition that). The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq lays out the criteria: conditions that are required by the contract, compatible, beneficial, or customary are permissible. Conditions that are extraneous and provide a benefit to the entitled party render the contract invalid. Let's work through these rules analytically.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional particle
Determine whether the condition is introduced by 'in' or 'ala'. This initial classification determines the default ruling.
'In' conditions are presumptively valid; 'ala' conditions require further evaluation.
2
For 'in' conditions, rule valid
If the condition uses 'in' (e.g., 'if so-and-so approves'), both sale and condition are valid. Example: 'I sold it to you if you wish' – acceptance completes the sale.
This is essentially a khiyar al-shart (option conditional).
3
For 'ala' conditions, evaluate nature
Check if the condition is (a) required by the contract (e.g., delivery), (b) compatible (e.g., option), (c) beneficial, or (d) customary. If yes, valid.
The sandal-making example shows a customary condition.
4
If condition is extraneous, check benefit
If the condition is not required, compatible, or customary, then see if it benefits the party who stipulated it. If yes, the sale is invalid (fasid). If no benefit, condition is void but sale remains valid.
Benefit to the entitled party (ahl al-istihqaq) triggers invalidity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال بعته بكذا إن رضي فلان جاز البيع والشرط جميعاً ولو قال بعته منك بكذا إن شئت فقال قبلت تم البيع ا.هـ. وإن كان الشرط بكلمة «على» فقد قدمنا أنه إن كان مما يقتضيه العقد أو يلائمه أو فيه أثر أو جرى التعامل فيه كشرط تسليم المبيع أو الثمن أو التأجيل أو الخيار لا يفسد ويصح الشرط، وكذا إذا اشترى نعلاً على أن يحذوها البائع وإن كان الشرط لا يقتضيه العقد ولا يلائمه ولا جرت العادة به فإن كان فيه منفعة لأهل الاستحقاق فسد وإلا فلا. وفي جامع الفصولين وتعليق القبول في البيع بعد ما أوجب الآخر هل يصح؟ ذكر أنه لو قال إن أديت ثمن هذا فقد بعت منك صح البيع استحساناً إن دفع الثمن إليه، وقيل هذا خلاف ظاهر الرواية والصحيح أنه لا يجوز ا هـ . قوله : (وفي جامع الفصولين ولو قال بعته بكذا الخ) قال الرملي هذا ذكره في أول الفصل السادس والعشرين وذكر فيه بعده بنحو ورقة مثل ما قدمه هذا الشارح فلا مخالفة لحمل المطلق على المقيد تأمل اهـ. أي فيحمل قوله جاز البيع والشرط جميعاً على ما إذا وقته بثلاثة أيام. قوله: (وصورة تعليقها) أفاد أن الصورة الأولى صورة اقترانها بالشرط الفاسد بدون تعليق قوله : ( على أن يقرضه المستأجر) صورة الاقتران بالشرط الفاسد بدون تعليق . وقوله أو إن قدم زيد صورة التعليق بأداة الشرط.
And if he said, 'I sold it to you for such provided that so-and-so is pleased,' the sale and the condition are both valid. And if he said, 'I sold it to you for such if you wish,' and the other said, 'I accept,' the sale is complete. End quote. And if the condition is with the word 'ala', we have already stated that if it is something required by the contract or compatible with it or has a beneficial effect or is customary — like a condition of delivery of the sold item or the price or deferment or option — it does not invalidate and the condition is valid. Likewise if he bought sandals on condition that the seller make them. If the condition is not required by the contract nor compatible nor customary, then if it contains a benefit for the entitled party, the contract is invalid; otherwise not. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: 'And suspending acceptance in sale after the other party has made an offer — is it valid?' It mentioned that if he said, 'If you pay the price of this, I have sold to you,' the sale is valid by istihsan if he pays the price to him. And it was said this contradicts the zahir al-riwaya, and the correct view is that it is not permissible. End quote. His saying: (In Jami' al-Fusulayn, and if he said 'I sold it for such ... etc.') Al-Ramli said: He mentioned this at the beginning of the twenty-sixth chapter and mentioned after it about a leaf of what this commentator had presented, so there is no contradiction, carrying the absolute to the restricted. Contemplate. End quote. That is, the statement 'the sale and condition are both valid' is interpreted as when he specified it to three days. His saying: (And the form of its suspension) indicates that the first form is the form of its conjunction with the invalid condition without suspension. His saying: (on condition that the lessee lends him) is a form of conjunction with the invalid condition without suspension. And his saying 'or if Zaid comes' is a form of suspension with the conditional tool.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on conditional sales in Hanafi fiqh, drawn from the commentary of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. It opens with a key principle: if the seller conditions the sale on the approval of a third party using 'in' (if), the sale and condition are both valid. Similarly, if the condition is expressed as 'if you wish' and the buyer accepts, the sale is complete. The text then distinguishes conditions introduced with 'ala' (upon condition that). Here, the validity depends on the nature of the condition: if it is inherent to the contract (like delivery or payment), compatible (like an option), beneficial, or customary, it is valid and does not invalidate the sale. If the condition is unrelated and provides no benefit to any party, it is void but the sale remains valid only if the condition is for a non-beneficial purpose. The passage then cites Jami' al-Fusulayn on the issue of suspending acceptance (ta'liq al-qabul) after an offer. The view of istihsan allows the sale if the price is paid, but the sound position (sahih) rejects it as contrary to zahir al-riwaya. The commentary by al-Ramli clarifies that the earlier ruling of validity applies only when the condition is limited to three days (an option period), and the forms of suspension are distinguished: the first scenario (رضي فلان) is a condition without suspension, while 'على أن يقرضه' is also a condition without suspension, and 'إن قدم زيد' is a true suspension using the conditional particle.

Key Terms
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspending the completion of a contract on a future condition, typically using 'in' or 'idha'.
شرط (shart): A stipulation in a contract; may be valid (sahih) or invalid (fasid) depending on its nature.
استحسان (istihsan): A juristic preference that sets aside a qiyas ruling for a more equitable outcome, used here to validate ta'liq al-qabul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a seller says, 'I sell you this car for $5,000 on condition that you paint my house,' and painting is not customary in such sales, what is the ruling?
A) Sale valid, condition valid.
B) Sale valid, condition void.
C) Sale invalid.
D) Sale suspended.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi sales, conditions that are inherent, compatible, customary, or non-beneficial are valid; only extraneous conditions benefiting the stipulator invalidate the sale.

Suspending Acceptance in Sales (Ta'liq al-Qabul)
Dispute on suspending acceptance in sales.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi dispute on suspending acceptance after an offer and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Suspending acceptance upon a future event is invalid per the sound view, despite a weak istihsan exception.

This passage from Jami' al-Fusulayn, quoted in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, addresses a nuanced scenario: a buyer says to the seller, 'If you pay the price, I have sold to you.' The offer is made, but acceptance is tied to a future payment. According to istihsan, once payment occurs, the sale is valid. However, the dominant view rejects this as contrary to the principles of contract law, where acceptance must be immediate and unconditional. Let's dissect this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario of ta'liq al-qabul
Understand the situation: after an offer, acceptance is expressed conditionally on a future event, e.g., 'If you pay the price, I have sold to you.'
This is different from a condition in the sale itself; it attaches to the acceptance.
2
Note the two Hanafi opinions
Istihsan (attributed to Abu Hanifa) allows the sale if the condition is fulfilled. The zahir al-riwaya (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) declares it invalid.
The passage explicitly says the correct view (الصحيح) is that it is not permissible.
3
Evaluate the proofs
Istihsan is based on preventing hardship. The opposing view holds that acceptance must be immediate and unconditional to avoid gharar.
The mufta bihi follows the principle that contracts require certainty (al-yaqin).
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The sound view (mufta bihi) is that ta'liq al-qabul is invalid. The passage affirms this.
Al-Ramli's commentary reconciles an earlier statement by restricting it to a three-day option.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال بعته بكذا إن رضي فلان جاز البيع والشرط جميعاً ولو قال بعته منك بكذا إن شئت فقال قبلت تم البيع ا.هـ. وإن كان الشرط بكلمة «على» فقد قدمنا أنه إن كان مما يقتضيه العقد أو يلائمه أو فيه أثر أو جرى التعامل فيه كشرط تسليم المبيع أو الثمن أو التأجيل أو الخيار لا يفسد ويصح الشرط، وكذا إذا اشترى نعلاً على أن يحذوها البائع وإن كان الشرط لا يقتضيه العقد ولا يلائمه ولا جرت العادة به فإن كان فيه منفعة لأهل الاستحقاق فسد وإلا فلا. وفي جامع الفصولين وتعليق القبول في البيع بعد ما أوجب الآخر هل يصح؟ ذكر أنه لو قال إن أديت ثمن هذا فقد بعت منك صح البيع استحساناً إن دفع الثمن إليه، وقيل هذا خلاف ظاهر الرواية والصحيح أنه لا يجوز ا هـ . قوله : (وفي جامع الفصولين ولو قال بعته بكذا الخ) قال الرملي هذا ذكره في أول الفصل السادس والعشرين وذكر فيه بعده بنحو ورقة مثل ما قدمه هذا الشارح فلا مخالفة لحمل المطلق على المقيد تأمل اهـ. أي فيحمل قوله جاز البيع والشرط جميعاً على ما إذا وقته بثلاثة أيام. قوله: (وصورة تعليقها) أفاد أن الصورة الأولى صورة اقترانها بالشرط الفاسد بدون تعليق قوله : ( على أن يقرضه المستأجر) صورة الاقتران بالشرط الفاسد بدون تعليق . وقوله أو إن قدم زيد صورة التعليق بأداة الشرط.

Invalid Conditions in Qisma: The Analogy to Sale
Ruling with examples on conditional division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify invalid conditions in qisma (division) and distinguish valid ones by applying the Hanafi analogy to sale.

Core Idea
A division with an extraneous condition is invalid, just as a conditional sale would be.

This ruling from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes that qisma (partition of jointly owned property) is treated as a form of exchange, analogous to sale. Therefore, any condition that would invalidate a sale also invalidates a division. The passage from al-Walwalijiyya provides several practical examples to illustrate the rule.

Guided Path
1
Understand the foundational analogy
Recognize that Hanafi jurists treat qisma as an exchange (mubadala), subject to the same rules as sale (bay'). This is the key principle driving the rulings.
The text explicitly says: 'because division contains the meaning of exchange, so it is like a sale.'
2
Identify the invalidating conditions
List the conditions that render a division fasid (invalid) according to the examples: conditional debts split with reimbursement, third-party approval, conditional refund for losses, conditional separate purchase, conditional gift or charity.
Each of these conditions would also invalidate a sale if added as an extraneous condition.
3
Distinguish valid conditions
Note that conditions analogous to valid sale conditions (e.g., additional payment of a known amount, deferred payment following salam rules) are permissible and do not invalidate the division.
The text states: 'If they stipulate that one will give the other something known, it is permissible like a sale.'
4
Apply the exception for options (khiyar)
Understand that khiyar al-shart (option condition) and khiyar al-ru'ya (option of inspection) apply only to non-compulsory divisions of different types, not to compulsory divisions of fungibles of the same type.
This is a nuanced rule: in compulsory divisions, options are not established.
5
Evaluate practical scenarios
Given a specific division scenario, determine whether the condition invalidates the division by comparing it to the sale analogy.
Use the listed examples as benchmarks.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والقسمة) بأن كان للميت دين على الناس فاقتسموا التركة من الدين والعين على أن يكون الدين لأحدهم والعين للباقين فهي فاسدة وصورة تعليقها أن يقتسموا داراً وشرطوا رضا فلان فسدت أيضاً لأن القسمة فيها معنى المبادلة فهي كالبيع؛ كذا ذكر العيني مع أن البيع يصح تعليقه برضا فلان ويكون شرط خيار إذا وقته ولكن شرط الخيار هل يدخلها قال في الولوالجية من القسمة وأما خيار الرؤية والشرط فيثبت في قسمة لا يجبر القسمة في الأجناس المختلفة، وأما في كل قسمة يجبر الآبي عليها كالقسمة وهو الآبي عليها في ذوات الأمثال في الجنس الواحد فإنه لا يثبت ا هـ. ومن صور فسادها بالشرط ما إذا اقتسم الشريكان على أن لأحدهما الصامت وللآخر العروض وقماش الحانوت والديون التي على الناس على أنه إن توى عليه شيء من الديون يرد عليه نصفه فالقسمة فاسدة، وعلى الذي أخذه الصامت أن يرد على شريكه نصف ما أخذه وعلى شريكه أن يرد نصف ما أخذه أيضاً. ومنها أيضاً ما إذا اقتسما داراً على أن يشتري أحدهما من الآخر داراً له خاصة بألف درهم فهي فاسدة وكذا كل قسمة على شرط هبة أو صدقة. وإن شرط أن یزیده شيئاً معلوماً فهو جائز كالبيع، وإن اقتسما داراً وأخذ كل واحد طائفة على أن یرد أحدهما على الآخر دراهم مسماة فهو جائز، وكذا إن كانت الدراهم إلى ،آجل فإن كان له حمل ومؤنة ولم مكان الإيفاء فعلى الخلاف المعروف في السلم ؛ الكل في الولوالجية
His saying: (And division) such as if the deceased had a debt owed by people, and they divided the estate between the debt and the tangible property on condition that the debt be for one of them and the tangible property for the rest, then it is invalid. And the form of suspending it is that they divide a house and stipulate the approval of so-and-so — it also becomes invalid, because division contains the meaning of exchange, so it is like a sale. Thus al-Ayni mentioned, even though a sale can be suspended by the approval of so-and-so and becomes an option condition if time-bound. But the option condition — does it enter division? He said in al-Walwalijiyya: 'As for the option of inspection and the stipulated option, they are established in a division that is not compulsory in different types, but in every division that the averse party is compelled to accept — such as division of fungibles of the same type — it is not established.' End quote. Among the forms of its invalidity due to condition: If two partners divide such that one gets the cash (samit) and the other gets the goods (urud), the shop fittings, and the debts owed by people, on condition that if anything from the debts is lost, the other will refund half of it — then the division is invalid. And the one who took the cash must return half of what he took to his partner, and his partner must return half of what he took as well. Also, if they divide a house on condition that one of them buys the other's private house for a thousand dirhams, it is invalid, and similarly every division on condition of a gift or charity. If they stipulate that one will give the other something known, it is permissible like a sale. If they divide a house and each takes a portion on condition that one pays the other named dirhams, it is permissible, likewise if the dirhams are deferred, and if it has transportation and expense and there is possibility of fulfillment, then it is according to the well-known difference in salam. All from al-Walwalijiyya.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on conditional division (qisma) in Hanafi law, drawing from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and citing al-Walwalijiyya. It establishes that division, being a type of exchange, is analogous to sale. Therefore, invalid conditions in sale likewise invalidate division. The first example: if the deceased had debts and assets, and the heirs divide such that one takes all debts and others all assets, the division is invalid because it is a conditional exchange without proper reciprocity. Another example: if partners divide a house on condition of a third party's approval, it is invalid, even though in a sale such a condition can be valid as an option (khiyar al-shart) if time-bound. The text clarifies that options (khiyar al-ru'ya and khiyar al-shart) apply to non-compulsory divisions of different types, but not to compulsory divisions of fungibles of the same type. Several more examples illustrate invalid conditions: one partner taking cash and the other taking goods plus debts, with a condition to reimburse for losses; division on condition of a separate sale; division on condition of a gift or charity. Valid conditions include a stipulation for additional payment of a known amount, analogous to sale. If the payment is deferred, the ruling follows the rules of salam (advance sale).

Key Terms
قسمة (qisma): Partition of jointly owned property among co-owners or heirs.
صامت (samit): Cash or liquid assets in a division context.
عروض (urud): Goods or commodities, as opposed to cash.
شرط (shart): Condition stipulated in a contract or division.
خيار (khiyar): Option or right to rescind a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two partners divide their shop: one takes the cash, the other takes the goods and debts, with a condition that if any debt is lost the first partner refunds half. What is the ruling?
A) The division is valid because it is a mutual agreement.
B) The division is invalid because of the condition, and each must return what they took.
C) The division is valid only if the refund condition is waived.
D) The division is suspended until the debts are collected.

Key Takeaway
A division with an extraneous condition is invalid, just as a conditional sale would be; only conditions analogous to valid sale conditions are permissible.
