Conditional Ratification of a Fuduli Sale is Invalid
Explains that conditional ratification is invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional ratification of a fuduli sale and apply the same principle to other suspended contracts.

Core Idea
Ratification (ijaza) is a sale in meaning; suspending it on a condition invalidates it.

When an unauthorized person sells property, the owner may ratify the sale. But can the owner add a condition to the ratification? This lesson explains why conditional ratification is invalid in the Hanafi school, based on the principle that ratification is equivalent to the original contract itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is conditional ratification of a fuduli sale. The ruling is that it is invalid (batil).
The passage explicitly states that conditional ratification is not valid.
2
Understand the ratio legis (illah)
The reason is that ratification is 'a sale in meaning' (بَيْعٌ مَعْنًى). Therefore, any condition that would invalidate a sale also invalidates its ratification.
Al-Ayni is cited for this reasoning.
3
Apply the analogy to other contracts
The same principle extends to ratification of division (qisma) and leasing (ijara) — indeed, any contract that is concluded as suspended (mawquf) cannot have its ratification suspended by a condition.
The author suggests the matn should have specified 'ratification of sale' to avoid ambiguity.
4
Recognize exceptions
The passage mentions 'except the exceptions mentioned' (إلا مستثناة وهي), indicating that there are specific cases where conditional ratification may be valid, but they are not detailed here.
These exceptions are likely found in other sections of Hanafi fiqh.
5
Summarize the legal principle
The key takeaway: ratification cannot be conditional because it inherits the same legal nature as the original contract.
This principle aids in understanding the broader Hanafi approach to suspended contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والإجازة) بالزاي المعجمة بأن باع فضولي عبده فقال أجزته بشرط أن تقرضني أو تهدي إلي أو علقها بشرط لأنها بيع معنى ; كذا ذكر العيني فظاهره تخصيص إجازة البيع فلو قال المصنف وإجازة البيع لكان أولى فإن ظاهره أن إجازة القسمة والإجارة كذلك بل كل شيء لا يصح تعليقه بالشرط إذا انعقد موقوفاً لا يصح تعليق إجازته بالشرط حتى مستثناة وهي
His saying: (And ratification) with the dotted za (ijaza), such as if an unauthorized person (fuduli) sold his slave, and he [the owner] said, 'I ratify it on condition that you lend me or give me a gift,' or he suspended it on a condition, because ratification is a sale in meaning. Thus al-Ayni mentioned, so its apparent meaning is specifically ratification of a sale. So if the author had said 'and ratification of sale' it would have been better, because it appears that ratification of division and leasing are likewise, rather everything that is not valid to suspend by a condition when it is concluded as suspended (mawquf) — the suspension of its ratification by a condition is not valid, except the exceptions mentioned.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on conditional ratification (ijaza) in Hanafi law. It explains that if a fuduli (unauthorized agent) sells a slave, and the owner ratifies the sale with a condition — such as 'I ratify on condition that you lend me money' or 'give me a gift' — the ratification is invalid because it is a sale in meaning, and conditions that invalidate a sale also invalidate its ratification. The passage notes that the same applies to ratification of division and leasing, i.e., any contract that cannot be validly suspended by a condition when originally formed also cannot have its ratification suspended by a condition. The author suggests that the matn should have specified 'ratification of sale' to avoid ambiguity, but the principle extends to all such contracts. There are exceptions (not detailed here) where conditional ratification may be valid.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijaza): Ratification or approval of a contract made by an unauthorized person (fuduli), which gives it full effect.
فضولي (fuduli): An unauthorized agent who acts without permission; his contract is suspended (mawquf) on ratification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A fuduli sells a car without the owner's permission. The owner later says, 'I ratify the sale on condition that the buyer pays an extra fee.' What is the ruling?
A) The ratification is valid because the owner approves the sale.
B) The ratification is invalid because the condition is extraneous.
C) The ratification is valid if the buyer agrees.
D) The sale is void from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
Conditional ratification of any suspended contract is invalid because ratification shares the same legal nature as the original contract.

The General Rule: Contracts Cannot Be Conditional
States the general prohibition of conditional contracts with a list of affected transactions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that sale, lease, and five other named contracts cannot be made conditional, and explain the rationale of avoiding uncertainty.

Core Idea
A condition that contradicts the nature of a contract renders it fasid.

In this passage, the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states a core principle: certain contracts are fundamentally incompatible with being tied to a future condition. This rule prevents gharar and ensures that the essential terms are known at the time of contract. Understanding which contracts are covered and why is crucial for evaluating contractual validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contracts listed
The matn lists: sale, division, lease, ratification, revocable divorce, settlement for property, and discharge. Know each.
2
Understand the rationale
The condition introduces uncertainty (gharar) or contradicts the immediate exchange nature of these contracts.
3
Note the scope
This is a general rule; later passages provide exceptions and details.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب المتفرقات لا يصح تعليقه بالشرط البيع والقسمة والإجارة والإجازة والرجعة والصلح عن مال والإبراء عن صورها : استأجر حانوتاً احترق كل شهر بكذا على أن يعمره ويحتسب ما أنفقه من الأجرة لأن شرط العمارة على المستأجر يفسد العقد فعليه أجر المثل وله ما أنفقه وأجر مثل قيامه عليه، واشتراط تطيين الدار ومرمتها أو تعليق الباب عليها أو إدخال جذع في سقفها على المستأجر مفسد للعقد، وكذا اشتراط كري النهر أو حفر بئر فيها أو أن يسرقنها، وكذا على أن يردها مكروبة هكذا أطلقه في الكافي وفصل خواهر زاده فإن شرطه في المدة فسدت وبعد انقضائها لا والصحيح أن شرطه في المدة فسدت وإلا فإن قال أجرتك بكذا بأن تكربها بعد انقضاء المدة فتردها على مكروبة فلا تفسد وإن قال على أن تكربها بعدها فهي فاسدة؛ الكل من فتاوى الولوالجية. ويستثنى من إطلاق قولهم لا يصح تعليقها بالشرط ما صرحوا به في الإجارات لو قال لغاصب داره فرغها وإلا فأجر كل شهر كذا فسكت ولم يفرغها وجب المسمى مع أنه تعليق بعدم التفريع.
Book of Sale, Chapter of Miscellaneous Matters. It is not valid to condition sale, division, lease, ratification, revocable divorce, settlement for property, and discharge upon a condition. Examples thereof: He rented a shop [with the condition] that he will repair it and deduct from the rent every month such-and-such, because the condition of repair on the tenant invalidates the contract, so he must pay the fair rent and he gets what he spent and the fair wage for his work. And stipulating the plastering of the house and its repair, or hanging the door on it, or inserting a beam in its ceiling, on the tenant invalidates the contract. Similarly, stipulating the digging of a canal or digging a well in it, or that he waters it. Similarly, that he returns it tilled; thus it was absolute in al-Kafi, and Khwahar Zadeh detailed: if he stipulated it within the term it is invalidated, and after its expiry no; and the correct is that if he stipulated it within the term it is invalidated. Otherwise, if he said 'I lease it to you for such-and-such that you till it after the expiry of the term and return it tilled', it is not invalidated; and if he said 'on condition that you till it after it', then it is invalid. All from Fatawa al-Walwaljiyya. And an exception is made from the absolute statement 'it is not valid to condition it' what they explicitly stated in leases: if one says to a usurper of his house 'vacate it, otherwise the rent is such per month', and he remained silent and did not vacate, the named rent is binding, even though it is a conditional statement.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq stating that sale, division, lease, ratification, revocable divorce, settlement for property, and discharge cannot be made conditional upon a future event. The sharh provides examples from lease contracts showing that conditions such as requiring the tenant to repair the shop and deduct from rent, plaster the house, hang the door, insert a beam in the ceiling, dig a well, or water the land invalidate the contract. A detailed discussion from Khwahar Zadeh distinguishes tilling conditions based on timing and wording. An exception is noted: if a landlord demands a usurper to vacate or pay rent, the rent is due even though it is conditional.

Key Terms
تعليق بالشرط (ta'liq bi al-shart): Making a contract contingent upon a future condition; invalid in these contracts according to Hanafis.
إجارة (ijara): Lease contract; selling usufruct for a known period in exchange for known rent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following contracts CANNOT be made conditional according to the Hanafi school?
A) Sale (بيع)
B) Marriage (نكاح)
C) Wakalah (وكالة)
D) Ariyah (عارية)

Key Takeaway
Sale, lease, and five other contracts cannot be made conditional; doing so renders them fasid.

Lease Conditions: Invalidating and Permissible Stipulations
Provides detailed examples from lease contracts to illustrate the general rule, including a scholarly dispute and an exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which conditions invalidate a lease contract according to the Hanafi school and distinguish the different rulings based on timing and wording, especially regarding tilling.

Core Idea
A condition requiring the tenant to improve the property during the lease term invalidates it, but a condition to till after the term may be valid if expressed as part of the return.

The passage provides a series of examples from lease contracts, illustrating what kinds of conditions trigger invalidity. It also reveals a nuanced distinction by Khwahar Zadeh regarding tilling conditions, and an exception for the usurper case. Mastering these details is essential for correctly assessing lease agreements.

Guided Path
1
List the prohibited conditions
Repair, plastering, hanging door, inserting beam, digging well/canal, watering, tilling. Each is a 'mufsid' for the lease.
2
Apply the rule
For each, the lease becomes fasid; tenant pays fair rent and may claim expenses.
3
Analyze Khwahar Zadeh's distinction
Tilling condition: if stipulated during the term, invalid; if after the term, depends on wording: 'that you till' (invalid) vs 'with the understanding that you till' (valid). This is an intra-Hanafi difference.
4
Identify the exception
The usurper case: condition 'vacate or pay rent' is binding because the rent is not a condition that alters the lease but a penalty.

Ratification Cannot Be Conditional: Principle and Application
Expands on the matn's word 'al-Ijaza' with ruling and examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that conditional ratification is invalid to contracts of sale, marriage, and lease, and evaluate the intra-madhhab dispute about its scope.

Core Idea
Ratification inherits the contract's nature: if the contract cannot be conditional, ratification cannot either.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into the ruling on conditional ratification (ijaza). It establishes that any condition attached to ratification invalidates it, because ratification is considered a replication of the original contract. The commentator builds on Ayni's specification to extend this rule to all contracts that fundamentally cannot be conditional, including lease and marriage. Understanding this principle helps muftis determine the validity of conditional approvals in various transactions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the nature of ratification (ijaza)
Ratification is the subsequent approval of a contract made by an unauthorized person (fuduli). In Hanafi fiqh, ratification relates back to the time of the contract and is treated like the contract itself.
2
Identify the ruling on conditional ratification
The text states that if the ratifier says 'I ratify on condition that you lend me' or attaches any condition, it is invalid. The reason: ratification is a sale in meaning (بيع معنى).
The condition invalidates the entire ratification.
3
Analyze the extension beyond sale
Ayni understood the ruling as specific to sale, but the commentator argues it applies to all contracts that cannot be conditional, such as division (qisma) and lease (ijara).
The extension is based on qiyas.
4
Apply to marriage example
The text cites Jami' al-Fusulayn: if a father marries his adult daughter without consent, and she later says 'I ratified if my mother is pleased,' the ratification is invalid because it is conditional.
Marriage cannot initially be conditional; thus ratification cannot either.
5
Note the lease detail (tilling)
The passage includes a discussion of lease contracts with tilling conditions. This shows that the principle also applies to lease, but with nuanced scenarios (e.g., tilling within or after the lease term).
The commentator emphasizes that the general rule remains that conditional ratification is void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والإجازة) بالزاي المعجمة بأن باع فضولي عبده فقال أجزته بشرط أن تقرضني أو تهدي إلي أو علقها بشرط لأنها بيع معنى ؛ كذا ذكر العيني فظاهره تخصيص إجازة البيع فلو قال المصنف وإجازة البيع لكان أولى فإن ظاهره أن إجازة القسمة والإجارة كذلك بل كل شيء لا يصح تعليقه بالشرط إذا انعقد موقوفاً لا يصح تعليق إجازته بالشرط حتى مستثناة وهي قوله : ( وفصل خواهر زاده (الخ) عبارة الولوالجية هكذا على وجهين إما أن يشترط الكراب في مدة الإجارة أو بعدها ؛ ففي الأول الإجارة فاسدة لأن مدة الإجارة مجهولة لأن مدة الكراب تقل وتكثر عن مدة الإجارة لأن المستأجر في هذا الكراب لرب الأرض ؛ هكذا ذكر وهو خلاف ما قال محمد رحمه الله في الجامع الصغير أنه إذا شرط الكراب على المستأجر صحت لأنه في أصل الكراب عامل لنفسه فلا تكون تلك المدة مستثناة لكن الصحيح أنه إذا شرط أن يرد عليه مكروبة بكراب في مدة الإجارة تفسد. وفي الوجه الثاني على وجهين : إما أن يقول أجرتك بكذا بأن تكر بها بعد انقضاء المدة وتردها على مكروبة أو قال أجرتها بكذا على أن تكر بها بعد انقضاء المدة، ففي الأول جازت وفي الثاني لم تصح فلو أطلق بأن قال وبأن تردها على مكروبة يجب أن تصح ويصرف إلى الكراب بعد انقضائها وهذا التفصيل صحيح .اهـ. بحذف التعليل. والظاهر أن في النسخة تحريفاً تأمل وفي الذخيرة وذكر شيخ الإسلام إذا شرط على المستأجر أن يردها مكروبة بكراب في مدة الإجارة فالعقد فاسد والمسألة على وجهين أما إذا قال صاحب الأرض أجرتك هذه الأرض بكذا وبأن تكر بها بعد مضي المدة وفي هذا الوجه العقد جائز ، أما إذا قال أجرتك بكذا على أن تكر بها بعد انقضاء مدة الإجارة ،ففاسد فإن أطلق الكراب ينصرف بعد العقد فيصح ولكن جواب هذا الفصل يخالف ظاهر ما ذكر ههنا ولا يظن به أنه قال جزافاً لظاهر أنه عثر على رواية أخرى بخلاف ما ذكر هنا .اهـ. قوله : فظاهره تخصيص إجازة البيع قال الرملي تأمل في هذه العبارة كتاب البيع باب المتفرقات النكاح، ويدل عليه ما في جامع الفصولين والبزازية وتعليق الإجازة بالشرط باطل كقوله إن زاد فلان في الثمن فقد أجزت. ولو زوج بنته البالغة بلا رضاها فبلغها الخبر فقالت أجزت إن رضيت أمي بطلت الإجازة إذ التعليق يبطل الإجازة اعتباراً بابتداء العقد ا هـ.
His statement: (and al-Ijaza) with the dotted za [i.e., pronounced with zay], as when a discretionary agent sold his slave and he said 'I have ratified it on condition that you lend me or give me a gift' or conditioned it upon a condition, because it is a sale in meaning. Thus Ayni mentioned, so its apparent meaning is the specification of ratification of sale. So if the author had said 'and ratification of sale' it would be better, because its apparent meaning is that ratification of division and lease is likewise; rather everything that is not valid to condition when concluded suspended, its ratification is not valid to condition, except for some exceptions which are... His statement: (and the detail of Khwahar Zadeh etc.) The expression of al-Walwaljiyya is thus in two ways: either he stipulates the tilling within the lease term or after it; in the first, the lease is invalid because the lease term is unknown because the tilling period varies. ... until the end of the discussion. Then: His statement: so its apparent meaning is specification of ratification of sale; al-Ramli said reflect on this expression. Book of Sale, Chapter of Miscellaneous Matters: marriage, and what is in Jami' al-Fusulayn and al-Bazzaziyya indicates that conditioning ratification upon a condition is invalid, like his saying 'if Zaid increases the price, I have ratified.' And if he married his adult daughter without her consent and the news reached her and she said 'I have ratified if my mother is pleased,' the ratification is invalid because conditioning invalidates ratification, considering it like the inception of the contract.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn's word 'الإجازة' (ratification). It begins by explaining that ratification of a sale by a discretionary agent cannot be conditioned on a loan or gift, because ratification is like the original sale. The commentator discusses Ayni's view that this applies only to sale, but argues it applies to all contracts that cannot be conditional. Then follows a detailed discussion of tilling conditions in leases from Khwahar Zadeh and other sources, showing different scenarios. Then the text returns to ratification with a proof from Jami' al-Fusulayn and an example from marriage: if a father marries off his adult daughter without her consent and she later says 'I have ratified if my mother is pleased,' the ratification is invalid because it is conditional.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijaza): Ratification of a contract made by an unauthorized person (fuduli), giving it legal effect.
فضولي (fuduli): An unauthorized agent who acts on behalf of another without prior permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a father marries his adult daughter without her consent, and she later says 'I ratify this marriage if my mother is pleased,' what is the ruling?
A) The ratification is valid, and the marriage becomes effective.
B) The ratification is invalid because it is conditional.
C) The ratification is valid only if the mother gets pleased.
D) The marriage is void from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
Conditional ratification is void because ratification mirrors the contract's nature; if the contract cannot be conditional, ratification cannot either.

Condition in Settlement (Sulh) Involving Property
Clarifying that sulh for property is a sale, and a condition causing uncertainty is void.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a settlement (sulh) for property is treated as a sale and apply the rule that a suspensive condition invalidates it due to ignorance of the amount forgiven.

Core Idea
Sulh for property is a sale — any condition causing uncertainty in the amount forgiven invalidates the contract.

Settlement (sulh) is a flexible contract, but when it involves property exchange, the Hanafi school treats it as a sale. This means that all conditions that invalidate a sale also invalidate such a settlement. The key example in this passage shows that a suspensive condition—like 'if you do not pay by a certain date, the amount changes'—creates uncertainty in the amount forgiven (jahalat al-mahṭūṭ) and renders the settlement void. Understanding this distinction helps you identify valid compromises from exploitative ones.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nature of the settlement
Determine if the settlement involves an exchange of property for property. If so, it is treated as a sale (bay‘) in Hanafi fiqh.
This is because it is a mu‘āwaḍa (exchange), and the rules of sales apply.
2
Check the genus of the consideration
If the consideration is of a different genus than the claimed amount, it is a sale. If it is of the same genus, classify further: less than claim = reduction and discharge (ḥaṭṭ wa ibrā’), equal = receipt and collection (qabḍ wa istīfā’), more = excess and usury (faḍl wa ribā).
Only the first case (different genus) triggers sale rules fully.
3
Examine the condition for suspensive element
If the settlement includes a condition that suspends it on a future event (e.g., 'if Zayd comes' or 'if you pay by a certain date'), identify whether this creates uncertainty in the amount forgiven.
The condition must not make the forgiven amount unknown at the time of contract.
4
Apply the rule of jahalah
If the suspensive condition leads to different possible amounts of forgiveness (e.g., 900 vs. 800), the settlement is invalid due to jahālat al-maḥṭūṭ (ignorance of the amount forgiven).
This is based on the example from al-Bazzaziyyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والصلح عن مال) أي بمال بأن قال صالحتك على أن تكسنني في الدار مثلاً سنة أو إن قدم زيد لأنه معاوضة مال بمال فيكون بيعاً ؛ كذا ذكره العيني. واعلم أنه إنما يكون بيعاً إذا كان البدل خلاف جنس المدعى به أما إذا كان على جنسه ؛ فإن كان بأقل من المدعي فهو حط وإبراء، وإن كان بمثله فهو قبض واستيفاء، وإن كان بأكثر منه فهو فضل وربا ؛ كذا ذكره الشارح من الصلح، فينبغي أن يخصص هنا وظاهر ما في البزازية الإطلاق في عدم صحة تعليقه بالشرط قال له عليه ألف صالح على مائة إلى شهر وعلى مائتين إن لم يعطه إلى شهر لا يصح لجهالة المحطوط لأنه على تقدير الإعطاء تسع مائة وعلى تقدير عدمه ثمان مائة ا هـ .
His saying: (And the settlement for property) i.e., with property, such as saying: 'I settle with you on condition that you house me in the house for a year' or 'if Zayd comes', because it is an exchange of property for property, so it is a sale. Thus al-Ayni mentioned it. And know that it is considered a sale only if the consideration is of a different genus from the claimed amount. If it is of the same genus, then: if it is less than the claimed amount, it is a reduction and discharge; if it is equal, it is a receipt and collection; if it is more, it is excess and usury. This is what the commentator mentioned from the chapter of sulh. So it should be specified here. And the apparent meaning of what is in al-Bazzaziyyah is absolute in the invalidity of suspending it on a condition. He said: A person has a claim of one thousand; he settles for one hundred until a month, or for two hundred if he does not pay until a month; it is not valid because of ignorance of the amount forgiven, for on the premise of payment it is nine hundred, and on the premise of non-payment it is eight hundred. End.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This is a ruling on settlement (sulh) when it involves property (sulh 'an mal). The passage explains that such a settlement is essentially a sale (bay') because it is an exchange of property for property. Therefore, the rules of sales apply: it cannot be suspended on a condition, and a corrupt condition invalidates it. The author then distinguishes different scenarios: if the settlement amount is of a different type than the claim, it is a sale; if it is the same type, it may be a reduction, discharge, or usury depending on the amount. The example from al-Bazzaziyyah illustrates that suspending a settlement on a condition (e.g., 'if you do not pay by month, then it is two hundred') is invalid due to uncertainty in the amount forgiven. The key point is that sulh in property is treated as a sale for the purposes of conditions.

Key Terms
الصلح عن مال (al-sulh 'an mal): Settlement where the consideration is property; treated as a sale in Hanafi fiqh.
جهالة المحطوط (jahalat al-mahṭūṭ): Ignorance of the amount forgiven; invalidates the contract due to gharar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a settlement for property, if the consideration is of the same genus as the claim but less, what is it considered?
A) A sale
B) A reduction and discharge (hatt wa ibra')
C) Usury (riba)
D) A gift

Key Takeaway
A settlement for property is treated as a sale; any condition that creates uncertainty in the amount forgiven invalidates it.

6 min
Condition in Discharge of Debt (Ibra')
Expansion on ruling for ibra' with corrupt condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on discharge of debt (ibra') when a corrupt condition is attached and explain why the ibra' remains valid while the condition becomes void.

Core Idea
Ibra' is a release, not a sale; a corrupt condition does not nullify the discharge, only the condition is void.

When you forgive someone's debt but impose a service condition, does the forgiveness stand? The Hanafi school distinguishes between contracts of exchange (like sale) and non-exchange acts like ibra'. This lesson unpacks a marginal note from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifying that a corrupt condition attached to ibra' does not invalidate the release, although it cannot be suspended (ta'liq). We also touch on a related intra-Hanafi dispute regarding ruj'ah and swearing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its nature
Recognize that ibra' (discharge of debt) is a unilateral release, not an exchange of property (mubadala mal bi mal). This classification determines how conditions affect it.
Compare with sale: corrupt condition invalidates a sale but not ibra'.
2
Apply the general rule for non-exchange contracts
In Hanafi fiqh, corrupt conditions invalidate only contracts of exchange. Since ibra' is not an exchange, the corrupt condition is void, but the ibra' itself remains valid.
3
Note the limitation on suspension
Ibra' cannot be suspended (ta'liq) by a condition; it is immediate and irrevocable once uttered. However, the corrupt condition here is not a valid suspension, so the rule on suspension does not apply directly.
The passage mentions that ibra' does not enter under the first principle (which allowed conditions only in exchange contracts).
4
Consider the intra-Hanafi excursus on ruj'ah
The commentator digresses into ruj'ah (revocation of revocable divorce). Like ibra', ruj'ah is not an exchange, so corrupt conditions do not invalidate it. However, there is a dispute on whether ruj'ah can be sworn by (tahlif). Abu Hanifah says no; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say yes, and this affects the validity of suspending ruj'ah by a condition.
This excursus is not central to the ibra' ruling but illustrates the broader principle.
5
Conclude the operative ruling
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position for ibra' is that a corrupt condition is null while the ibra' stands. For ruj'ah suspension, the fatwa follows the Sahibayn, allowing swearing and thus permitting conditional ruj'ah in their view.
See the hanafi_position_box for details.

Commentary
This passage discusses discharge of debt (ibra') and whether it is invalidated by a corrupt condition. The commentator notes that ibra' is not an exchange of property, so it should follow the rule of non-exchange contracts: corrupt conditions do not invalidate it, though it cannot be suspended. The text also includes an excursus on ruj'ah and swearing, contrasting the views of Abu Hanifah with the sahibayn regarding swearing by ruj'ah. The main point is that ibra' is not a sale, so its treatment regarding conditions differs from that of property exchanges.

Ruling on Suspending Ibra' on a Condition
States the ruling on ta'liq al-ibra' and exception for kafalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on suspending ibra' on a condition, distinguish between ibra' from debt and ibra' from kafalah, and explain the underlying reason based on tamlik and isqat.

Core Idea
Ibra' from debt cannot be suspended because it partakes of tamlik; ibra' from kafalah can be suspended because it is pure isqat.

Ibra' (discharge of debt) is a common financial transaction, but its validity when conditioned on a future event depends on its legal nature. The Hanafi school classifies ibra' as having aspects of both tamlik (transfer of ownership) and isqat (dropping of a right). This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling and the exception for kafalah (suretyship), providing a clear application of usul principles to fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is ibra' (discharge of debt) suspended on a condition. The ruling is that it is invalid for debt but valid for kafalah with a suitable condition.
This distinction is the core of the lesson.
2
Locate the dalil (reasoning)
The passage does not cite a Quranic verse or hadith; instead, it uses talil (reasoning) based on the nature of ibra'. It argues that ibra' from debt has an aspect of tamlik (because it can be revoked by rejection), so it follows the rules of tamlikat, which prohibit suspension on conditions.
For kafalah, ibra' is pure isqat, so suspension is allowed.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The reasoning connects the ruling to the underlying legal nature: because ibra' from debt contains tamlik, it cannot be suspended; because ibra' from kafalah is pure isqat, it can be suspended (with a suitable condition).
This is a form of qiyas? Actually, it's a direct legal classification.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is a legitimate ikhtilaf among scholars: some view ibra' entirely as isqat, while others (including the Hanafi school) see it as mixed. For kafalah, al-Marghinani preferred the isqat view, making suspension valid.
This ikhtilaf is acknowledged and resolved by tarjih.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that ibra' from debt cannot be suspended; ibra' from kafalah can be suspended on a suitable condition. This is supported by al-Marghinani in Fath al-Qadir.
The author also notes that a fasid (corrupt) condition does not necessarily invalidate, but the principle is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

It (ibra') is like tamlik in one aspect so it can be revoked by rejection, and although it has the meaning of isqat, it is considered by the rules of tamlikat, so it is not permissible to suspend it upon a condition; thus mentioned by al-'Ayni. He restricted it to debt because ibra' from kafalah is valid to suspend upon a suitable condition, like his saying: 'If you bring him tomorrow, you are discharged'; so if he brings him, he is discharged from the debt according to some. And al-Marghinani chose this in Fath al-Qadir and said it is the preferable view, reasoning that it is isqat, not tamlik. He mentioned it in the book of kafalah. And upon this is interpreted the statement of the author (may Allah have mercy on him): 'And the suspension of discharge from kafalah upon a condition is invalid' as referring to when the condition is unsuitable. I say: It is supported by what we will mention from al-Nahr regarding the issue of sulh, but in al-Hawashi al-'Azmiyya from al-Idah: ibra' from debt with a fasid condition, like he said to his debtor: 'I discharge your liability from my debt on condition that I have the option to revoke the ibra' and validate it at any time I wish,' or he said: 'If you enter the house, I have discharged you.' End quote. I say: Even if it is established that it is not invalidated by a fasid condition, its mention here is appropriate because it falls under the second principle, which is what is invalidated by suspension on a condition, as passed. His statement: '(He is not discharged, and it is a risk) ' perhaps its aspect is that the risk is in his dying while indebted, otherwise death is certain existence. It is objected that this exists in suspension upon the death of the creditor, for there is risk in terms of his death and the debt being in the debtor's liability. The answer is that suspension upon his death makes it a bequest, and a bequest is valid to suspend upon a condition, unlike suspension upon the death of the debtor, for it is pure discharge, so it remains suspended upon something containing risk, so it does not. This is what appeared to me, so contemplate it.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This is a ruling passage explaining the legal nature of ibra' (discharge of debt) and the permissibility of suspending it on a condition. The author begins by noting that ibra' has aspects of both tamlik (transfer of ownership) and isqat (dropping of right). Because it is considered like tamlik in some respects (e.g., it can be revoked by rejection), it falls under the rules of tamlikat, and thus cannot be suspended on a condition. However, al-'Ayni restricts this to ibra' from debt; ibra' from kafalah (suretyship) is an exception because it is pure isqat, as preferred by al-Marghinani in Fath al-Qadir. Therefore, the statement of the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq that suspending ibra' from kafalah on a condition is invalid applies only when the condition is unsuitable. The author then adds his own commentary, noting that even if ibra' with a corrupt condition (shart fasid) is not invalidated, the issue is mentioned here because it falls under the principle of what is invalidated by suspension. He then discusses the concept of mukhatara (risk) in the context of discharging a debtor upon death, concluding that suspension on the creditor's death is valid as a bequest (wasiyyah), whereas suspension on the debtor's death is not because it is pure discharge tied to a risk.

Key Terms
إبراء (ibra'): Discharge of a debt, i.e., the creditor dropping the right to demand repayment.
كفالة (kafalah): Suretyship; a contract where one person guarantees the debt or presence of another.
تمليك (tamlik): Making someone owner; transfer of ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because conditions are always invalid in financial transactions.
D) Because the Prophet (ﷺ) prohibited it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between ibra' from debt (which partakes of tamlik and cannot be suspended) and ibra' from kafalah (which is pure isqat and can be suspended on a suitable condition).

Ibra' Conditioned on Death: Wasiyyah vs Mukhatara
Explains valid and invalid ibra' conditioning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and invalid conditions in ibra' (discharge of debt) when conditioned on death, applying the Hanafi distinction between bequest and risky speculation.

Core Idea
Ibra' conditioned on the creditor's death is valid as a bequest; if conditioned on another's death, it is invalid as mukhatara.

Discharging a debt is a legal act that normally takes effect immediately. But what if the creditor says: 'If I die, you are free from the debt'? Or: 'If you die, you are free'? Hanafi jurists classify these conditions differently based on whether the condition is a bequest (valid) or a risky speculation (invalid). This lesson unpacks that distinction using key examples from Fatawa Qadikhan and other authoritative Hanafi texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
The act is ibra' (discharge of debt) suspended on a future event (death). Determine whose death is the condition: the creditor's or the debtor's.
The identity of the person whose death triggers the discharge changes the legal nature.
2
Apply the wasiyyah criterion
If the condition is the creditor's own death, the discharge operates as a bequest (wasiyyah) taking effect after death. This is valid because a bequest can be suspended on the testator's death.
Bequests are limited to one-third of the estate if the debtor is not an heir.
3
Apply the mukhatara criterion
If the condition is the debtor's death (or any uncertain event like entering a house), the discharge is a risky speculation (mukhatara) that resembles gambling. Such a suspension is invalid.
Pure ibra' cannot be conditional on a risk; the discharge must be immediate or already realized.
4
Recognize the exception
If the debtor is the creditor's heir and the statement is made during the creditor's death-sickness, the ibra' may be treated as a bequest despite being conditioned on the debtor's death. This is an exception to the general rule.
This is a specific application of the principle that death-sickness statements are treated as bequests.
5
Analyze analogous cases
Examine the rulings from al-Bazzaziyyah (suspension on an already existing fact is valid) and al-Mabsut (suspension on an oath is invalid). These illustrate the limits of permissible suspension.
Suspension on an already realized fact (ka'in) is effectively immediate (munjaz) and valid; suspension on a risky event like an oath is mukhatara.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي فتاوى قاضيخان من فصل في هبة المرأة من الزوج: ولو قال الطالب لمديونه: إذا مت فأنت بريء من الدين الذي لي عليك جاز وتكون وصية من الطالب للمطلوب، ولو قال: إن مت فأنت بريء من ذلك الدين لا يبرأ وهو مخاطرة كقوله: إن دخلت الدار فأنت بريء مما لي عليك لا يبرأ. ا.هـ. وفيها أيضاً: لو قالت المريضة لزوجها: إن مت من مرضي هذا فمهري عليك صدقة أو أنت في حل من مهري فماتت من ذلك المرض كان مهرها على زوجها لأن هذه مخاطرة فلا تصح. ا.هـ. وحاصله أن التعليق بموت الدائن إلا إذا كان المديون وارثاً له وعلق في مرض موته فيكون مخصصاً لإطلاق الكتاب. صحيح. وفي البزازية من الدعوى: قال المديون: دفعت إلى فلان، فقال: إن كنت دفعت إليه فقد أبرأتك لأنه تعليق بأمر كائن. ا.هـ. ومن فروع عدم صحة تعليق الإبراء ما في المبسوط: لو قال الطالب للخصم: إن حلفت فأنت بريء فهذا باطل لأنه تعليق البراءة بخطر رهي لا تحتمل التعليق. ا.هـ.
And in Fatawa Qadikhan, from the chapter on hibah of a woman from her husband: If the creditor says to his debtor: 'If I die, you are discharged from the debt that I have against you,' it is valid and it is a bequest from the creditor to the debtor. And if he says: 'If you die, you are discharged from that debt,' he is not discharged, and it is a risk (mukhatara), like his saying: 'If you enter the house, you are discharged from what I have against you,' he is not discharged. End quote. And in it also: If a sick woman says to her husband: 'If I die from this illness, my mahr upon you is charity, or you are released from my mahr,' then she dies from that illness, her mahr is upon her husband, because this is a risk, so it is not valid. End quote. The summary is that suspension on the death of the creditor (is valid) unless the debtor is his heir and he suspended it in his death-sickness, then it is specific to the absolute statement of the book. Correct. And in al-Bazzaziyyah from the chapter of claims: The debtor said: 'I paid to so-and-so,' and he said: 'If you paid to him, I have discharged you,' because it is suspension upon an existing matter. End quote. And among the branches of the invalidity of suspending ibra' is what is in al-Mabsut: If the creditor says to the opponent: 'If you swear, you are discharged,' this is invalid, because it is suspending discharge upon a dangerous risk that cannot bear suspension. End quote.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage presents specific applications of the ruling on ta'liq al-ibra' from Fatawa Qadikhan, al-Bazzaziyyah, and al-Mabsut. The key distinction is between a condition that is a bequest (wasiyyah) and one that is a risk (mukhatara). When the creditor says 'If I die, you are discharged,' it is valid because it operates as a bequest from the creditor to the debtor, and a bequest can be suspended on the testator's death. However, when the debtor's death is the condition ('If you die, you are discharged'), it is invalid because it is a pure discharge tied to an uncertain event (the debtor's death may occur when the debt is still owed), resembling gambling. Similarly, a sick wife forgiving her mahr upon her own death is invalid because it is a risk. The exception is when the debtor is the creditor's heir and the statement is made during death-sickness, in which case it may be treated as a bequest. The al-Bazzaziyyah example shows that if the condition is already realized (the debtor had already paid), the suspension is valid because the condition is known (kain). The al-Mabsut example shows that suspending discharge on an oath (a risky condition) is invalid.

Key Terms
مخاطرة (mukhatara): A risky or speculative condition that involves uncertainty (gharar) akin to gambling.
وصية (wasiyyah): A bequest, a disposition of property taking effect after death.
تعليق بأمر كائن (ta'liq bi-amr ka'in): A suspension upon an already existing fact, which is effectively immediate (munjaz).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a wife's statement to her husband 'If I die from this illness, my mahr is charity for you' considered invalid?
A) Because it is a bequest and bequests require witnesses.
B) Because it is a risk (mukhatara) since it depends on an uncertain death.
C) Because mahr cannot be forgiven after marriage.
D) Because the husband is her heir, so it is invalid as a bequest.

Key Takeaway
Ibra' conditioned on the creditor's death is valid as a bequest; conditioned on the debtor's death or any other risk is invalid as mukhatara.

Conditional Ibra: Customary Conditions Make It Valid
Resolves apparent contradiction in conditional ibra through customary condition distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between customary and non-customary conditions in ibra and state the Hanafi ruling on conditional waiver of dower.

Core Idea
Ibra is valid when suspended on a customary condition; non-customary conditions invalidate it.

In this passage, Ibn Nujaym addresses a critical question: how can a woman's waiver of her dower be tied to a condition like divorce, when ibra is supposed to be a unilateral discharge? The answer lies in the nature of the condition — if it is customary (mutta'araf), the conditional ibra is valid; if not, it is void. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and applies it to several real marriage scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The passage raises the objection: since a gift of debt is ibra, and ibra is a unilateral discharge, how can it be suspended on a future condition (ta'liq)? This seems contradictory.
The objection appears after the examples: 'If you say: gift of a debt is ibra, so how is it valid to suspend it on a condition?'
2
Analyze the response
The author responds by distinguishing between customary and non-customary conditions. Ibra can be validly suspended on a customary condition (shart muta'araf). This is the key principle.
The author cites al-Qunya and other sources to support this distinction.
3
Apply the distinction to the examples
Go through each example in the passage: (1) wife waives dower if husband divorces her → valid condition? The condition is customary, so the ibra is valid. (2) wife waives dower if husband places her affair in her hand → valid only if she actually divorces herself. (3) wife waives dower if husband remarries her → invalid because the condition is not customary; the dower remains due.
The passage also discusses ibra by implication (dilalah) and the difference between ta'liq (suspension) and taqyeed (restriction).
4
Extract the general ruling
From the examples and the author's explanation, extract the Hanafi ruling: ibra can be conditional, but only if the condition is customary. Non-customary conditions make the ibra invalid. This is the mufta bihi position.
The author emphasizes that this detail is a special feature of this commentary and should be memorized.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يعود مهرها على الزوج، وإن وقت وقتاً وطلقها قبل ذلك الوقت كان المهر عليه على حاله فقيل له : إذا لم يوقت لذلك وقتاً كان قصدها أن يمسكها ما عاش قال : نعم إلا أن العبرة لإطلاق اللفظ فإنه ذكر في كتاب الوصايا. رجل أوصى لأم ولده بثلث ماله إن لم تتزوج فقبلت ذلك ثم تزوجت بعد انقضاء عدتها بزمان فإنها تستحق الثلث بحكم الوصية. امرأة وهبت مهرها من زوجها على أن يطلقها فقبل الزوج قال خلف: صحت الهبة طلقها أو لم يطلقها لأن ترك الطلاق لا يكون عوضاً بقيت هذه هبة بشرط فاسد والهبة لا تبطل بالشروط الفاسدة، وذكر في النوازل : إذا قالت المرأة لزوجها تركت مهري عليك على أن تجعل أمري بيدي ففعل الزوج ذلك قال : مهرها عليه ما لم تطلق نفسها ولو وهبت مهرها الذي على المطلق منه على أن يتزوجها ثم أبى أن يتزوجها قالوا مهرها عليه على حاله تزوجها أو لم يتزوجها لأنها جعلت المال على نفسها عوضاً عن النكاح وفي النكاح العوض لا يكون على المرأة . ا هـ ما في الخانية فإن قلت إن هبة الدين إبراء فكيف صح تعليقه بالشرط في بعض هذه المسائل؟ قلت : الإبراء يصح تعليقه بالشرط المتعارف وبهذا يجب تقييد كلام المصنف رحمه الله تعالى ومن أطلق ففي المسائل التي قدمناها التي قالوا فيها بصحة التعليق إنما هو في المتعارف. وما قالوا فيها بعدمها فإنما هو في غير المتعارف ويدل على هذا التقييد أيضاً ما في القنية من باب مسائل الإبراء بالطلاق من كتاب الطلاق ولو أبرأته مطلقته بشرط الأمهار صح التعليق لأنه شرط متعارف وتعليق الإبراء بشرط متعارف جائز ، فإن قبل الإمهار وهم بأن يمهرها فأبت ولم تزوج نفسها منه لا يبرأ الفوات الإمهار الصحيح، ولو أبرأته المبتوتة بشرط تجديد النكاح بمهر ومهر مثلها مائة فلو جدد لها نكاحاً بدينار فأبت لا يبرأ بدون الشرط. قالت المسرحة لزوجها تزوجني فقال لها هبي لي المهر الذي لك علي فأتزوجك فأبرأته مطلقاً غير معلق بشرط التزوج يبرأ إذا تزوجها وإلا فلا، لأنه إبراء معلق دلالة. وقيل : لا يبرأ وإن تزوجها لأن هذا الإبراء على سبيل الرشوة فلا يصح. أبرأته بشرط أن يمسكها بمعروف ويحسن معاشرتها ولا يؤذيها ولا يطلقها فقبل ثم تزوج عليها وأغار على مالها وأذاها وطلقها فالإبراء بهذا الشرط غير صحيح. وساق فيها فروعاً كثيرة في بعضها لا يصح التعليق وفي بعضها يصح. قوله : (لأنه إبراء معلق (دلالة قال الرملي : يعلم منه أن التعليق يكون بالدلالة ويتفرع على ذلك مسائل كثيرة فليحفظ ذلك قوله : (ثم اعلم أن الإبراء يصح تقييده الخ) قال في النهر : واعلم أنه سيأتي في الصلح أنه لو كان عليه ألف فقال أد إلي غداً نصفه على أنك برئ من الفضل ففعل برئ، ولو قال إن أو إذا أو متى أديت لا يصح . وفرق الشارح بينهما بأنه في الأول لم يعلق البراءة بصريح الشرط وإنما أتى بالتقييد وفي الثاني بصريحه وهي لا يحتمل التعليق بالشرط .اهـ. أقول : قد ذكر الشارح الزيلعي في الصلح من صور المسألة ما إذا قال أبرأتك من خمسمائة من الألف على أن تعطيني خمسمائة غداً يبرأ مطلقاً، أدى خمسمائة في الغد أو لم يؤد لأن البراءة قد حصلت بالإطلاق أولاً فلا تتغير بما يوجب الشك في آخره. ثم اعلم أن الإبراء يصح تقييده بالشرط وليس هو تعلقاً وعليه فروع كثيرة مذكورة في آخر كتاب الصلح . وذكر الشارح هناك أن الإبراء يصح تقييده لا تعليقه والله تعالى أعلم. وهذا التقرير إن شاء الله تعالى من خواص هذا الشرح فاغتنمه واحفظ هذا التفصيل في الإبراء.
Her dower returns to the husband. If he set a time and divorced her before that time, the dower remains upon him as it was. It was said to him: if he did not set a time for that, her intention was that he should keep her as long as he lived. He said: yes, except that the consideration is the literal wording, for it is mentioned in the Book of Wills: A man bequeathed a third of his property to his umm walad on condition that she not marry; she accepted, then married after the expiration of her 'idda by some time: she is entitled to the third by virtue of the bequest. A woman gifted her dower to her husband on condition that he divorce her; the husband accepted. Khalaf said: the gift is valid whether he divorces her or not, because refraining from divorce is not a consideration; this remains a gift with a void condition, and a gift is not invalidated by void conditions. It is mentioned in al-Nawazil: If a woman said to her husband, 'I have left my dower for you on condition that you place my affair in my hand,' and the husband did that, he said: her dower is due from him as long as she does not divorce herself. And if she gifted her dower that was due from the man divorcing her on condition that he marry her, then he refused to marry her, they said: her dower remains due from him as it was, whether he marries her or not, because she made the wealth an exchange for herself for marriage, and in marriage the exchange is not upon the woman. End of what is in al-Khaniyya. If you say: gift of a debt is ibra, so how is it valid to suspend it on a condition in some of these issues? I say: ibra is validly suspended on a customary condition, and by this the words of the author (may Allah have mercy on him) must be restricted. And whoever speaks generally, in the issues we have presented where they said suspension is valid, it is only in customary matters; and what they said about its invalidity is only in non-customary matters. This restriction is also indicated by what is in al-Qunya from the chapter of issues of ibra by divorce from the Book of Divorce: 'If a divorced woman gave him ibra on condition of immediate payment (immar), the suspension is valid because it is a customary condition, and suspension of ibra on a customary condition is permissible. If he accepted the immediate payment and intended to give it, but she refused and did not marry herself to him, he is not discharged due to the loss of the valid immediate payment. And if a woman divorced irrevocably gave him ibra on condition of renewing the marriage with a dower, and her mithl dower is a hundred, then if he renewed the marriage for a dinar and she refused, he is not discharged without the condition. A woman who was divorced said to her husband, 'Marry me,' and he said to her, 'Give me the dower that you have against me as a gift, and I will marry you,' and she gave him ibra absolutely, not suspended on the condition of marriage: he is discharged if he marries her, otherwise not, because it is an ibra suspended by implication. It is said: he is not discharged even if he marries her, because this ibra is by way of bribery, so it is not valid. She gave him ibra on condition that he keep her honorably, treat her well, not harm her, and not divorce her; he accepted, then he took another wife, seized her property, harmed her, and divorced her: the ibra on this condition is not valid. He cited many branches, in some of which suspension is not valid and in some it is valid.' His saying: (because it is an ibra suspended by implication) al-Ramli said: from this it is known that suspension can be by implication, and many issues branch from this, so let that be memorized. His saying: (then know that ibra is validly restricted etc.) He said in al-Nahr: know that it will come in the chapter of Sulh that if he owed a thousand and said, 'Pay me half tomorrow on condition that you are discharged from the remainder,' and he did, he is discharged. But if he said 'if' or 'when' or 'whenever' you pay, it is not valid. The commentator distinguished between them by saying that in the first he did not suspend the discharge by an explicit condition, but rather came with a restriction; in the second it is explicit, and it does not bear suspension on a condition. End. I say: The commentator al-Zayla'i mentioned in Sulh among the forms of the issue: if he said, 'I give you ibra from five hundred out of the thousand on condition that you give me five hundred tomorrow,' he is discharged absolutely, whether he pays the five hundred tomorrow or not, because the discharge occurred absolutely at the beginning, so it is not changed by what causes doubt at the end. Then know that ibra is validly restricted by a condition, and it is not suspension; and there are many branches on this mentioned at the end of the Book of Sulh. The commentator mentioned there that ibra is validly restricted, not suspended. And Allah knows best. This exposition, Allah willing, is among the special features of this commentary, so seize it and memorize this detail on ibra.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the ruling on conditional ibra (discharge of debt) in the context of marriage, specifically the waiver of dower (mahr). The passage type is a ruling with proof, where the author presents several cases from earlier works (al-Khaniyya, al-Nawazil, al-Qunya) and then addresses a key objection: since a gift of a debt is legally equivalent to ibra (which is a unilateral discharge), how can it be validly suspended on a condition? The answer is that ibra can be suspended on a customary condition (shart muta'araf). The author distinguishes between customary conditions (which are allowed) and non-customary ones (which are not). This distinction is necessary to reconcile the general statements of earlier scholars. The passage provides examples: a woman gifting her dower on condition of divorce (valid), leaving dower on condition of self-divorce (valid only if she actually divorces herself), gifting dower on condition of remarriage (invalid condition, dower remains due). The key legal principle is that ibra is valid with a condition that is customary, and ta'liq (suspension) is only valid with customary conditions. Non-customary ta'liq invalidates the ibra. The author emphasizes that this is a critical distinction and urges the reader to memorize it.

Key Terms
إبراء (ibra): Discharge of a debt; a unilateral release of a debtor from liability.
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspending a legal effect on a future condition; in ibra, it is when the discharge is made contingent on a condition.
شرط متعارف (shart muta'araf): A condition that is customary or conventionally accepted in transactions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the gift of dower by a wife to her husband on condition of divorce considered valid even if he does not divorce her?
A) Because the condition is customary and therefore valid.
B) Because the gift is not ibra but a simple gift, and gifts are not invalidated by void conditions.
C) Because the husband's acceptance alone makes the gift valid regardless of the condition.
D) Because divorce is a valid consideration in marriage.

Key Takeaway
Ibra can be conditional only if the condition is customary; otherwise, the ibra is invalid.

The Taqyeed-Ta'liq Distinction in Ibra and 'Azl al-Wakeel
Analyzes conditional dismissal of an agent and the taqyeed-ta'liq distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between taqyeed and ta'liq in Hanafi law and apply that distinction to determine the validity of a conditional dismissal of an agent.

Core Idea
Dismissal of an agent can be restricted (taqyeed) but not suspended (ta'liq); a void condition does not invalidate it.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explores the critical distinction between taqyeed (restriction) and ta'liq (suspension) in the context of ibra (discharge of debt) and extends it to 'azl al-wakeel (dismissal of an agent). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying conditions in legal statements. The author defends the view that a conditional dismissal is valid as a restriction, contrary to some earlier scholars like al-Ayni.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their contexts
The passage discusses two legal acts: ibra (discharge of debt) and 'azl al-wakeel (dismissal of an agent). Both involve attaching a condition to a unilateral legal declaration. Identify the statements used (e.g., 'ala an tuhdiya shay'an).
These are ikrar-style acts; the condition is part of the principal's statement.
2
Distinguish taqyeed from ta'liq
Taqyeed means restricting the act with a condition that is inherent and simultaneous; ta'liq means suspending the effect on a future uncertain event. In Hanafi law, ta'liq is generally invalid in ibra and 'azl, while taqyeed is permissible.
The word 'ala can indicate either; interpretation depends on context and possibility of exchange.
3
Apply the distinction to ibra
Ibra can be restricted (e.g., 'I discharge you on condition you pay immediately') but not suspended (e.g., 'I discharge you if you pay tomorrow'). The passage gives examples of valid and invalid cases, including customary exceptions.
Suspension on death of creditor with no heir is an exception.
4
Apply the distinction to 'azl al-wakeel
The author argues that 'azl is like ibra: a condition can be a restriction (taqyeed) not a suspension. A void condition does not invalidate the dismissal; the agent is dismissed immediately.
Al-Ayni held the opposite view, that conditional dismissal is invalid entirely.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah al-khilaf
The author's view (supported by later Hanafi texts) is that conditional dismissal is valid as taqyeed. The practical difference: if a principal says 'I dismiss you on condition you give me a robe,' according to the author, the agent is dismissed immediately; according to al-Ayni, the agent remains.
The condition is not enforced; it is merely a restriction on the dismissal.

Book of Sales, Chapter on Miscellaneous Matters: The debt, dismissal of the agent, i'tikaf, muzara'a, mu'amala, iqrar, waqf, tahkim, and what does not invalidate; suspension is valid in some and in some it is valid. And if he said to his debtor, 'The ten dinars I have against you, give me five of them and I have gifted you the five,' the ibra is valid, whether he gives him the five or not, because it is an immediate ibra, not its suspension. And if he said, 'I have discharged you from the five on condition that you pay the five immediately,' if the ten were due immediately, the ibra is valid because payment of the five is due immediately, so this is not suspending ibra on a condition of expediting the five; if it was deferred, the ibra is invalid if he does not give him the five immediately. His saying: (And dismissal of the agent, such as if he said to his agent, 'I have dismissed you on condition that you give me something,' or 'if so-and-so comes,' because it is not an oath, so its suspension on a condition is not permissible. Thus al-Ayni mentioned, and his reasoning implies that its suspension is not valid. As for its being invalidated by a void condition, there is no evidence for that from this. In my view, this is also a mistake: the dismissal of an agent is not of that category, i.e., what is invalidated by a void condition. Rather, it is of the second category, i.e., its suspension on a condition is valid but it is not invalidated by a void condition. For this reason, al-Bazzaziyya restricted itself in the Book of Agency to saying that its suspension is not valid, and did not mention that it is invalidated by a void condition. The essence of the difference he mentioned between them is that the word 'ala can be for condition as it is for exchange, so it is interpreted accordingly when exchange is impossible. Ibra is permissible to be restricted by a condition even if it is not permissible to suspend it by it, so it is interpreted as restriction. This is unlike the case where ibra is preceded because he is discharged at the beginning, so the debt does not return with doubt. In the first case, he was not discharged at the beginning or end; it is suspended on a condition, so the debt is not dropped with doubt. This is because the word 'ala is ambiguous: it could be for condition, so he is not discharged except with payment, or it could be for exchange, so he is discharged absolutely. In that case, he is not discharged due to doubt and probability. End. It is not hidden that this explicitly shows that ibra is not invalidated by a condition, but rather is invalidated by suspension. His saying: (This exposition) from which it is derived that ibra from a debt is not valid to suspend except if it is suspended on the death of the creditor and the debtor is not an heir, or he suspends it on an existing matter, or on a customary condition. It is also derived that it is not invalidated by a condition, so it falls under the second rule of the author's words. His saying: (In my view, this is also a mistake...) In al-Hawashi al-Azmiyya, it is transmitted from al-Idah what contradicts it, where he said: The dismissal of an agent with a void condition is invalid, as when the principal says, 'I have dismissed so-and-so from agency on condition that he give me a robe,' which is a void condition because the agent does not give the principal something for the dismissal, since he can dismiss himself in the presence of the principal without anything. The agency remains because the dismissal is invalid. And its suspension...
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq (page 306) continues the discussion on ibra and introduces the topic of dismissal of an agent ('azl al-wakeel). The passage type is a ruling with conceptual clarification. The author first reiterates that ibra can be restricted (taqyeed) by a condition but not suspended (ta'liq) except in certain cases (customary conditions, death of creditor, etc.). He then turns to the dismissal of an agent, where scholars like al-Ayni held that it cannot be suspended on a condition. The author disagrees, arguing that dismissal of an agent is like ibra: it can be conditional (taqyeed) but not suspended, and a void condition does not invalidate it. The key distinction is between taqyeed (restriction, where the condition is an inherent part of the statement) and ta'liq (suspension, where the condition is external). The word 'ala (on condition) can be interpreted either as a condition or as an exchange; when exchange is impossible, it is interpreted as restriction. The author concludes that ibra is not invalidated by a void condition but by improper ta'liq. This is important for practical fatwa: a conditional dismissal of an agent is valid as long as the condition is customary, and the agent is dismissed immediately.

Key Terms
عزل الوكيل ('azl al-wakeel): Dismissal of an agent by the principal; a legal act that removes the agent's authority.
تقييد (taqyeed): Restriction; attaching a condition that is inherent to the contract, not a separate future event.
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspension; making a legal effect dependent on a future uncertain event.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq, what is the ruling if a principal says to his agent, 'I dismiss you on condition that you give me a robe'?
A) The dismissal is invalid, and the agency remains.
B) The dismissal is valid, but the agent must give the robe.
C) The dismissal is valid, and the agent is dismissed immediately; the condition does not affect it.
D) The dismissal is valid only if the robe is given.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, conditional dismissal of an agent is valid as a restriction (taqyeed) and does not invalidate the dismissal, while suspension (ta'liq) is generally invalid except in specific customary cases.

Suspending Dismissal of Agent and I'tikaf on a Condition
Author critiques errors in classifying suspendable acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that suspending the dismissal of an agent and i'tikaf on a condition is valid, and evaluate the counter-arguments from some Hanafi scholars.

Core Idea
Acts not involving transfer of ownership are not invalidated by corrupt conditions.

In this passage, Ibn Nujaym addresses a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding whether certain acts can be validly suspended on a condition. He criticizes those who claim that suspending the dismissal of an agent or the performance of i'tikaf is invalid, arguing instead that both are valid. The key principle is that corrupt conditions only invalidate acts of tamlik (transfer of ownership); dismissal of an agent is not tamlik, and i'tikaf as a vowed act of worship enjoys consensus on the validity of suspension.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on suspension
Identify the ruling that suspending the dismissal of an agent and i'tikaf on a condition is valid and that corrupt conditions do not invalidate them.
The author considers this the correct view.
2
Identify the opposing view and its basis
Some Hanafi scholars (e.g., al-Ayni, Ibn al-Humam, al-Sarakhsi in one narration) hold that both are invalid because i'tikaf is not an oath and dismissal is like a contract.
These scholars are listed in the text.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the opposing proof
The author refutes by citing transmissions showing validity: dismissal is not tamlik, and i'tikaf as a vow can be suspended by consensus.
Key evidence: al-Qunyah, Fatawa Qadikhan, and the rule in Jami' al-Fusulayn.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If valid, the act takes effect only when the condition is met; the corrupt condition does not nullify the original act.
E.g., if the condition is 'if you travel', dismissal occurs only upon travel.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author's view is mufta bihi, supported by abundant explicit texts and consensus on vowed acts.
Ibn Nujaym considers the opposing view erroneous and warns against blindly following transmitted errors.

قوله : (والاعتكاف) بأن قال علي أن أعتكف إن شفى الله تعالى مريضي أو إن قدم زيد لأنه ليس مما يحلف به كعزل الوكيل فلا يصح تعليقه بالشرط ؛ كذا ذكر العيني. وهذا يدل على أن المراد بالاعتكاف النذر به والتزامه ليكون قولاً يمكن تعليقه. وعندي أن ذكره في هذا القسم خطأ من وجهين من كونه يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة، ومن كونه لا يصح تعليقه. أما الثاني فقال في القنية باب الاعتكاف : قال الله علي اعتكاف شهر إن دخلت الدار فدخل فعليه اعتكاف شهر عند علمائنا ا هـ . فإذا صح تعليقه بالشرط لم يبطل بالشرط الفاسد لما في جامع الفصولين وما جاز تعليقه بالشرط لا تبطله الشروط الفاسدة هـ . لكنه ذكر إيجاب الاعتكاف من جملة ما لا يصح تعليقه بشرط ويبطل بفاسده. وذكر في البزازية من هذا القسم إيجاب الاعتكاف فقال : وتعليق وجوب الاعتكاف بالشرط لا يصح ولا يلزم، والعجب من المحقق ابن الهمام في فتح القدير حيث جعل إيجاب الاعتكاف مما لا يصح تعليقه وعزاه إلى في كتاب البيوع ولم يقل في رواية مع أنه قدم في باب الاعتكاف أن الاعتكاف الواجب هو المنذر وتنجيزاً أو تعليقاً وهو صريح في صحة تعليقه بالشرط، والعجب من العيني كيف مشى هنا على أنه لا يصح تعليقه وقال في شرح الهداية من باب الاعتكاف : والواجب أن يقول الله علي أن أعتكف يوماً أو شهراً أو يعلقه بشرط فيقول إن شفى الله ا هـ. فقد أتى بعين ما مثل به هنا وتناقض، وكيف يصح أن يقال بعدم صحة تعليقه مع الإجماع على صحة تعليق المنذور من العبادات أي عبادة كانت حتى إن الوقف كما سيأتي يصح تعليقه بالشرط ولو علق النذر به بشرط صح التعليق قال في الواقعات الحسامية

And it is invalidated by its corrupt condition. In al-Bazzaziyya: Suspending the dismissal of an agent on a condition is valid in one narration (al-Sughra), and invalid in another (Imam al-Sarakhsi). This is the correct view, so it must be attached to the second category. I hope from the generosity of al-Fattah to find the transmission regarding revocation (ruj'ah) and dismissal of an agent consistent with what I said. It is restricted to an agent because there is disagreement on the validity of suspending the dismissal of a judge. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: If the governor says, 'When this letter reaches you, you are dismissed,' he is dismissed upon its arrival; and it is said, no. It will come explicitly in the book that dismissal is among what is not invalidated by a corrupt condition. His statement: (and i'tikaf) as in saying: I owe it to myself to perform i'tikaf if Allah cures my sick or if Zaid arrives, because it is not something by which an oath is taken, like dismissal of an agent, so its suspension on a condition is not valid; as mentioned by al-Ayni. This indicates that what is meant by i'tikaf is the vow (nadhr) and its undertaking, to be a statement that can be suspended. In my view, its mention in this section is wrong in two respects: that it is invalidated by corrupt conditions, and that it cannot be suspended. As for the second, he said in al-Qunyah, chapter of i'tikaf: He said 'I owe it to Allah to perform i'tikaf for a month if I enter the house' and he entered, so he must perform i'tikaf for a month according to our scholars. So if its suspension by a condition is valid, it is not invalidated by a corrupt condition because of what is in Jami' al-Fusulayn: 'What is permitted to be suspended by a condition is not invalidated by corrupt conditions.' But he mentioned making i'tikaf obligatory as part of what cannot be suspended by a condition and is invalidated by a corrupt one. And he mentioned in al-Bazzaziyya from this category making i'tikaf obligatory: 'The suspension of the obligation of i'tikaf by a condition is not valid and does not become incumbent.' And it is amazing from the muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir that he made making i'tikaf obligatory as what cannot be suspended, attributing it to the book of Sales, and did not say 'in a narration', whereas earlier in the chapter of i'tikaf he stated that obligatory i'tikaf is that which is vowed, whether unconditionally or suspended, which is explicit on the validity of its suspension by a condition. And it is amazing from al-Ayni how he proceeded here that it cannot be suspended, while in his commentary on al-Hidayah, chapter of i'tikaf, he said: 'The obligatory is that one says: I owe it to Allah to perform i'tikaf for a day or a month, or he suspends it on a condition saying: If Allah cures...' So he gave exactly the same example as here and contradicted himself. How can it be correct to claim its suspension is invalid when there is consensus on the validity of suspending vowed acts of worship, any act of worship? Even a waqf, as will come, can be suspended on a condition; if one suspends a vow on a condition, the suspension is valid. He said in al-Waqi'at al-Husamiyya:

[PAGE_308]
From the seventh chapter on the vow of charity: A man lost something and said: If I find it, I owe it to Allah to waqf my land for the wayfarers; then he found it, so he must make a waqf because this is a vow and fulfilling vows is obligatory. And he said before: If he said: If I enter this house, I owe it to Allah to give this hundred in charity; then he entered the house intending by his entry to give charity for his zakat, then he entered and gave it, it does not suffice for his zakat, because the first is an oath and an oath is binding, he does not have the power to revoke it; so when he entered the house, giving charity in that manner became incumbent on him. So it is understood that a vowed act suspended is of the category of oath, and then suspension is valid. Thus the statement of the commentators that it is not something by which an oath is taken is shown to be false; and he explicitly stated in the vow of fasting the validity of its suspension on a condition. And in Fatawa Qadikhan: i'tikaf is a sunnah act prescribed; it becomes obligatory by vow and by suspension on a condition, and starting it is considered like other acts of worship. Then he said: If one vowed to perform i'tikaf in Rajab and brought forward a month before it, it is permissible in the view of Abu Yusuf contrary to Muhammad. And they all agree that if the vow was suspended, as when he said: If my absent one arrives or Allah cures so-and-so, I owe it to Allah to perform i'tikaf for a month, and he brought forward a month before that, it is not permissible. This statement in its phrasing indicates the validity of its suspension by consensus, because its implication is that the vow and that it must be fulfilled when its condition is met; as for bringing it forward before the condition is met, it is not permissible. This is the third place where they erred in explaining what does not have its suspension valid, and the error here is worse and more heinous than the first two due to the abundance of clear texts on the validity of its suspension. I am amazed that they have circulated these expressions in matns, commentaries, and fatwas without noticing the error in changing the rulings—and Allah grants success to what is correct. It often happens that an author mentions something incorrectly in his book, then later scholars come and transmit that expression without change or correction, so the transmitters multiply while the origin is from one mistaken person, as occurred in this place. There is no defect in the madhhab because our master Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, the codifier of the madhhab, did not mention the entire list of what cannot be suspended by a condition and what can be in this manner. And we have pointed out similar things in al-Fawa'id al-Fiqhiyya regarding the statement of Qadikhan and others that trusts become guaranteed by death due to ignorance except in three cases. The truth is that their opinion here is based on a narration concerning i'tikaf, even if the other narration is the one followed by the majority. And that Muhammad did not mention them collectively does not detract from the establishment of each individual one, since he mentioned them separately. The excuse for the author of al-Hidayah is that he undertook to combine al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir, and those are not in them, so he omitted them there.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and critical refinement. The author (Ibn Nujaym, likely) discusses the validity of suspending the dismissal of an agent ('azl al-wakil) and the performance of i'tikaf on a condition. He argues that both can be validly suspended, contrary to some Hanafi scholars who placed them in the category of 'what is invalidated by a corrupt condition'. He provides evidence: the dismissal of an agent is not transfer of ownership (tamlik), so it should not be invalidated by a corrupt condition. For i'tikaf, he cites that vowed acts of worship can be suspended by condition by consensus, and quotes various sources like al-Qunyah and Fatawa Qadikhan to show that i'tikaf, when vowed, can be suspended. He criticizes al-Ayni and Ibn al-Humam for inconsistency, noting that they themselves elsewhere affirmed the validity. The passage also distinguishes between the dismissal of an agent (valid) and of a judge (disputed). The author concludes that the errors stem from later scholars copying earlier mistakes without verification, but this does not impugn the Hanafi madhhab because the foundational texts (of Muhammad al-Shaybani) do not contain these errors. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that both 'azl al-wakil and i'tikaf can be validly suspended on a condition.

Key Terms
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspending the legal effect of an act on the occurrence of a future condition.
عزل الوكيل ('azl al-wakil): Dismissal of an agent by the principal.
الاعتكاف (al-i'tikaf): Seclusion in a mosque for worship; when vowed, it becomes wajib.
الشرط الفاسد (al-shart al-fasid): A condition that is invalid according to shariah, e.g., one that contradicts the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the evidence that suspending i'tikaf on a condition is valid?
A) I'tikaf is a sunnah act and sunnah acts can always be suspended.
B) There is consensus that vowed acts of worship can be suspended, and i'tikaf is a vowed act.
C) The dismissal of an agent is valid, so i'tikaf follows by analogy.
D) The author's personal opinion based on istihsan.

Key Takeaway
Acts that are not tamlik (transfer of ownership), such as dismissal of an agent and vowed acts like i'tikaf, can be validly suspended on a condition, and corrupt conditions do not invalidate them.
