The Conditional Vow as a Binding Oath
Establishes conditional vow as a type of oath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional vows and explain why they are treated as binding oaths.

Core Idea
A conditional vow becomes a binding oath the moment the condition is met.

This lesson examines a key ruling from the Hanafi school: a conditional vow (al-nadhr al-mu'allaq) is legally treated as an oath (yamin). Through a detailed passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq, we will see how the author establishes this through a case analysis and refutes a common misunderstanding. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly handling vows made by Muslims in daily life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and ruling
Read the first case: a man loses something and makes a conditional vow to give his land as waqf if he finds it. The ruling is that he must perform the waqf because fulfilling a vow is obligatory.
This establishes the general obligation of vows.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the general obligation 'الوفاء بالنذر واجب' (fulfilling a vow is wajib) as the proof. This is a derived principle from the Qur'an and Sunnah.
The dalil is not quoted verbatim but is referenced.
3
Trace the analogy to oaths
The second case shows that a conditional vow intended as zakat does not count as zakat because the vow is an oath (yamin) and an oath is binding and cannot be retracted. This shows the conditional vow functions exactly like an oath.
The analogy (qiyas) is between conditional vows and oaths.
4
Note the refutation of opposing view
The author explicitly refutes commentators who claimed conditional vows are not a form of oath. He affirms that conditioning is valid, even for fasting vows.
This strengthens the Hanafi position.
5
Apply to similar cases
The principle extends to any conditional vow: upon fulfillment of the condition, performance becomes wajib. For example, a vow to fast if cured must be fulfilled.
This is the operative ruling (mufta bihi).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب المتفرقات من الفصل السابع في النذر بالصدقة رجل ذهب له شيء فقال إن وجدته فلله علي أن أقف أرضي على أبناء السبيل فوجده وجب عليه أن يقف لأن هذا نذر والوفاء بالنذر واجب . وقال قبله : لو قال إن دخلت هذه الدار فلله علي أن أتصدق بهذه المائة فدخل الدار وهو ينوي بدخوله أن يتصدق عن زكاة ماله فدخل ثم تصدق بها لا يجزئه عن الزكاة لأن الأول يمين واليمين لازم لا يملك الرجوع عنها، فإذا دخل الدار لزمه التصدق بها بجهة اليمين ا هـ. فقد أفاد أن المنذور المعلق من باب اليمين وحينئذ صح التعليق، وبهذا ظهر بطلان قول. الشارحين أنه ليس مما يحلف به وصرح في النذر بالصوم بصحة تعليقه بالشرط.
Book of Sales, Miscellaneous Section, from the seventh chapter on the vow of charity: A man lost something and said, 'If I find it, Allah has an obligation on me that I dedicate my land as a waqf for wayfarers.' He found it, so he must do the waqf because this is a vow and fulfilling a vow is obligatory. And he said before that: If he said, 'If I enter this house, Allah has an obligation on me that I give this hundred as charity,' and he entered the house intending by entering to give it as zakat for his wealth, then entered and gave it, it does not suffice for zakat because the first is an oath, and an oath is binding and one cannot retract it. So when he entered the house, giving it became obligatory in the capacity of an oath. Thus it is understood that a conditional vow is a type of oath, and therefore the condition is valid. And by this the falsehood of the commentators' statement that it is not something sworn by becomes apparent, and it has been explicitly stated regarding the vow of fasting that its conditioning is valid.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof establishing that a conditional vow (al-nadhr al-mu'allaq) is a type of oath (yamin). The author begins with a case: a man loses something and makes a conditional vow to give his land as waqf if he finds it. Upon finding it, the vow is binding because fulfilling a vow is obligatory (wajib). He then contrasts this with a case where someone intends a charitable payment as zakat but makes it conditional on entering a house. The ruling is that it does not count as zakat because the first statement is an oath—it is binding and cannot be changed. Therefore, a conditional vow is treated like an oath: it becomes binding when the condition occurs, and the validity of such a vow is established. The author explicitly refutes the erroneous view of some commentators who claimed that conditional vows are not like oaths, and affirms that even vows of fasting can be conditioned, as stated in earlier texts.

Key Terms
النذر المعلق (al-nadhr al-mu'allaq): A vow whose obligation is suspended upon the occurrence of a future condition.
اليمين (al-yamin): An oath invoking Allah's name or attributes, which creates a binding obligation to fulfill or abstain from an action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man loses his wallet and says, 'If I find it, I will give $100 as sadaqah.' He finds it. According to the passage, what is the ruling?
A) He may choose whether to give the $100.
B) He must give the $100 because the vow is obligatory.
C) It is recommended but not obligatory.
D) He must give the $100, but it can count as his zakat.

Key Takeaway
A conditional vow in the Hanafi school is a binding oath; once the condition occurs, performance is wajib.

Accelerating a Conditional Vow: Ruling and Error Correction
Intra-Hanafi dispute on accelerating conditional i'tikāf with correction of transmission error

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accelerating a conditional vow and identify the common scholarly error regarding which acts can be conditioned.

Core Idea
A conditional vow is only binding after the condition occurs; accelerating it is invalid by consensus.

Conditional vows (al-nadhr al-mu'allaq) are a common form of commitment in Islamic practice. However, there is confusion about whether one can perform the vowed act before the condition materializes. This lesson examines the Hanafi position on accelerating such vows and corrects a historical error in transmission that claimed conditioning i'tikaf is invalid. You will learn the distinction between simple and conditional vows, the consensus on the latter, and how to avoid a common mistake found in some classical texts.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish simple from conditional vows
Identify two types: a simple vow (e.g., 'I owe Allah to observe i'tikaf in Rajab') and a conditional vow (e.g., 'If my relative returns, I owe Allah i'tikaf'). The ruling differs: in simple vows, accelerating (doing it early) is disputed; in conditional vows, it is unanimously invalid.
The source mentions both types to highlight the difference.
2
Identify the consensus on conditional vows
Recognize that the Hanafi school (and others) agree: if the condition has not occurred, performing the act does not fulfill the vow. The vow must be performed after the condition is met.
This consensus is the basis for rejecting any claim that conditional i'tikaf is invalid.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute on simple vows
Note that Abu Yūsuf and Muhammad differ on whether one can accelerate a simple vow (e.g., vow to do i'tikaf in Rajab but do it a month early). Abu Yūsuf permits it; Muhammad does not. This dispute does not affect conditional vows.
The author cites this to show that even where ikhtilaf exists, the ruling on conditional vows is separate and unanimous.
4
Understand the error in transmission
Some earlier scholars (e.g., al-Nāṭifī) transmitted a list of things that cannot be conditioned, including i'tikaf. However, this is based on a flawed reading of Imam Muhammad's statement. The correct position is that conditioning i'tikaf is valid by consensus, and the error arose from a corrupted transmission.
The author identifies this as the third of several errors, emphasizing that later scholars uncritically copied the mistake.
5
Apply the rule to avoid common pitfalls
When faced with a conditional vow, always verify whether the condition has occurred before performing the act. If the act is done prematurely, it does not count. Also, be aware that lists of 'what cannot be conditioned' in some texts may be erroneous; rely on the established consensus.
This practical step prevents incorrect practice and fatwa.

يصح على هذا الوجه وقد نبهنا على مثل ذلك في الفوائد الفقهية في قول قاضيخان وغيره أن الأمانات تنقلب مضمونة بالموت عن تجهيل إلا في ثلاث ثم إني تتبعت كلامهم مريضي لا قوله : (وهذا هو الموضع الثالث من جملة And in the Fatawa of Qadikhan: I'tikaf is a prescribed sunnah that becomes obligatory by vow, and conditioning it with a condition and starting it are like other acts of worship. Then he said: If he vowed to observe i'tikaf in Rajab and accelerated a month before it, it is permissible according to Abu Yusuf contrary to Muhammad. And they agreed that if the vow was conditional, such as if he said 'If my absent one returns or Allah heals so-and-so, I owe Allah to observe i'tikaf for a month' and then he accelerated a month before that, it is not permissible. So this expression indicates by its placement the validity of conditioning it by consensus, because its meaning is that the vow and the obligation to fulfill it are valid when its condition is met, but accelerating it before the condition exists is not permissible. This is the third place where they erred in explaining what cannot be conditioned, and the error here is more severe and greater due to the abundance of clear statements about the validity of conditioning it. May Allah have mercy on the researcher, the author of al-Hidayah, who did not pay attention to collecting these things and placing them in his book, which is evidence of his complete precision and mastery. If the author had omitted them, it would have been safer.

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and critical refinement. It begins by citing Qadikhan's Fatawa that i'tikaf is a sunnah that becomes obligatory by vow and can be conditioned. Then it presents a dispute: if someone vows to observe i'tikaf in Rajab but does it a month earlier, Abu Yusuf allows it while Muhammad does not. However, if the vow is conditional (e.g., 'If my absent one returns, I owe i'tikaf'), then accelerating the i'tikaf before the condition occurs is invalid by consensus. The author uses this to show that conditional vows are valid, and that the earlier scholars who claimed otherwise were mistaken. He identifies this as the third error they made in stating what cannot be conditioned. He criticizes the proliferation of this error in texts and commentaries. He then engages with a contemporary objection that the discussion is about conditioning i'tikaf itself, not the vow, but refutes it by citing Hibat al-Nihaya, which lists conditioning the obligation of i'tikaf as one of the thirteen things that can be conditioned with a corrupt condition. He concludes that the correct position is that conditional i'tikaf is valid, and that Muhammad's statement in al-Asl about its invalidity is based on a different narration. The author praises al-Hidayah for not including these erroneous lists.

Key Terms
الاعتكاف (al-i'tikaf): Seclusion in the mosque for worship; a sunnah that becomes obligatory by vow.
التعليق بالشرط (al-ta'liq bi al-shart): Suspending the obligation of an act upon the occurrence of a future condition.

A conditional vow only becomes binding after the condition is fulfilled; any act done before the condition is invalid and does not count towards the vow.

Conditional Sharecropping, Irrigation, and Admission Invalid
Rulings that conditional sharecropping, irrigation contracts, and admissions are invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that conditional sharecropping, irrigation sharecropping, and admission are invalid, and explain the legal reason based on their classification as leases or admissions.

Core Idea
Conditional sharecropping, irrigation, and admission are invalid because they contradict the nature of leases and acknowledgments.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, three distinct contractual acts are examined: sharecropping (muzara'ah), irrigation sharecropping (mu'amalah), and admission (iqrar). The common ruling is that attaching a condition—such as a loan or a future event—invalidates them. You will learn why each is treated as a lease or acknowledgment that cannot be conditional, and explore the nuanced exceptions and distinctions that Hanafi jurists have made.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three contracts and their common classification
Note that the passage addresses sharecropping, irrigation sharecropping, and admission. Each is analogized to a 'lease' (ijarah) or an 'admission' (iqrar). Understand that leases cannot be conditional because they are executory contracts requiring certainty of consideration.
The ruling applies to both muzara'ah and mu'amalah because they are forms of ijarah.
2
Understand the underlying principle: contracts of exchange and admissions cannot be conditional
A condition that introduces an additional obligation (like a loan) or a future event undermines the mutuality and finality required. For admissions, a conditional statement is not an admission but a contingent promise.
The exception for admission conditioned on death or a specific time is due to the likelihood of avoiding denial.
3
Apply the principle to sharecropping and irrigation
If a landowner says, 'I sharecrop with you on condition you lend me X,' the contract is invalid. The condition is not part of the sharecropping work and benefits one party extrinsically.
Al-Bazzaziyya distinguishes conditions that are part of the work (valid) from those that are not (invalidating). Neutral conditions (e.g., not watering one's share) do not invalidate.
4
Apply the principle to admission
Admission of a debt cannot be conditioned on a loan or future event. However, conditioning on death or the arrival of time is permissible and becomes binding immediately to prevent denial.
The branch case from al-Mabsut: a conditional admission like 'If I do not come tomorrow, I owe it' does not bind.
5
Recognize the nuance: conditioning i'tikaf is also invalid
The passage extends the principle to i'tikaf (spiritual retreat). Conditioning i'tikaf (e.g., 'I intend to observe i'tikaf if Allah wills') is invalid because the obligation must be unconditional.
The clarification emphasizes that the invalidity attaches to the commencement, not the vow itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والمزارعة) بأن قال زارعتك أرضي على أن تقرضني كذا أو إن قدم فلان لأنها إجازة فلا يصح تعليقها بالشرط كالإجازة؛ كذا ذكره العيني. وفي البزازية من المزارعة : شرطاً في المزارعة على المزارع أو رب الأرض ما ليس من أعمال المزارعة فسدت وما ينبت وما ينمي الخارج أو يزيد في وجود الخارج فهو من عمل المزارعة، وما لا ينبت ولا ينمي ولا يزيد في الخارج فليس من أعمالها، فإذا شرط على المزارع أو ربها الحصاد أو فعل ذلك للاحتراز عن الجحود أو دعوى الأجل فيلزمه للحال؛ ذكره العيني ومن فروع تعليقه ما ذكره في المبسوط والمحيط والولوالجية في كتاب الكفالة: لو ادعى رجل على رجل مالاً قفال له المطلوب إن لم آتك غداً فهو علي لم يلزمه إن لم يأت به غداً لأنه تعليق المجمع لالتزامه المنظومة والقدوري .اهـ. ومما يدل على ثبوت مسألة الاعتكاف ما في الفصول العمادية حيث قال وتعليق الاعتكاف بالشرط لا يصح ولا يلزمه ؛ كذا ذكر في صوم الأصل اهـ. الأصل من مؤلفات الإمام محمد رحمه الله تعالى. وفي الحواشي العزمية فساد الاعتكاف بالشرط بأن قال من عليه اعتكاف أيام نويت إن اعتكف عشرة أيام لأجله بشرط أن لا أصوم أو أباشر امرأتي في الاعتكاف أو أن أخرج عنه في أي وقت شئت بحاجة أو بغير حاجة يكون الاعتكاف فاسداً وتعليقه بالشرط بأن يقول نويت أن أعتكف عشرة أيام إن شاء الله تعالى .اهـ. وهذا ما ذكره صاحب النهر أولاً عن بعض أهل العصر ويرد عليه تعبير بعضهم بإيجاب الاعتكاف. وقد يجاب عنه بأن يقال لو نذر اعتکاف شهر مثلاً ثم دخل المسجد فقال نويت الاعتكاف المنذور إن شاء الله تعالى فقد أوجب الاعتكاف معلقاً فلم يصح، فليس المراد بتعليق إيجابه تعليق النذر به بل تعليق الشروع فيه فلا خطأ في كلامهم أصلاً وإنما الخطأ في فهم مرامهم، وحيث ثبت بطلان تعليقه بالشرط صح ذكره في هذا المقام . قوله : (لو ادعى رجل على رجل مالاً فقال المطلوب الخ قال الرملي : سيأتي في كتاب الإقرار
His statement: (And sharecropping) such as if he said 'I sharecrop my land with you on condition that you lend me such-and-such or if so-and-so comes' because it is a lease, so conditioning it by condition is invalid like a lease. Thus al-Ayni mentioned it. And in al-Bazzaziyya regarding sharecropping: a condition in sharecropping upon the sharecropper or landowner that is not from the work of sharecropping invalidates it. What grows, causes growth, or increases the produce is from the work of sharecropping; what does not grow nor cause growth nor increase the produce is not from its work. So if they condition upon the sharecropper or landowner the harvest or threshing, regardless of who has the seed, in the apparent narration. Then he said after many distinctions: All this is regarding a condition that benefits one of them. If they condition something that does not benefit, such as if they condition that one of them should not water his share, it does not invalidate the sharecropping. And regarding a corrupting condition, if they nullify it, the condition in the body of the contract does not become valid, otherwise it returns to being valid, etc. His statement: (And the mu'amalah) which is irrigation sharecropping, such as if he said 'I give you my trees or vines for irrigation on condition that you lend me such-and-such or if so-and-so comes' because it is also a lease. Thus al-Ayni mentioned it. His statement: (And admission) such as if he said 'So-and-so has a right against me of such-and-such if he lends me such-and-such or if so-and-so comes' because it is not something sworn by custom, so conditioning it by condition is invalid, unlike if he conditions it on his death or the arrival of time, then it is permissible. It is interpreted that he did that to avoid denial or claim of a term, so it becomes binding immediately. Al-Ayni mentioned it. Among the branches of conditioning it is what is mentioned in al-Mabsut, al-Muhit, and al-Walwalijiyya in the Book of Kafala: If a man claims money from a man, and the defendant says, 'If I do not come to you tomorrow, it is upon me,' it does not become binding if he does not come the next day because it is a conditional admission of the agreed commitment of the al-Manzuma and al-Quduri. This indicates the establishment of the issue of i'tikaf in al-Fusul al-Imadiyya where he said: Conditioning i'tikaf by condition is invalid and does not become binding; thus it is mentioned in Sawm al-Asl. Al-Asl is from the works of Imam Muhammad. And in al-Hawashi al-Azmiyya: The invalidity of i'tikaf by condition such as if one who has i'tikaf due says 'I intend to observe i'tikaf for ten days for him on condition that I do not fast or I touch my wife during i'tikaf or I leave it at any time I wish, with or without need,' then the i'tikaf is invalid. And conditioning it by condition such as saying 'I intend to observe i'tikaf for ten days if Allah wills.' This is what the author of al-Nahr mentioned from some contemporaries, and the expression of some of them about obligating i'tikaf is refuted. It may be answered by saying: If he vowed to observe i'tikaf for a month, then entered the mosque and said 'I intend the i'tikaf I vowed if Allah wills,' then he has obligated i'tikaf conditionally and it is not valid. The intended meaning is not conditioning its obligation but conditioning the commencement of it. So there is no error in their words at all; rather the error is in understanding their intent. Since the invalidity of conditioning it by condition is established, its mention in this context is correct. His statement: (If a man claims from a man money, and the defendant says...) al-Ramli said: It will come in the Book of Admission.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage presents several rulings on the invalidity of conditioning contractual acts. First, sharecropping (muzara'ah) cannot be conditioned on a loan or a future event because it is a type of lease (ijarah) and leases cannot be conditional. Al-Ayni is cited. Then details from al-Bazzaziyya explain that conditions not pertaining to the work of sharecropping invalidate the contract, while neutral conditions do not. Second, irrigation sharecropping (mu'amalah) has the same ruling as sharecropping because it is also a lease. Third, admission (iqrar) of a debt cannot be conditional on a loan or future event because it is not normally sworn by; however, conditioning it on death or time is permissible and becomes binding immediately to prevent denial. A branch from al-Mabsut shows a conditional admission like 'If I don't come, I owe it' does not bind. Then the text returns to i'tikaf, citing al-Fusul al-Imadiyya and al-Asl that conditioning i'tikaf is invalid. It clarifies that the error is not in the original texts but in the understanding of later scholars: the invalidity relates to conditioning the commencement, not the vow itself. Finally, it references al-Ramli for further detail in the Book of Admission.

Key Terms
المزارعة (al-muzara'ah): A contract of sharecropping where one provides land and the other provides labor and seeds, and they share the produce.
الاقرار (al-iqrar): An admission of a right or debt against oneself, which is binding and cannot be made conditional.
المعاملة (al-mu'amalah): Irrigation sharecropping, typically for trees and vines, analogous to muzara'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a valid admission (iqrar)?
A) 'I owe you $100 if you give me a ride.'
B) 'If I die, my debt to you is $500.'
C) 'I admit I owe you $200, provided you lend me $100.'
D) 'If you come to my house, I owe you $50.'

Key Takeaway
Sharecropping, irrigation sharecropping, and admission are all invalid if conditional on an extraneous benefit or future event, reflecting the Hanafi principle that contracts of exchange and acknowledgments must be definitive.

Conditions Invalidating Sharecropping and Irrigation Contracts
Rulings on conditions invalidating sharecropping and irrigation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which conditions invalidate a muzara'ah or mu'amalah contract and distinguish between beneficial and non-beneficial conditions.

Core Idea
A condition beneficial to one party and not part of the work invalidates the contract; a non-beneficial condition does not.

This lesson examines when a condition in a sharecropping or irrigation contract renders it invalid. In the Hanafi school, these contracts are treated as leases, so they cannot be conditional on future events or contain conditions outside the nature of the work. The text from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, citing al-Ayni and al-Bazzaziyyah, provides the key criteria: conditions that are part of the work (like harvesting) are valid, while beneficial conditions unrelated to the work cause invalidity. Non-beneficial conditions, even if stipulated, do not affect validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract type
Recognize that muzara'ah (sharecropping) and mu'amalah (irrigation) are treated as ijarah (lease) in Hanafi fiqh. This affects how conditions are regulated.
2
Classify the condition
Determine whether the condition benefits one party, both, or neither. Also check if it is part of the usual work of the contract (e.g., harvesting, threshing).
Conditions that are not part of the work and benefit one party invalidate.
3
Apply the invalidity rule
If the condition is beneficial to one party and not from the work, the contract becomes fasid. If it is non-beneficial (e.g., waiving watering), the contract remains valid.
A corrupting condition can be nullified, but if it is in the substance, the contract cannot become valid.
4
Note the exception for harvesting/threshing
According to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), stipulating harvesting or threshing does not invalidate, regardless of who owns the seed. These are considered part of the work.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والمزارعة) بأن قال زارعتك أرضي على أن تقرضني كذا أو إن قدم فلان لأنها إجازة فلا يصح تعليقها بالشرط كالإجازة؛ كذا ذكره العيني. وفي البزازية من المزارعة : شرطاً في المزارعة على المزارع أو رب الأرض ما ليس من أعمال المزارعة فسدت وما ينبت وما ينمي الخارج أو يزيد في وجود الخارج فهو من عمل المزارعة، وما لا ينبت ولا ينمي ولا يزيد في الخارج فليس من أعمالها، فإذا شرط على المزارع أو ربها الحصاد أو الدياسة من أيهما كان البذر في ظاهر الرواية اهـ . ثم قال بعد تفريقات كثيرة: هذا كله في الشرط النافع لأحدهما، وإن شرطا لا ينفع كما لو شرط أن لا يسقي أحدهما حصته لا تفسد المزارعة، وفيما إذا كان شرطاً مفسداً لو أبطلاه أن الشرط في صلب العقد لا ينقلب جائزاً وإلا عاد جائزاً إلى آخر ما فيها قوله : (والمعاملة) وهي المساقاة أن قال ساقيتك شجري أو كرمي على أن تقرضني كذا أو إن قدم فلان لأنها إجازة أيضاً؛ كذا ذكره العيني.
His saying: (and sharecropping) such that he says 'I sharecrop my land with you on condition that you lend me such-and-such' or 'if so-and-so comes' because it is a lease (ijarah), so its conditioning upon a condition is not valid, like the lease; thus mentioned by al-Ayni. And in al-Bazzaziyyah from sharecropping: a condition in sharecropping upon the sharecropper or the landowner of what is not among the works of sharecropping invalidates it; and what causes growth and increases the produce or increases the existence of the produce is from the works of sharecropping; what does not cause growth nor increase nor increase in the produce is not from its works. So if he stipulates upon the sharecropper or the landowner the harvesting or the threshing, from whichever of them the seed is, in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) it is valid. Then he said after many distinctions: all this is regarding a condition beneficial to one of them; if they stipulate something not beneficial, as if they stipulate that neither of them water his share, it does not invalidate the sharecropping. And regarding a corrupting condition, if they nullify it, the condition in the substance of the contract does not become permissible; otherwise it returns to being permissible. To the end of what is in it. His saying: (and mu'amalah) which is irrigation (musaqah), such that he says 'I irrigate your trees or your vineyard on condition that you lend me such-and-such' or 'if so-and-so comes' because it is also a lease; thus mentioned by al-Ayni.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explaining conditions that invalidate sharecropping (muzara'ah) and irrigation (mu'amalah) contracts. The author begins with al-Ayni's principle that both are considered leases (ijarah), so conditioning them on a future event is invalid, like a conditional lease. He then quotes al-Bazzaziyyah with a detailed criterion: conditions that are not part of the work of sharecropping invalidate the contract. The work of sharecropping is anything that helps growth and produce; harvesting and threshing are part of that work, so stipulating them does not invalidate—this is the relied-upon view (zahir al-riwayah). Afterwards, distinctions are made: beneficial conditions for one party cause invalidity; non-beneficial conditions (like waiving watering) do not. A corrupting condition can be nullified, but if it is in the substance of the contract, it cannot become valid; otherwise it may. The same rule applies to mu'amalah (irrigation), which is analogized to sharecropping.

Key Terms
المزارعة (al-muzara'ah): Sharecropping contract: one party provides land, the other labor, and they share the produce.
المعاملة (al-mu'amalah): Irrigation contract (musaqah): one party provides trees, the other waters them, sharing fruit.
الشرط النافع (al-shart al-nafi'): A condition that benefits one party, e.g., a loan or extra payment.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent or well-known narration in the Hanafi school, relied upon for fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sharecropping contract, which of the following conditions does NOT invalidate the contract?
A) The farmer must lend the landowner 50 dirhams.
B) The farmer must not water his own share of the crop.
C) The landowner must receive the produce if a specific person arrives.
D) The farmer must harvest the crop.

Key Takeaway
Only conditions that benefit one party and are not part of the work invalidate sharecropping and irrigation contracts.

Conditional Acknowledgment: General Rule and Exception
General ruling on conditional acknowledgment and an example from kafalah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional acknowledgment, identify the exception for death/time, and apply the rule to a case from the chapter of kafalah.

Core Idea
A conditional acknowledgment is void unless conditioned on death or a fixed time, in which case it binds immediately.

In Hanafi law, an acknowledgment (iqrar) must be definitive and unconditional. This lesson explains why conditional acknowledgments are generally invalid, the two exceptions (death and time), and an application from the chapter of surety (kafalah). The underlying rationale is the need for certainty in establishing rights and the potential for a conditioned acknowledgment to be a precaution against denial or dispute about a term.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is conditional acknowledgment (ta'liq al-iqrar). The ruling is batil (void) because it lacks the definitiveness required for an acknowledgment.
The general rule is stated by al-Ayni.
2
Note the exceptions
The text allows conditioning on death or the arrival of a time. In such cases, the acknowledgment is interpreted as a precaution against denial or claim of term, and it is binding immediately.
These exceptions are based on custom and necessity.
3
Apply the rule to a branch case
In kafalah, if the defendant says 'If I do not come tomorrow, the debt is on me,' it is not binding because it is a conditional acknowledgment. Note the condition here is not death/time.
This example is from al-Mabsut, al-Muhit, and al-Walwaljiyyah.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The general rule prevents uncertainty (gharar). The exceptions are based on common practice and the need to prevent disputes about terms.
The rationale is similar to the prohibition of conditional oaths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( والاقرار) بأن قال لفلان علي كذا إن أقرضني كذا أو إن قدم فلان لأنه ليس مما يحلف به عادة فلا يصح تعليقه بالشرط بخلاف ما إذا علقه بموته أو بمجيء الوقت فإنه يجوز، ويحمل على أنه فعل ذلك للاحتراز عن الجحود أو دعوى الأجل فيلزمه للحال؛ ذكره العيني ومن فروع تعليقه ما ذكره في المبسوط والمحيط والولوالجية في كتاب الكفالة: لو ادعى رجل على رجل مالاً قفال له المطلوب إن لم آتك غداً فهو علي لم يلزمه إن لم يأت به غداً لأنه تعليق
His saying: (and acknowledgment) such that he says 'I owe so-and-so such-and-such if he lends me such-and-such' or 'if so-and-so comes' because it is not something by which an oath is customarily taken, so its conditioning upon a condition is not valid, unlike if he conditions it upon his death or upon the arrival of time, then it is permissible, and it is interpreted that he did that to avoid denial or claim of term, so it becomes binding immediately; mentioned by al-Ayni. And among its branches of conditioning what is mentioned in al-Mabsut, al-Muhit, and al-Walwaljiyyah in the book of Suretyship: If a man claims money from another, and the defendant says 'If I do not come to you tomorrow, it is upon me' it does not become binding upon him if he does not come the next day, because it is a conditioning.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This is a ruling statement on conditional acknowledgment (iqrar). Al-Ayni explains that if someone makes an acknowledgment conditioned on a future event (like 'I owe you if you lend me'), it is invalid because it resembles a gamble (khatar). However, if the condition is death or the arrival of a specific time, it is valid and the acknowledgment is considered immediate, interpreted as a precaution against denial or dispute about the term. The text then gives a branch from the book of Kafalah: if the defendant says 'If I don't come tomorrow, I owe you', it is not binding even if he doesn't come, because it is a conditional acknowledgment and hence invalid.

Key Terms
الإقرار (al-iqrar): An acknowledgment of a right or debt by a person against himself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following conditional acknowledgments is valid?
A) 'I owe you 100 if you lend me money'
B) 'I owe you 100 if so-and-so comes'
C) 'I owe you 100 when I die'
D) 'I owe you 100 if I do not come tomorrow'

Key Takeaway
A conditional acknowledgment is void in the Hanafi school unless conditioned on death or a fixed time, in which case it binds immediately.

Types of Invalid Conditional Acknowledgment in Hanafi Fiqh
Multiple case rulings on conditional acknowledgment from various sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain why conditional acknowledgments tied to risk or ignorance are invalid according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Conditional acknowledgment is void—it resembles gambling and lacks the certainty required for legal recognition.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq presents several case rulings on conditional acknowledgment (al-iqrar al-mu'allaq). The author expands on the general principle that conditioning an acknowledgment on a future event or linking it to unknown content renders it invalid. We will examine cases from sale, oath, divorce, and debt registration to see how this principle applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition in each statement
Read each case and determine what the acknowledgment is made conditional upon—e.g., a future event (swearing), a later denial, or the content of a document.
2
Apply the rule that conditioning acknowledgment makes it a gamble
Once the condition is identified, note that Hanafi usul holds that conditioning an iqrar introduces risk (khatar) and removes the certainty necessary for a valid acknowledgment. Hence it is void.
The text uses the term 'mukhatara' (gamble) to describe such statements.
3
Distinguish between acknowledgment of a past right and creation of a new right
The passage asks whether the rule applies to divorce and manumission. The author notes a difference: creating (insha') a divorce under coercion is valid, but acknowledging it under coercion is not. This highlights that iqrar and insha' have different conditions.
Acknowledgment confirms a pre-existing right; creation establishes a new one.
4
Evaluate acknowledgment based on unknown content
Analyze the cases from al-Bazzaziyyah: acknowledgment linked to 'whatever is in the plaintiff's note' or 'whatever is in the register'. Determine validity based on whether the content is known and whether pointing specifies it.
If the content is unknown, the acknowledgment is void due to jahalah (ignorance).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لو ادعى رجل على رجل مالاً فقال المطلوب الخ قال الرملي : سيأتي في كتاب الإقرار الإقرار بالخطر وتعليقه بالشرط باطل .اهـ. وفي المبسوط من باب الإقرار بكذا وإلا فعليه كذا لو قال قد ابتعت من فلان هذا العبد بألف وإلا فلفلان علي خمسمائة درهم إن أقر رب العبد لزمه الألف، وإن أنكر ذلك لم يلزمه شيء لأنه صار راداً لإقراره حين أنكر ببيع العبد منه وإقراره بالخمسمائة كان معلقاً بشرط وهو باطل من بيع أصله اهـ. وقال في باب اليمين والاقرار : رجل قال لفلان علي ألف درهم إن حلف أو على أن يحلف أو إذا حلف أو متى يحلف أو حين حلف أو مع يمينه أو في يمينه أو بعد يمينه فخلف فلان على ذلك وجحد المقر المال لم يؤخذ بالمال لأن هذا ليس بإقرار وإنما هو مخاطرة، ومعناه أنه علق الإقرار بشرط فيه خطر وهو بمنزله الخصم والتعليق بالشرط يخرج كلامه أن يكون إقراراً اهـ. فإن من قلت : هل يدخل في الإقرار بالطلاق والعتاق كما لو قال إن دخلت الدار فأنا مقر بطلاقها أو بعتقه ويفرق بين الإقرار بهما وبين الإنشاء؟ قلت: ظاهر الإطلاق الدخول ولم أره صريحاً، ويدل على الفرق بينهما ما نقلناه في كتاب الطلاق من هذا الشرح أنه لو أكره على إنشاء الطلاق فطلق وقع، ولو أكره على الإقرار به فأقر لم يقع. وفي البزازية من الإقرار : ادعى مالاً فقال المدعى عليه كلما يوجد في تذكرة المدعي بخطة فقد التزمته لا يكون إقراراً لأنه محفوظ عن أصحابنا أنه لو قال كلما أقر فلان علي فأنا مقر به لا يلزمه إذا أقر به فلان . وعلى هذا إذا كان بين اثنين أخذ وعطاء فقال المطلوب للطالب ما تقول فهو كذلك أو ما يكون في جريدتك فهو كذلك لا يكون إقراراً إلا إذا كان في الجريدة شيء معلوم أو ذكر المدعي شيئاً معلوماً فقال المدعي ما ذكرنا يكون تصديقاً لأن التصديق لا يحلق بالمجهول. وكذا إذا أشار للجريدة وقال ما فيها فهو علي كذلك يصبح، ولو لم يكن مشاراً إليه لا يصح للجهالة اهـ.
His saying: (If a man claims money from another, and the defendant says...). Al-Ramli said: It will come in the book of Acknowledgment that acknowledgment by risk (khatar) and its conditioning by condition is void. In al-Mabsut from the chapter of Acknowledgment: 'Such-and-such, otherwise such-and-such is upon him.' If he said 'I have bought this slave from so-and-so for one thousand, otherwise I owe so-and-so five hundred dirhams' — if the owner of the slave acknowledges, the thousand becomes binding; if he denies, nothing becomes binding because he became a rejecter of his acknowledgment when he denied the sale of the slave from him, and his acknowledgment of the five hundred was conditioned by a condition, and it is void from the origin of the sale. And he said in the chapter of Oath and Acknowledgment: A man said to another 'I owe one thousand dirhams if he swears' or 'on condition that he swears' or 'when he swears' or 'whenever he swears' or 'when he swore' or 'with his oath' or 'in his oath' or 'after his oath' — then that man swore and the acknowledger denied the money, he is not taken for the money because this is not an acknowledgment but rather a gamble (mukhatara), and its meaning is that he conditioned the acknowledgment by a condition that contains risk; it is like a bet, and conditioning by condition removes his speech from being an acknowledgment. So if you ask: Does this include acknowledgment of divorce and manumission, as if he said 'If you enter the house, I acknowledge her divorce' or 'his manumission'? And is there a difference between acknowledgment of these and creation (insha')? I say: The apparent general inclusion is, but I have not seen it explicitly. And evidence for the difference between them is what we narrated in the book of Divorce from this commentary: If he is coerced to create a divorce and he divorces, it occurs; if he is coerced to acknowledge it and he acknowledges, it does not occur. And in al-Bazzaziyyah from Acknowledgment: He claimed money, and the defendant said 'Whenever it is found in the plaintiff's note in his handwriting, I have undertaken it' — this is not an acknowledgment, because it is preserved from our companions that if he said 'Whenever so-and-so acknowledges against me, I acknowledge it' it does not become binding when so-and-so acknowledges. Likewise, if between two there is give-and-take, and the defendant says to the claimant 'What you say is so' or 'What is in your register is so' — this is not an acknowledgment unless it is in the register something known, or the claimant mentions something known and the defendant says 'We have mentioned' then it is a confirmation (tasdiq) because confirmation does not attach to the unknown. Similarly, if he points to the register and says 'What is in it is upon me' — it becomes valid; but if there is no pointing, it is not valid due to ignorance.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage presents several case studies on conditional acknowledgment from various sources. The first case from al-Mabsut involves a conditional statement in a sale: 'I bought this slave for 1000, otherwise I owe 500 to someone else.' If the seller acknowledges the sale, the 1000 is binding; if he denies, the conditional acknowledgment is void. The second case from the chapter on oath and acknowledgment lists various ways of tying acknowledgment to a condition (if he swears, when he swears, etc.). Such statements are considered gambling, not valid acknowledgment. The third question addresses whether this includes divorce and manumission acknowledgments. The author distinguishes between creation (insha') of divorce/manumission and acknowledgment of them: coercion invalidates creation but not acknowledgment? Actually the text says the reverse: coercion on creating divorce is effective, but on acknowledgment it is not. So there is a difference. The final case from al-Bazzaziyyah concerns acknowledgment based on a note or register: saying 'whatever is in the plaintiff's note is acknowledged' is not valid unless the content is known; similarly, pointing to a register without specification is invalid due to ignorance.

Key Terms
المخاطرة (al-mukhatara): A gamble or risk: a statement that depends on an uncertain event.
التذكرة (al-tadhkirah): A note or written record of debts.
الإقرار المعلق (al-iqrar al-mu'allaq): Conditional acknowledgment: linking an acknowledgment to a future condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a defendant says to the plaintiff: 'Whatever is in your register is upon me'?
A) It is a valid acknowledgment and binding
B) It is invalid because the content is unknown
C) It is valid only if the register is signed
D) It is valid only if the defendant points to the register

Key Takeaway
Conditional acknowledgment is void in Hanafi fiqh because it lacks the certainty required for legal recognition.

Conditional Iqrar and Its Invalidity Due to Risk (Khatar)
Ruling on conditional iqrar in a sale scenario with an example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional iqrar and apply it to a sale scenario to determine liability.

Core Idea
A conditional acknowledgment (iqrar) tied to a risky condition is void; only an unconditional, definite iqrar is binding.

This passage from al-Mabsut illustrates a case where a buyer makes a conditional acknowledgment about the price in a sale. The Hanafi school holds that such conditional iqrar is invalid because it involves uncertainty (khatar). Understanding this ruling clarifies the boundaries of valid acknowledgments in Islamic law and prevents enforcing uncertain obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a conditional acknowledgment in a sale. The ruling: it is void (batil) because it involves risk (khatar).
2
Understand the specific scenario
The buyer says: 'I purchased this slave from you for one thousand, otherwise I owe you five hundred.' The condition is the owner's acknowledgment of the sale.
The phrase 'otherwise' introduces uncertainty.
3
Apply the ruling to both outcomes
If the owner acknowledges the sale, the buyer owes one thousand (sale confirmed). If the owner denies, the conditional iqrar of five hundred is void, and the original iqrar of the sale is also rejected, so nothing is owed.
The denial nullifies the entire statement.
4
Extract the general principle
A conditional iqrar tied to a risky condition (khatar) is batil. The original iqrar is also rejected if the condition fails.
This aligns with the Hanafi emphasis on certainty in contracts.
5
Connect to broader Hanafi doctrine
Hanafi law prohibits gharar; similarly, conditional iqrar with khatar is invalid to prevent uncertainty in obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المبسوط من باب الإقرار بكذا وإلا فعليه كذا لو قال قد ابتعت من فلان هذا العبد بألف وإلا فلفلان علي خمسمائة درهم إن أقر رب العبد لزمه الألف، وإن أنكر ذلك لم يلزمه شيء لأنه صار راداً لإقراره حين أنكر ببيع العبد منه وإقراره بالخمسمائة كان معلقاً بشرط وهو باطل من بيع أصله اهـ.
And in al-Mabsut from the chapter of acknowledgment: such and such otherwise he owes such and such: if he said, 'I purchased this slave from so-and-so for one thousand, otherwise I owe so-and-so five hundred dirhams.' If the slave's owner acknowledges, he is liable for one thousand; if he denies that, nothing is binding on him because he became a rejecter of his acknowledgment when he denied the sale of the slave from him, and his acknowledgment of the five hundred was conditional upon a condition, and it is void due to the invalidity of the original sale. End.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on a specific case of conditional iqrar in a sale. The Hanafi position is that a conditional acknowledgment tied to a risky condition (khatar) is void. In the example, a person says he bought a slave for 1000 but also says otherwise he owes 500. The condition 'otherwise' introduces uncertainty. If the owner acknowledges the sale, the 1000 is binding because the sale is confirmed. If the owner denies the sale, the whole statement is void because the iqrar of 500 was conditional on a void sale, and the original iqrar of the sale is rejected. The principle: an iqrar cannot be made conditional in a way that implies risk (gharar).

Key Terms
الإقرار المعلق (al-iqrar al-mu'allaq): An acknowledgment that is tied to a future condition; such iqrar is void if the condition involves risk (khatar).
خطر (khatar): Risk or uncertainty that makes a conditional iqrar invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The buyer must pay 1000 dirhams.
C) The buyer owes nothing.
D) The slave is freed.

Key Takeaway
A conditional iqrar tied to a risky condition (khatar) is void in Hanafi law; only an unconditional, definite iqrar is binding.

Conditional Iqrar with an Oath is Not Valid Iqrar
Ruling that conditional iqrar tied to an oath is not iqrar but a wager

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on conditional iqrar tied to an oath and explain why it is considered a wager rather than a valid acknowledgment.

Core Idea
A conditional acknowledgment tied to an oath is a void wager, not a valid iqrar.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies that declaring a debt contingent on someone's oath is not a valid acknowledgment. Instead, it falls under mukhatara (wager), a prohibited transaction. Understanding this distinction prevents misuse of iqrar in legal settings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
Recognize the man's statement: 'I owe you a thousand dirhams if he swears' or similar phrasing. This is a conditional acknowledgment.
The condition is the occurrence of an oath.
2
Analyze the Condition
Note that the iqrar is tied to an oath. The condition involves risk because the occurrence of the oath is uncertain and controllable by the other party.
Risk (khatar) is a key element.
3
State the Ruling
The Hanafi ruling: such a statement is not a valid iqrar; it is a wager (mukhatara). The acknowledger is not liable even if the condition occurs.
The ruling is based on the presence of risk and similarity to gambling.
4
Understand the Reasoning (Talil)
The condition involves risk (khatar), making the statement akin to a bet. Tying an acknowledgment to an uncertain future event voids the iqrar because it lacks the required definiteness.
Iqrar must be absolute and unconditional.
5
Apply the Principle
Any conditional iqrar tied to an oath (using words like 'if', 'when', 'after', etc.) is invalid. The principle extends to other similar conditions involving risk.
The ruling is strict: no valid iqrar if conditioned on an oath.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال في باب اليمين والاقرار : رجل قال لفلان علي ألف درهم إن حلف أو على أن يحلف أو إذا حلف أو متى يحلف أو حين حلف أو مع يمينه أو في يمينه أو بعد يمينه فخلف فلان على ذلك وجحد المقر المال لم يؤخذ بالمال لأن هذا ليس بإقرار وإنما هو مخاطرة، ومعناه أنه علق الإقرار بشرط فيه خطر وهو بمنزله الخصم والتعليق بالشرط يخرج كلامه أن يكون إقراراً اهـ.
And he said in the chapter of oath and acknowledgment: A man said to someone, 'I owe you a thousand dirhams if he swears, or on condition that he swears, or when he swears, or whenever he swears, or when he swore, or with his oath, or in his oath, or after his oath.' Then that person swore to that, and the acknowledger denied the wealth. He is not taken for the wealth because this is not an acknowledgment; rather it is a wager, and its meaning is that he tied the acknowledgment to a condition involving risk, and it is like a bet, and tying to a condition removes his speech from being an acknowledgment. End.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage addresses conditional iqrar tied to an oath. The Hanafi ruling is that such a statement is not a valid iqrar; it is a type of wager (mukhatara) because the condition involves risk (the occurrence of the oath). Regardless of the wording (if, when, after, etc.), the iqrar is not binding. The key principle: an iqrar must be definite and unconditional; tying it to a future uncertain event voids it as an iqrar.

Key Terms
مخاطرة (mukhatara): A wager or risky undertaking, not a valid acknowledgment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the iqrar in the example not binding on the acknowledger?
A) Because the condition is impossible.
B) Because it is tied to an oath and involves risk.
C) Because the amount is unclear.
D) Because the acknowledger did not repeat the statement.

Key Takeaway
A conditional iqrar tied to an oath is not a valid acknowledgment but a void wager.

Iqrar by Reference to a Document: Validity Depends on Certainty
Rulings on iqrar by reference to a document

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for iqrar by reference to a document and identify the condition (knowledge) that makes it valid or invalid.

Core Idea
An iqrar made by referencing an unknown document is void; certainty is required.

In Hanafi law, iqrar (acknowledgment) must be definite and certain. This passage from al-Bazzaziyya addresses cases where a person acknowledges a debt by referring to a document or list without specifying its contents. The ruling clarifies when such indirect acknowledgments are valid and when they are void due to ignorance (jahalah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Recognize that the legal act under discussion is iqrar (acknowledgment) made by reference to a document or list, not a direct verbal statement.
This is a form of indirect iqrar.
2
State the general rule
From the passage, extract the rule: 'If the defendant says whatever is in the plaintiff's document, I owe it, it is not an iqrar.'
The key phrase is 'لا يكون إقراراً' (it is not an iqrar).
3
Identify the condition for validity
The passage states that such an iqrar is valid only if the contents of the document are known (معلوم) or if the claimant specifies a known item and the defendant confirms.
Knowledge (علم) is the condition that transforms the statement from invalid iqrar to valid tasdiq (confirmation).
4
Distinguish tasdiq from iqrar
Tasdiq is a confirmation of a known claim, while iqrar is an original acknowledgment. The passage says 'التصديق لا يحلق بالمجهول' (confirmation does not attach to the unknown).
Tasdiq requires knowledge; iqrar by reference without knowledge is void.
5
Apply the rule to pointed documents
If the person physically points to a document and says 'What is in it is owed by me,' it becomes valid because the pointing removes uncertainty.
Pointing (الإشارة) makes the document specific and the contents known.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي البزازية من الإقرار : ادعى مالاً فقال المدعى عليه كلما يوجد في تذكرة المدعي بخطة فقد التزمته لا يكون إقراراً لأنه محفوظ عن أصحابنا أنه لو قال كلما أقر فلان علي فأنا مقر به لا يلزمه إذا أقر به فلان . وعلى هذا إذا كان بين اثنين أخذ وعطاء فقال المطلوب للطالب ما تقول فهو كذلك أو ما يكون في جريدتك فهو كذلك لا يكون إقراراً إلا إذا كان في الجريدة شيء معلوم أو ذكر المدعي شيئاً معلوماً فقال المدعي ما ذكرنا يكون تصديقاً لأن التصديق لا يحلق بالمجهول. وكذا إذا أشار للجريدة وقال ما فيها فهو علي كذلك يصبح، ولو لم يكن مشاراً إليه لا يصح للجهالة اهـ.
And in al-Bazzaziyya from iqrar: He claimed wealth, so the defendant said, 'Whatever is found in the plaintiff's document in his handwriting, I have undertaken it.' This is not an iqrar because it is preserved from our scholars that if he said, 'Whenever so-and-so acknowledges against me, I acknowledge it,' it is not binding on him when so-and-so acknowledges it. And likewise, if there is a debit-credit relationship between two people, and the defendant says to the claimant, 'Whatever you say is so,' or 'Whatever is in your list is so,' it is not an iqrar unless there is something known in the list or the claimant mentions something known and the defendant says what we mentioned, then it is a confirmation (tasdiq) because confirmation is not attached to the unknown. Similarly, if he points to the list and says, 'What is in it is owed by me,' it becomes valid; if he did not point to it, it is not valid due to ignorance. End.
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage from al-Bazzaziyya discusses iqrar by referencing a document or list. The Hanafi position is that such iqrar is not valid if the contents are unknown. For example, saying 'Whatever is in your list, I owe it' is not binding because the iqrar is uncertain (jahalah). However, if the document is pointed to and its contents are known or specified, then it is valid. The ruling is based on the principle that iqrar must be definite; an iqrar based on ignorance is void.

Key Terms
تصديق (tasdiq): Confirmation of a known claim, distinct from iqrar which requires specific knowledge.
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty about the subject matter, which invalidates the iqrar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does an iqrar by reference to a document become valid?
A) Always, if the document exists and is in writing.
B) Only if the document's contents are known or specified.
C) Only if the document is pointed to but not necessarily known.
D) Never, because it is indirect.

Key Takeaway
An iqrar by reference to a document is valid only when the contents are known or the document is pointed to, removing uncertainty.

Suspended Waqf is Invalid: The Relied-Upon Hanafi Ruling
Commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq explaining invalid conditions in waqf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a suspended waqf and explain why waqf cannot be suspended like a vow.

Core Idea
Waqf is an immediate transfer; suspension by condition invalidates it entirely.

A common misunderstanding is that waqf, being a charitable act, can be suspended like a vow. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on a waqf that is conditioned upon a future event, such as 'If my son arrives, my house is a waqf.' The passage clarifies that such a waqf is invalid because waqf does not bear suspension by a risk (khatar), unlike nadhr (vows). We will explore the textual evidence and the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on this point.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the legal ruling on a waqf that is suspended upon a condition like 'If so-and-so arrives, my house is a waqf'? The text states it is invalid (batil).
2
Locate the basis for the ruling
Why is it invalid? Because waqf is a non-compensatory contract (tabarru') that requires immediate (munajjaz) execution. It cannot be suspended because it is not an oath (yamin).
The text analogizes to iqrar (acknowledgment) which is also invalid when suspended.
3
Identify the ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school
Is there any difference of opinion? Yes, there are two narrations: one that suspension invalidates (the relied-upon view), and another that it might be valid. The commentator weakens the latter.
References: Jami' al-Fusulayn, Fath Kitab al-Waqf.
4
Understand the distinction from vows (nadh)
Why is a suspended vow valid but a suspended waqf not? Because a vow can be suspended and one swears by it (it is akin to an oath), whereas waqf is not something one swears by.
The text from al-Is'af: 'if I recover, my land is a sadaqah endowed' is not a vow but a suspended waqf, which is invalid.
5
Evaluate corrupt conditions that negate the essence of waqf
What about conditions like retaining ownership or the original corpus? Such conditions make the waqf invalid because they contradict the essential nature of waqf (transfer of ownership).
This is a separate category: shart fasad that nullifies the waqf entirely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب المتفرقات عن النهاية كما هنا أن الإقرار المعلق باطل، ونقل عن المحيط أن الإقرار صحيح والشرط باطل، ونقل عن المبسوط ما يشهد للمحيط فظاهره ترجيحه والحق تضعيفه لتصريحهم هنا بأن الإقرار والوقف لا يصح تعليقه بالشرط وأنه يبطل بالشرط الفاسد. قوله : (والوقف) بأن قال وقفت داري إن قدم فلان أو وقفت داري عليك إن أخبرتني بقدم زيد لأنه ليس مما يحلف به أيضاً فلا يصح تعليقه بالشرط؛ كذا ذكره العيني. وفي جامع الفصولين والوقف في رواية فظاهره أن في صحة تعليقه روايتين، وفي فتح كتاب الوقف وشرطه أن يكون منجزاً غير معلق فلو قال إن قدم ولدي فداري صدقة موقوفة على المساكين فجاء ولده لا يصير وقفاً .اهـ. وفي الإسعاف: ولو قال إذا جاء غدا وإذا جاء رأس الشهر أو قال إذا كلمت فلاناً أو إذا تزوجت فلانة وما أشبه ذلك فأرضي هذه صدقة موقوفة يكون الوقف باطلاً لأنه تعليق والوقف لا يحتمل التعليق بالخطر لكونه مما لا يحلف به بخلاف النذر لأنه يحتمل التعليق ويحلف به فلو قال إن برئت من مرضي هذا فأرضي صدقة موقوفة يلزمه التصدق بعينها إذا وجد الشرط، ولو قال صدقة موقوفة إن شئت أو أحببت أو رضيت أو هويت كان باطلاً .اهـ. ولم يذكر العيني صورة بطلانه بالشرط الفاسد وصورته ما في الإسعاف وقفها على أن له أصلها أو على أن يزول ملكه عنها أو على أصلها ويتصدق بثمنها كان الوقف باطلاً اهـ. يبيع وقدمنا في الوقف أن شرط الاستبدال صحيح على المفتى به قوله : (والتحكيم بأن يقول المحكمان إذا أهل الشهر أو قالا لعبد أو كافر، إذا أعتقت أو أسلمت فاحكم بيننا وهذا عند أبي يوسف وعند محمد يجوز تعليقه بشرط وإضافته إلى زمان كالوكالة والإمارة والقضاء. وله أن التحكيم تولية صورة وصلح معنى فباعتبار أنه صلح لا يصح تعليقه ولا إضافته وباعتبار أنه تولية يصح بالشك والاحتمال؛ ذكره العيني. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان من القضاء الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف. وقد فات المصنف إبطال الأجل. قال في البزازية : وإبطال الأجل يبطل بالشرط الفاسد بأن قال كلما حل نجم ولم تؤد فالمال حال صح وصار حالاً اهـ. وعبارة الخلاصة: وإبطال الأجل يبطل بالشرط الفاسد، ولو قال كلما دخل نجم فلم تؤد فالمال حال صح والمال يصير حالاً اهـ. فجعلهما مسألتين وهو الصواب. وأما قوله في البزازية «بأن قال تصويراً للأولى» فسهو ظاهر لأنه لو كان كذلك لبقي الأجل فكيف يقول صح فيتأمل. وفاته أيضاً تعليق الرد بالعيب فإنه باطل وله الرد كما في البزازية، وليس هو من القسم الأول لأنه لا يبطل بالشرط الفاسد كما ذكره المصنف في القسم الثاني ولا يصح تعليقه فهو كالنكاح. وبهذا علم المصنف فاته بيان ما لا يصح تعليقه ولا يبطل بالشرط الفاسد كما فاته ما يجوز تعليقه. قوله : (ولم يذكر العيني صورة بطلانه بالشرط الفاسد الخ) أقول في كونه مما يبطل بالشرط الفاسد نظر لما قدمه المؤلف من الأصل وهو أن ما كان مبادلة مال بغير مال أو كان من التبرعات لا يبطل بالشرط الفاسد والوقف من التبرعات وفي العزمية على الدرر : صرح قاضيخان بأن الوقف لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة ا.هـ. وقد يجاب أن الشرط الفاسد إنما لا يبطل التبرعات إذا لم يكن موجباً نقض أصله. فإن اشتراط أن تبقى رقبة الأرض له أو أنه لا يزول ملكه عنها أو أنه على أصله بلا استبدال شيء مكانها نقض للتبرع لأنه بذلك الشرط لم يوجد التبرع أصلاً كما إذا قال في الهبة وهبتك هذه الدار بشرط أن لا تخرج عن ملكي بخلاف ما إذا قال بشرط أن تخدمني سنة تأمل.
Book of Sale, Chapter of Miscellaneous Matters. From al-Nihayah, here that suspended iqrar is void, and transmitted from al-Muhit that iqrar is valid and the condition is void, and transmitted from al-Mabsut what supports al-Muhit, so apparently it is preferred, but the truth is to weaken it because they explicitly stated here that iqrar and waqf cannot be suspended with a condition and that they become invalid with a corrupt condition. His statement: (And waqf) by saying 'I have endowed my house if so-and-so arrives' or 'I have endowed my house upon you if you inform me of so-and-so's arrival' because it is not something one swears by, so its suspension with a condition is not valid; thus mentioned by al-Ayni. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn, waqf according to one narration, so apparently there are two narrations about the validity of its suspension. And in Fath Kitab al-Waqf, its condition is that it be immediate, not suspended. So if he says 'If my son arrives, my house is a sadaqah endowed upon the poor' and his son arrives, it does not become a waqf. In al-Is'af: And if he says 'When tomorrow comes' or 'When the beginning of the month comes' or 'If I speak to so-and-so' or 'If I marry so-and-so' and the like, 'this land of mine is a sadaqah endowed,' the waqf is void because it is a suspension, and waqf does not bear suspension by risk because it is not something one swears by, unlike a vow because it bears suspension and one swears by it. So if he says 'If I recover from this illness, my land is a sadaqah endowed,' it is necessary for him to give it in charity when the condition occurs. And if he says 'A sadaqah endowed if you wish, or desire, or are pleased, or love,' it is void. Al-Ayni did not mention the form of its invalidation by a corrupt condition, and its form is what is in al-Is'af: that he endows it on condition that he retains its original ownership, or that his ownership does not cease, or that he retains its original and gives its price in charity, the waqf is void. The author said: 'and we have previously mentioned in waqf that the condition of substitution is valid according to the fatwa.' His statement: (And tahkim) by the two arbitrators saying 'When the month begins' or they say to a slave or an unbeliever, 'If you are freed or become Muslim, then judge between us,' and this is according to Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad, its suspension by a condition and its addition to a time are permissible, like agency, governorship, and judgeship. He (Muhammad) has that tahkim is a delegation in form and a compromise in meaning. So, considering it is a compromise, its suspension and addition are not valid; considering it is a delegation, it is valid by doubt and probability; mentioned by al-Ayni. And in Fatawa Qadikhan from the chapter of judiciary, the fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's statement. The author also missed (the ruling of) ibtal al-ajal. He said in al-Bazzaziyyah: And ibtal al-ajal becomes invalid with a corrupt condition, by saying 'Whenever a installment comes due and you do not pay, the entire amount becomes due immediately' - it is valid and the amount becomes due immediately. And the expression of al-Khulasah: And ibtal al-ajal becomes invalid with a corrupt condition, and if he says 'Whenever an installment enters and you do not pay, the amount becomes due immediately' - it is valid and the amount becomes due immediately. So he made them two issues, which is correct. As for his statement in al-Bazzaziyyah 'by saying' as a depiction of the first, it is an apparent oversight because if it were so, the deferment would remain; how then does he say 'it is valid'? So contemplate. He also missed the suspension of the option of defect (khiyar al-ayb), for it is void and he (the buyer) has the right of return, as in al-Bazzaziyyah. It is not of the first category because it is not invalidated by a corrupt condition as the author mentioned in the second category, nor is its suspension valid; so it is like marriage. By this, the author missed the explanation of what cannot be suspended and is not invalidated by a corrupt condition, just as he missed what can be suspended. His statement: (And he did not mention al-Ayni the form of its invalidation by a corrupt condition etc.) I say regarding its being invalidated by a corrupt condition, there is consideration based on what the author presented as the principle, which is that what is an exchange of property for non-property or is from voluntary donations is not invalidated by a corrupt condition, and waqf is from voluntary donations. And in al-Azimiyyah on al-Durar: Qadikhan explicitly stated that waqf is not invalidated by corrupt conditions. And it can be answered that a corrupt condition only does not invalidate voluntary donations if it does not necessitate nullifying its essence. For stipulating that the corpus of the land remains his, or that his ownership does not cease, or that it remains as it is without substitution of something in its place, nullifies the donation because with that condition the donation did not occur at all, as if he said in gift: 'I have gifted you this house on condition that it does not leave my ownership,' unlike if he said 'on condition that you serve me for a year.' Consider.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining which contracts become invalid when a corrupt condition (shart fasad) is attached, and which remain valid with the condition being void. The commentator begins with iqrar (acknowledgment): a suspended iqrar is invalid according to al-Nihayah, but there is a narration from al-Muhit that it is valid, and the commentator prefers the view of invalidity because iqrar is not something one swears by, similar to waqf. For waqf, the ruling is that it cannot be suspended because it is not a form of oath; it is an immediate transfer of ownership. The text mentions two narrations regarding the validity of suspension, but the relied-upon position is that suspension invalidates the waqf. The commentator then discusses corrupt conditions such as stipulating that the donor retains ownership, which makes the waqf void because it contradicts the essence of waqf. For tahkim (arbitration), there is a dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: Abu Yusuf does not allow suspension, while Muhammad allows it by analogy with agency. The fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view. For ibtal al-ajal (annulment of deferment), a condition that accelerates the debt upon default is valid and does not invalidate the underlying contract; however, the condition itself is a form of ibtal al-ajal, which is a contract that is invalidated by a corrupt condition. The commentator clarifies the correct depiction of this issue. Finally, the commentator criticizes the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq for omitting the category of things that are not invalidated by a corrupt condition nor can be suspended, such as the option of defect (khiyar al-ayb), which is like marriage in that respect. Throughout, the commentator relies on the principle that contracts involving exchange of property (mu'awadat maliyyah) are affected by corrupt conditions related to riba, while non-compensatory contracts (tabarru'at) are not invalidated by such conditions, unless the condition negates the essence of the donation.

Key Terms
الوقف المعلق (al-waqf al-mu'allaq): A waqf that is made contingent upon a future condition, e.g., 'If my son arrives, this house is a waqf.'
النذر (al-nadhr): A vow to perform an act of worship or charity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is a suspended vow (nadh) valid but a suspended waqf invalid?
A) Because a vow is an oath and waqf is not.
B) Because a vow is less important than waqf.
C) Because waqf requires a judge's approval.
D) Because a vow can be revoked later.

Key Takeaway
A waqf must be immediate; any conditional suspension invalidates it.
