Tahkim (Arbitration) and the Effect of Suspension: Abu Yusuf's View is Fatwa
Commentary explaining intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on suspended tahkim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on suspended tahkim and explain the ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Core Idea
Tahkim is a compromise in meaning; suspension invalidates it per the fatwa.

Tahkim (arbitration) is a contract where disputants appoint an arbitrator. When is tahkim invalid due to a condition? This lesson examines the ruling when the appointment is suspended on a future event. There is a well-known ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on this issue. The passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that the fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view that suspension invalidates the arbitration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on suspended tahkim
What is the ruling when the two parties say to the arbitrator: 'When the month begins, judge between us'? The text states that according to Abu Yusuf, it is invalid; according to Muhammad, it is valid.
2
Analyze the reasoning of each imam
Why does Muhammad allow it? Because tahkim is a delegation (tawliyah) in form, and agency can be suspended. Why does Abu Yusuf not allow it? Because tahkim is also a compromise (sulh) in meaning, and sulh cannot be suspended or added to a time.
The text: 'tahkim is a delegation in form and a compromise in meaning'.
3
Determine the fatwa (mufta bihi)
Which view is relied upon? The text cites Fatawa Qadikhan that the fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's statement.
So, suspended tahkim is invalid according to the operative ruling.
4
Contrast with agency (wakalah)
Why is agency different? Agency can be suspended because it is purely a delegation without the element of compromise.
The text mentions 'like agency, governorship, and judgeship' for Muhammad's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب المتفرقات عن النهاية كما هنا أن الإقرار المعلق باطل، ونقل عن المحيط أن الإقرار صحيح والشرط باطل، ونقل عن المبسوط ما يشهد للمحيط فظاهره ترجيحه والحق تضعيفه لتصريحهم هنا بأن الإقرار والوقف لا يصح تعليقه بالشرط وأنه يبطل بالشرط الفاسد. قوله : (والوقف) بأن قال وقفت داري إن قدم فلان أو وقفت داري عليك إن أخبرتني بقدم زيد لأنه ليس مما يحلف به أيضاً فلا يصح تعليقه بالشرط؛ كذا ذكره العيني. وفي جامع الفصولين والوقف في رواية فظاهره أن في صحة تعليقه روايتين، وفي فتح كتاب الوقف وشرطه أن يكون منجزاً غير معلق فلو قال إن قدم ولدي فداري صدقة موقوفة على المساكين فجاء ولده لا يصير وقفاً .اهـ. وفي الإسعاف: ولو قال إذا جاء غدا وإذا جاء رأس الشهر أو قال إذا كلمت فلاناً أو إذا تزوجت فلانة وما أشبه ذلك فأرضي هذه صدقة موقوفة يكون الوقف باطلاً لأنه تعليق والوقف لا يحتمل التعليق بالخطر لكونه مما لا يحلف به بخلاف النذر لأنه يحتمل التعليق ويحلف به فلو قال إن برئت من مرضي هذا فأرضي صدقة موقوفة يلزمه التصدق بعينها إذا وجد الشرط، ولو قال صدقة موقوفة إن شئت أو أحببت أو رضيت أو هويت كان باطلاً .اهـ. ولم يذكر العيني صورة بطلانه بالشرط الفاسد وصورته ما في الإسعاف وقفها على أن له أصلها أو على أن يزول ملكه عنها أو على أصلها ويتصدق بثمنها كان الوقف باطلاً اهـ. يبيع وقدمنا في الوقف أن شرط الاستبدال صحيح على المفتى به قوله : (والتحكيم بأن يقول المحكمان إذا أهل الشهر أو قالا لعبد أو كافر، إذا أعتقت أو أسلمت فاحكم بيننا وهذا عند أبي يوسف وعند محمد يجوز تعليقه بشرط وإضافته إلى زمان كالوكالة والإمارة والقضاء. وله أن التحكيم تولية صورة وصلح معنى فباعتبار أنه صلح لا يصح تعليقه ولا إضافته وباعتبار أنه تولية يصح بالشك والاحتمال؛ ذكره العيني. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان من القضاء الفتوى على قول أبي يوسف. وقد فات المصنف إبطال الأجل. قال في البزازية : وإبطال الأجل يبطل بالشرط الفاسد بأن قال كلما حل نجم ولم تؤد فالمال حال صح وصار حالاً اهـ. وعبارة الخلاصة: وإبطال الأجل يبطل بالشرط الفاسد، ولو قال كلما دخل نجم فلم تؤد فالمال حال صح والمال يصير حالاً اهـ. فجعلهما مسألتين وهو الصواب. وأما قوله في البزازية «بأن قال تصويراً للأولى» فسهو ظاهر لأنه لو كان كذلك لبقي الأجل فكيف يقول صح فيتأمل. وفاته أيضاً تعليق الرد بالعيب فإنه باطل وله الرد كما في البزازية، وليس هو من القسم الأول لأنه لا يبطل بالشرط الفاسد كما ذكره المصنف في القسم الثاني ولا يصح تعليقه فهو كالنكاح. وبهذا علم المصنف فاته بيان ما لا يصح تعليقه ولا يبطل بالشرط الفاسد كما فاته ما يجوز تعليقه. قوله : (ولم يذكر العيني صورة بطلانه بالشرط الفاسد الخ) أقول في كونه مما يبطل بالشرط الفاسد نظر لما قدمه المؤلف من الأصل وهو أن ما كان مبادلة مال بغير مال أو كان من التبرعات لا يبطل بالشرط الفاسد والوقف من التبرعات وفي العزمية على الدرر : صرح قاضيخان بأن الوقف لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة ا.هـ. وقد يجاب أن الشرط الفاسد إنما لا يبطل التبرعات إذا لم يكن موجباً نقض أصله. فإن اشتراط أن تبقى رقبة الأرض له أو أنه لا يزول ملكه عنها أو أنه على أصله بلا استبدال شيء مكانها نقض للتبرع لأنه بذلك الشرط لم يوجد التبرع أصلاً كما إذا قال في الهبة وهبتك هذه الدار بشرط أن لا تخرج عن ملكي بخلاف ما إذا قال بشرط أن تخدمني سنة تأمل.
Book of Sale, Chapter of Miscellaneous Matters. From al-Nihayah, here that suspended iqrar is void, and transmitted from al-Muhit that iqrar is valid and the condition is void, and transmitted from al-Mabsut what supports al-Muhit, so apparently it is preferred, but the truth is to weaken it because they explicitly stated here that iqrar and waqf cannot be suspended with a condition and that they become invalid with a corrupt condition. His statement: (And waqf) by saying 'I have endowed my house if so-and-so arrives' or 'I have endowed my house upon you if you inform me of so-and-so's arrival' because it is not something one swears by, so its suspension with a condition is not valid; thus mentioned by al-Ayni. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn, waqf according to one narration, so apparently there are two narrations about the validity of its suspension. And in Fath Kitab al-Waqf, its condition is that it be immediate, not suspended. So if he says 'If my son arrives, my house is a sadaqah endowed upon the poor' and his son arrives, it does not become a waqf. In al-Is'af: And if he says 'When tomorrow comes' or 'When the beginning of the month comes' or 'If I speak to so-and-so' or 'If I marry so-and-so' and the like, 'this land of mine is a sadaqah endowed,' the waqf is void because it is a suspension, and waqf does not bear suspension by risk because it is not something one swears by, unlike a vow because it bears suspension and one swears by it. So if he says 'If I recover from this illness, my land is a sadaqah endowed,' it is necessary for him to give it in charity when the condition occurs. And if he says 'A sadaqah endowed if you wish, or desire, or are pleased, or love,' it is void. Al-Ayni did not mention the form of its invalidation by a corrupt condition, and its form is what is in al-Is'af: that he endows it on condition that he retains its original ownership, or that his ownership does not cease, or that he retains its original and gives its price in charity, the waqf is void. The author said: 'and we have previously mentioned in waqf that the condition of substitution is valid according to the fatwa.' His statement: (And tahkim) by the two arbitrators saying 'When the month begins' or they say to a slave or an unbeliever, 'If you are freed or become Muslim, then judge between us,' and this is according to Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad, its suspension by a condition and its addition to a time are permissible, like agency, governorship, and judgeship. He (Muhammad) has that tahkim is a delegation in form and a compromise in meaning. So, considering it is a compromise, its suspension and addition are not valid; considering it is a delegation, it is valid by doubt and probability; mentioned by al-Ayni. And in Fatawa Qadikhan from the chapter of judiciary, the fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's statement. The author also missed (the ruling of) ibtal al-ajal. He said in al-Bazzaziyyah: And ibtal al-ajal becomes invalid with a corrupt condition, by saying 'Whenever a installment comes due and you do not pay, the entire amount becomes due immediately' - it is valid and the amount becomes due immediately. And the expression of al-Khulasah: And ibtal al-ajal becomes invalid with a corrupt condition, and if he says 'Whenever an installment enters and you do not pay, the amount becomes due immediately' - it is valid and the amount becomes due immediately. So he made them two issues, which is correct. As for his statement in al-Bazzaziyyah 'by saying' as a depiction of the first, it is an apparent oversight because if it were so, the deferment would remain; how then does he say 'it is valid'? So contemplate. He also missed the suspension of the option of defect (khiyar al-ayb), for it is void and he (the buyer) has the right of return, as in al-Bazzaziyyah. It is not of the first category because it is not invalidated by a corrupt condition as the author mentioned in the second category, nor is its suspension valid; so it is like marriage. By this, the author missed the explanation of what cannot be suspended and is not invalidated by a corrupt condition, just as he missed what can be suspended. His statement: (And he did not mention al-Ayni the form of its invalidation by a corrupt condition etc.) I say regarding its being invalidated by a corrupt condition, there is consideration based on what the author presented as the principle, which is that what is an exchange of property for non-property or is from voluntary donations is not invalidated by a corrupt condition, and waqf is from voluntary donations. And in al-Azimiyyah on al-Durar: Qadikhan explicitly stated that waqf is not invalidated by corrupt conditions. And it can be answered that a corrupt condition only does not invalidate voluntary donations if it does not necessitate nullifying its essence. For stipulating that the corpus of the land remains his, or that his ownership does not cease, or that it remains as it is without substitution of something in its place, nullifies the donation because with that condition the donation did not occur at all, as if he said in gift: 'I have gifted you this house on condition that it does not leave my ownership,' unlike if he said 'on condition that you serve me for a year.' Consider.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining which contracts become invalid when a corrupt condition (shart fasad) is attached, and which remain valid with the condition being void. The commentator begins with iqrar (acknowledgment): a suspended iqrar is invalid according to al-Nihayah, but there is a narration from al-Muhit that it is valid, and the commentator prefers the view of invalidity because iqrar is not something one swears by, similar to waqf. For waqf, the ruling is that it cannot be suspended because it is not a form of oath; it is an immediate transfer of ownership. The text mentions two narrations regarding the validity of suspension, but the relied-upon position is that suspension invalidates the waqf. The commentator then discusses corrupt conditions such as stipulating that the donor retains ownership, which makes the waqf void because it contradicts the essence of waqf. For tahkim (arbitration), there is a dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: Abu Yusuf does not allow suspension, while Muhammad allows it by analogy with agency. The fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view. For ibtal al-ajal (annulment of deferment), a condition that accelerates the debt upon default is valid and does not invalidate the underlying contract; however, the condition itself is a form of ibtal al-ajal, which is a contract that is invalidated by a corrupt condition. The commentator clarifies the correct depiction of this issue. Finally, the commentator criticizes the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq for omitting the category of things that are not invalidated by a corrupt condition nor can be suspended, such as the option of defect (khiyar al-ayb), which is like marriage in that respect. Throughout, the commentator relies on the principle that contracts involving exchange of property (mu'awadat maliyyah) are affected by corrupt conditions related to riba, while non-compensatory contracts (tabarru'at) are not invalidated by such conditions, unless the condition negates the essence of the donation.

Key Terms
التحكيم (al-tahkim): Arbitration: disputants appoint a third party to judge their dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for Abu Yusuf ruling that suspended tahkim is invalid?
A) Because it is a delegation (tawliyah).
B) Because it is a compromise (sulh).
C) Because it is a sale (bay').
D) Because it is a gift (hibah).

Key Takeaway
Suspended tahkim is invalid per the fatwa because its meaning as a compromise overrides its form as a delegation.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Ibtal al-Ajal (Acceleration Clause): Valid Condition, Valid Contract
Commentary clarifying the validity of acceleration clauses in sale/debt contracts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that a condition accelerating a debt upon default (ibṭāl al-ajal) is valid and does not invalidate the underlying contract.

Core Idea
Acceleration clause is valid; the debtor forfeits deferment upon default.

Ibtal al-ajal is a clause that stipulates if the debtor misses an installment, the entire debt becomes due immediately. Some might think such a condition is corrupt because it changes the agreed term. This lesson clarifies that the condition is valid and the contract remains sound. The passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq corrects a mis formulation in some texts and distinguishes two versions of the clause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on ibtal al-ajal with a condition
What is the ruling when a creditor says: 'Whenever an installment comes due and you do not pay, the entire amount becomes due immediately'? The text says it is valid (sahih) and the entire amount becomes due.
2
Understand the two formulations
Al-Bazzaziyyah gives one phrasing: 'by saying...' al-Khulasah gives another: 'Whenever an installment enters and you do not pay...' The commentator notes that these are two distinct issues, and the first phrasing from al-Bazzaziyyah is a slip.
3
Recognize that the condition is not corrupt
Why is this condition not considered corrupt (shart fasad)? Because it is a valid stipulation that does not invalidate the original contract; it merely accelerates the debt upon breach of payment.
4
Distinguish from other cases
This is different from conditions that invalidate contracts (like suspended waqf or tahkim). Here the underlying sale or loan contract remains valid; only the deferment is canceled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيع باب المتفرقات عن النهاية كما هنا أن الإقرار المعلق باطل، ونقل عن المحيط أن الإقرار صحيح والشرط باطل، ونقل عن المبسوط ما يشهد للمحيط فظاهره ترجيحه والحق تضعيفه لتصريحهم هنا بأن الإقرار Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining which contracts become invalid when a corrupt condition (shart fasad) is attached, and which remain valid with the condition being void. The commentator begins with iqrar (acknowledgment): a suspended iqrar is invalid according to al-Nihayah, but there is a narration from al-Muhit that it is valid, and the commentator prefers the view of invalidity because iqrar is not something one swears by, similar to waqf. For waqf, the ruling is that it cannot be suspended because it is not a form of oath; it is an immediate transfer of ownership. The text mentions two narrations regarding the validity of suspension, but the relied-upon position is that suspension invalidates the waqf. The commentator then discusses corrupt conditions such as stipulating that the donor retains ownership, which makes the waqf void because it contradicts the essence of waqf. For tahkim (arbitration), there is a dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: Abu Yusuf does not allow suspension, while Muhammad allows it by analogy with agency. The fatwa is on Abu Yusuf's view. For ibtal al-ajal (annulment of deferment), a condition that accelerates the debt upon default is valid and does not invalidate the underlying contract; however, the condition itself is a form of ibtal al-ajal, which is a contract that is invalidated by a corrupt condition. The commentator clarifies the correct depiction of this issue. Finally, the commentator criticizes the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq for omitting the category of things that are not invalidated by a corrupt condition nor can be suspended, such as the option of defect (khiyar al-ayb), which is like marriage in that respect. Throughout, the commentator relies on the principle that contracts involving exchange of property (mu'awadat maliyyah) are affected by corrupt conditions related to riba, while non-compensatory contracts (tabarru'at) are not invalidated by such conditions, unless the condition negates the essence of the donation.

Key Terms
إبطال الأجل (ibṭāl al-ajal): A clause that cancels the deferment of a debt, making it due immediately upon a specified event (e.g., default).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a condition in a sale contract that says: 'If you fail to pay any installment, the entire price becomes due immediately'?
A) The condition is invalid and the contract is fasid.
B) The condition is valid and the contract remains sahih.
C) The condition is valid only if the buyer agrees after default.
D) The condition is invalid but the contract remains valid.

Key Takeaway
Acceleration clauses (ibṭāl al-ajal) are valid and enforceable; the contract remains sound.

Contracts Not Invalidated by a Corrupt Condition: The Hanafi Distinction
Listing contracts valid despite corrupt conditions, with proof and objection handling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which Hanafi contracts are not invalidated by a corrupt condition and explain why, using the principle that corrupt conditions only affect financial exchanges.

Core Idea
A corrupt condition voids only financial exchanges; other contracts stand, condition void.

The Hanafi school holds that corrupt conditions (shurut fasidah) do not always invalidate a contract. This lesson from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies that corrupt conditions are akin to riba, which only pertains to financial exchanges (mubadalah maliyyah). Thus, contracts like loans, gifts, marriage, divorce, and others that are not financial exchanges remain valid despite a corrupt condition; the condition is void but the contract is sound. The commentator also addresses a seeming inconsistency: why do some non-financial acts (e.g., dismissal of an agent) become invalid when conditioned? The answer lies in distinguishing between corruption by condition and the invalidity of the suspension itself (ta'liq).

Guided Path
1
Identify the contracts listed
List the contracts mentioned: qard (loan), hibah (gift), nikah (marriage), talaq (divorce), khul', itq (emancipation), rahn (pledge), isa' (gift of a house), wasiyyah (bequest), etc. Note that they are not financial exchanges.
2
Understand the ta'lil (legal basis)
The commentator states: 'corrupt conditions are from the category of riba, and it is specific to financial exchange.' This means the prohibition of corrupt conditions is tied to riba, which only applies when property is exchanged for property. Non-financial contracts are outside this scope.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) based on the nature of riba.
3
Distinguish between corruption by condition and invalid suspension
The commentator anticipates an objection: why do acts like 'azl al-wakil' (dismissal of an agent), i'tikaf, and raj'ah (revocable divorce) become invalid when conditioned, even though they are not financial exchanges? He clarifies that those become invalid not because of the condition per se, but because the suspension itself is invalid (the contract cannot be suspended). Thus, we must separate two issues: (a) a contract that is valid despite a corrupt condition, and (b) a contract whose suspension by a condition is invalid.
E.g., marriage cannot be suspended (ta'liq), so a marriage conditioned on something is valid but the condition is void. But an agency can be suspended, so a conditioned dismissal is valid if the condition occurs.
4
Apply the rule to examples
For each contract type, state the ruling: the contract is valid (sahih) and the condition is void (batil). For example, a loan on condition of service: loan valid, condition void. A marriage on condition of no dower: marriage valid, proper dower due. Bequest on condition of doing X: bequest valid, condition void. Also note the exception: some contracts like marriage cannot be suspended, so if the condition is phrased as a suspension (e.g., 'I marry you if X'), the suspension itself is invalid, but the contract is valid.
The commentator notes that the author of the matn missed explicit mention of which contracts cannot be suspended, but the branches cover it.

The author's statement: (And what is not invalidated by a corrupt condition) i.e., it is valid and not invalidated even if restricted by a corrupt condition, and this is the counterpart of his statement first 'what is invalidated by a corrupt condition' and he did not mention the counterpart of the second rule, which is his statement first 'and its suspension becomes invalid' – being content with what he mentioned here of the branches, for among them are those whose suspension becomes invalid by the condition and among them are those that do not become invalid, and most of them are not invalidated by suspension, such as divorce, bequest, guardianship, hawalah, agency, loan, pledge, judgeship, suretyship, permission to trade, and acknowledgment of a child. Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's list of contracts that are not invalidated by a corrupt condition. The commentator explains that corrupt conditions (shurut fasidah) are essentially a form of riba, which only applies to financial exchanges (mu'awadat maliyyah). Contracts that are not financial exchanges, such as loans (qard), gifts (hibah), marriage (nikah), divorce (talaq), etc., are not invalidated by such conditions; instead, the condition is void and the contract remains valid. For example, if someone lends money on condition that the borrower works for him, the loan is valid but the condition is not binding. Similarly, a marriage contracted on condition of no dower is valid with the condition void, and the wife receives her proper dower (mahr al-mithl). The commentator then addresses an objection: why are some non-financial acts like dismissal of an agent (azl al-wakil), i'tikaf, and revocable divorce (رجعة) invalidated by conditions? He answers that those are not invalidated because of the corrupt condition per se, but because the suspension (ta'liq) itself is invalid. The author of the matn missed distinguishing between contracts that are invalidated by a corrupt condition and those that are only invalid in terms of suspension. The commentator clarifies that contracts like divorce, bequest, guardianship, hawalah, agency, etc., are not invalidated by suspension either. The discussion ends with a note on the loan condition of repayment in a different currency (Iraq) being corrupt, and general remarks that the author's omission is only in expression, not substance.

Key Terms
مبادلة مالية (mubadalah maliyyah): A financial exchange where property is traded for property, like buying and selling.
تعليق بالشرط (ta'liq bi al-shart): Suspending the effect of a contract upon the occurrence of a future condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The loan is invalid because the condition is corrupt.
B) The loan is valid but the condition is void.
C) The loan is valid and the condition is binding.
D) The loan is invalid if the service is not performed.

Key Takeaway
Contracts that are not financial exchanges remain valid despite a corrupt condition; the condition is void but does not affect the contract's validity.

Contracts Not Invalidated by Fasid Conditions
Ruling with proof: explanation of principle and examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that fasid conditions only invalidate financial exchange contracts, and distinguish between fasid conditions and ta'liq.

Core Idea
Fasid conditions affect only financial exchanges; other contracts remain valid with the condition void.

In Hanafi fiqh, a fasid condition (e.g., one involving riba) does not necessarily void the contract. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq lists nine contracts—loan, gift, marriage, divorce, khul', emancipation, pledge, encharging, bequest—that remain valid even if a fasid condition is inserted. The key principle is that riba-related rules apply only to financial exchanges (mu'awadat maliyya). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying conditions in various contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the listed contracts
Read through the contracts: qard (loan), hibah (gift), nikah (marriage), talaq (divorce), khul' (divorce by redemption), itq (emancipation), rahn (pledge), iysa' (encharging), wasiyya (bequest). Each is explicitly stated as not invalidated by a fasid condition.
2
Understand the rationale
The commentator explains that fasid conditions are akin to riba, which is specific to financial exchange contracts. Since these contracts are not financial exchanges, the condition does not affect validity; it becomes void itself. This is a foundational Hanafi usul principle.
The term 'riba' here is used broadly to refer to any unlawful gain through conditions.
3
Analyze the examples
For each contract, a specific example is given. For instance, marriage with a condition of no dower or option for the husband—marriage valid, condition void. Work through these to see how the rule applies in practice.
Note that marriage does not accept suspension (ta'liq), but a simple condition within a valid contract is different.
4
Compare with Shafi'i position
The passage notes that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a fasid condition invalidates the pledge itself. Understand the practical difference: Hanafi says pledge valid, condition void; Shafi'i says pledge invalid.
This ikhtilaf is a legitimate difference in methodology.
5
Distinguish fasid condition from ta'liq
The commentator addresses a potential objection: why do conditions invalidate dismissal of an agent, i'tikaf, and ruj'a? These are not financial exchanges. The answer is that those are cases of ta'liq (suspension), not a fasid condition within a binding contract. Ta'liq can invalidate certain contracts like marriage.
This nuance prevents confusion between suspending a contract and adding a condition to it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

بمحضر من الشهود فقالت المرأة لي فقال الرجل ليس لك زوج فقالت المرأة إن لم يكن لي زوج فقد زوجت نفسي منك وقبل الزوج ولم يكن لها زوج قالوا: يجوز هذا النكاح لأن التعليق بشرط كائن تنجيز اهـ. وفي جامع الفصولين: تعليق النكاح بكائن تنجيز لو قال الأب زوجتك ابنتي إن لم أكن زوجتها فقبل صح. قوله: (والطلاق) بأن قال طلقتك على أن لا تتزوجي غيري. قوله: (والخلع) بأن قال خالعتك على أن يكون لي الخيار مدة سماها بطل الشرط ووقع الطلاق ووجب المال، وأما اشتراط الخلع لها فصيح عند الإمام كما مضى. قوله: (والعتق) بأن قال أعتقتك على أني بالخيار. قوله: (والرهن) بأن قال رهنت عندك عبدي بشرط أن استخدمه، ومن هذا القبيل ما And that which is not invalidated by a corrupt condition: loan, gift, marriage, divorce, khul', emancipation, pledge, encharging, and bequest. That is because corrupt conditions are of the category of riba, and it is specific to financial exchange, and all these contracts are not financial exchanges, so corrupt conditions do not affect them, mentioned by al-'Ayni. It is said to him: Then how is the dismissal of an agent, i'tikaf, and revocation invalidated by conditions, even though they are not financial exchanges? In al-Bazzaziyya: Suspension of a loan is prohibited and the condition is not binding. His statement: (Gift) such as saying 'I gift you this slave girl on condition that her pregnancy is mine.' His statement: (Marriage) such as saying 'I marry you on condition that you have no dower' — the marriage is valid, the condition is corrupt, and the proper dower is obligatory, as known in its place. And of this type is if he said 'I marry you with the option for me' — the marriage is valid and the option is not valid because he did not suspend the marriage on the condition, so the option becomes void; as in al-Khaniyya. And it will come that marriage cannot be suspended on a condition, and upon this is based what is in al-Khaniyya: 'I marry you if my father permits or approves' and she said 'I accept' — no, because it is a suspension and marriage does not accept suspension. Added in al-Zahiriyya: If the father was present in the session and approved, it is permissible. In al-Khaniyya: A man married a woman on the condition that he is a Madani, and he turned out to be a Qarawi — the marriage is valid if he is a suitable match and she has no option. A man asked a woman for marriage in the presence of witnesses, and the woman said 'I have a husband', the man said 'You have no husband', the woman said 'If I have no husband, I have married myself to you', and the husband accepted, and she had no husband — they said: This marriage is permissible because the suspension on an existing condition is an immediate effect. End. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: Suspension of marriage on an existing condition is immediate effect: if the father said 'I marry you my daughter if I have not married her' and he accepted, it is valid. His statement: (Divorce) such as saying 'I divorce you on condition that you do not marry anyone else.' His statement: (Khul') such as saying 'I divorce you by khul' on condition that I have an option for a specified period' — the condition is void, the divorce occurs, and the compensation is obligatory. As for stipulating the option for her, it is valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa, as passed. His statement: (Emancipation) such as saying 'I free you on condition that I have the option.' His statement: (Pledge) such as saying 'I pledge my slave to you on condition that I use him' — and of this type is what is in the pledge chapter of al-Bazzaziyya: He said 'He took a pledge from him on condition that if it is lost, it is lost without anything' and the pledgor said 'yes' — it becomes a pledge, the condition is void, and it is lost with the debt. Then he said: 'If I pay you your goods by such-and-such date, otherwise the pledge is for your property' — the condition is void and the pledge is valid. And al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: The pledge is also invalidated. End. His statement: (Encharging and bequest) such as saying 'I bequeath to you one third of my wealth if so-and-so approves'; mentioned by al-'Ayni. But there is consideration in it because it is an example of its suspension on a condition, and the discussion now is that it is not invalidated by a corrupt condition. In al-Bazzaziyya: Its suspension on a condition is permissible because it is in reality establishing a succession at death. End.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The matn states: 'That which is not invalidated by a corrupt condition: loan, gift, marriage, divorce, khul', emancipation, pledge, encharging, and bequest.' The commentator then provides the underlying rationale: corrupt conditions (shurut fasida) belong to the category of riba (usury/interest), and riba-related rules are specific to financial exchange contracts (mu'awadat maliyya). Since the listed contracts are not financial exchanges, a corrupt condition does not invalidate them; rather, the condition is void and the contract remains valid. This is a key Hanafi principle distinguishing between financial and non-financial contracts. The commentator anticipates an objection: if corrupt conditions only affect financial exchanges, then why do conditions invalidate the dismissal of an agent, i'tikaf, and revocation (ruj'a)? These are not financial exchanges either. The answer, implied by referring to al-Bazzaziyya, is that the issue here is about suspension (ta'liq) of the contract itself, not merely a condition within it. The contract may be invalidated by suspension but not by a corrupt condition within a valid contract. The passage then elaborates on each contract type with examples: for gift, a condition that the seller retains ownership of a pregnancy is void but the gift is valid; for marriage, stipulating no dower or option for the husband is void but marriage stands with proper dower; for divorce, a condition restricting remarriage is void but divorce occurs; for khul', a stipulation of option for the husband is void but khul' is valid; for emancipation, a condition of option is void; for pledge (rahn), a condition that the pledgee uses the item or that loss is without liability is void but the pledge is valid. The commentator then notes a disagreement with al-Shafi'i, who holds that such a condition invalidates the pledge itself. Finally, for bequest (wasiyya), a condition requiring another's approval is valid as a suspension (ta'liq), not a corrupt condition, because bequest is like establishing a succession at death.

Key Terms
الشرط الفاسد (al-shart al-fasid): A condition that is legally invalid, often involving riba or contrary to the nature of the contract.
المبادلة المالية (al-mubadalah al-maliyyah): A financial exchange contract, like sale, where property is exchanged for property.
التعليق (al-ta'liq): Suspending a contract's effect on a future event or condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone says 'I marry you on condition that I have the option to revoke', what is the ruling?
A) The marriage is invalid because the condition is fasid.
B) The marriage is valid but the option is void.
C) Both marriage and option are valid.
D) The marriage is valid only if the wife agrees.

Key Takeaway
Fasid conditions only invalidate financial exchange contracts; all other contracts remain valid with the condition void.

Condition in Partnership – Valid vs. Invalid
Discusses conditions in partnership contracts with examples and a proof from al-Dhakhira.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a condition that invalidates a partnership agreement and a voluntary act that does not, using the proof from al-Dhakhira.

Core Idea
A voluntary act after a partnership contract is not a condition; it does not affect the profit-sharing agreement.

In partnership contracts, the Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between conditions that are integral to the agreement and separate acts that occur after the contract is formed. This passage illustrates that with a real incident: two partners agreed on equal profit despite unequal capital, and the richer partner later voluntarily did extra work. The author shows that this voluntary act does not invalidate the profit-sharing condition, and he supports this with an analogy from the law of sale. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying partnership rulings in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the incident and the core issue
Read the passage and locate the incident where two partners have unequal capital but stipulate equal profit, and the richer partner voluntarily performs the work. Recognize that the legal question is whether this voluntary work invalidates the profit-sharing condition.
The incident is described right after the quote from al-Bazzaziyya.
2
Understand the precedent from al-Bazzaziyya
The earlier ruling states that if work is stipulated on the richer partner but profit is equal, the condition is invalid and profit must be proportional to capital. This is an example of a condition that contradicts the nature of partnership.
The condition was invalid because it was part of the contract.
3
Differentiate the incident from the precedent
In the incident, the work was not stipulated; it was voluntary. Therefore, the condition of equal profit remains valid. The key difference is that a condition must be explicitly stated as part of the contract.
Voluntary action (tabarru') is not a condition.
4
Examine the proof from al-Dhakhira
The author cites a sale case: after buying wood, the buyer says 'carry it to my home' without making it a condition. This separate statement does not invalidate the sale. Similarly, voluntary work after partnership is not a condition.
The proof uses qiyas: separate statements after a contract do not affect its validity.
5
Apply the principle to analogous cases
The author extends to rental: if after a rental contract one says 'the plowing is on the tenant,' it is not a condition. Generalize: any statement made after a contract, without being integral, does not invalidate.
Many fiqh issues derive from this distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والشركة) بأن قال شاركتك على أن تهديني ومن هذا القبيل ما في شركة البزازية : لو شرطا العمل على أكثرهما مالاً والربح بينهما نصفين لم يجز الشرط والربح بينهما أثلاثاً اهـ. وقد وقعت حادثه توهم بعض حنفيه العصر أنها من هذا القبيل وليس كذلك تفاضلا هي. في المال وشرطا الربح بينهما نصفين ثم تبرع أفضلهما مالاً بالعمل فأجبت بأن الشرط صحيح لعدم اشتراط العمل على أكثر هما مالاً، والتبرع ليس من قبيل الشرط، والدليل عليه ما في بيوع الذخيرة : اشترى حطباً في قرية شراء صحيحاً وقال موصولاً بالشراء من غير شرط في الشراء احمله إلى منزلي لا يفسد العقد لأن هذا ليس بشرط في البيع هو كلام مبتدأ بعد تمام البيع فلا يوجب فساده اهـ. فعلى هذا لو استأجر قرية أو أرضا للزراعة ثم قال بعد تمامها إن الحرث على المستأجر لا تفسد لأنه لم يكن شرطاً فيها وإنما يكون شرطاً لو قال على أن الحرث عليه فليحفظ هذا فإنه يخرج عليه كثير من المسائل
His statement: (And partnership) that he said: I partner with you on condition that you give me a gift. And of this category is what is in Shirkat al-Bazzaziyya: If they stipulate work on the one with more capital, and the profit is half-half, the condition is not valid and the profit is according to thirds. End. And an incident occurred that some contemporary Hanafis thought it was of this category, but it is not so; they were equal in capital? Actually, they differed in capital and stipulated profit half-half, then the one with more capital voluntarily did the work. So I answered that the condition is valid because they did not stipulate work on the one with more capital, and voluntary action is not a condition. The proof for this is what is in Buyu' al-Dhakhira: He bought firewood in a village with a valid purchase and said, connected to the purchase without a condition in the purchase, 'carry it to my home' – this does not invalidate the contract because this is not a condition in the sale; it is a separate speech after the completion of the sale, so it does not cause its invalidity. End. According to this, if someone rented a village or land for cultivation and then said after its completion, 'the plowing is on the tenant,' it does not invalidate because it was not a condition in it; it would be a condition only if he said 'on condition that the plowing is on him.' So remember this, for many issues derive from it.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage discusses conditions in partnership. It begins by quoting the matn: 'والشركة' meaning the section on partnership. The commentator gives an example: one says 'I partner with you on condition that you give me a gift.' This is a condition that benefits one partner exclusively, which is not permissible in partnership because profit should be proportional to capital or work. The ruling from al-Bazzaziyya is that if the partners stipulate that the work is on the partner with more capital, but the profit is half, the condition is invalid; the profit must be adjusted according to capital (here, thirds because the capital ratio is 1:2). Then a modern incident: two partners had unequal capital but stipulated profit half; later the richer partner voluntarily did the work. The author ruled that the condition is valid because the work was not stipulated; it was a voluntary act. The proof from al-Dhakhira shows that a statement made after a contract is complete, without being a condition, does not affect the contract. Similarly, saying after a rental 'the plowing is on the tenant' is not a condition and does not invalidate. The key is to distinguish between a condition integrated into the contract and a separate statement.

Key Terms
الشركة (al-shirkah): Partnership; a contract between two or more persons to share capital and profits.
التبرع (al-tabarru'): Voluntary act; something done without being compelled or conditioned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the incident described in the passage, why did the author rule the condition valid even though the richer partner did all the work with profit split equally?
A) Because the work was stipulated in the contract.
B) Because the profit was already split according to capital.
C) Because the work was voluntary, not a condition.
D) Because the richer partner had more capital anyway.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi partnership law, a voluntary act after the contract does not invalidate profit-sharing terms that differ from capital contributions.

Refining the Proof: Two Narrations on Condition Attachment in Sales
Super-commentary on the proof from al-Dhakhira

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi narrations regarding attachment of a void condition to a contract and explain why the non-attachment view treats it as a non-binding promise.

Core Idea
If a void condition is mentioned after a contract, it does not attach; it remains a mere promise.

In the discussion of a wood purchase, a proof from al-Dhakhira was cited. The commentator in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that this proof should be understood within the context of two known narrations from the Hanafi school. The key distinction is whether a statement made after the contract becomes part of the contract as a condition or remains separate. This refinement shows that the earlier proof is valid only under one narration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text and the proof being refined
Locate the original proof from al-Dhakhira that is being commented on. The super-commentary quotes al-Nahr's interpretation of that proof.
The proof is about a wood sale where a condition was mentioned after the contract.
2
State the two Hanafi narrations
Understand the ikhtilaf: one narration says a void condition does not attach to the contract; the other says it does attach. Al-Nahr advises interpreting al-Dhakhira's proof in light of the first narration.
These narrations are both transmitted from Abu Hanifa or his companions.
3
Explain the consequence of non-attachment
If the condition does not attach, then the statement remains a mere promise (wa'd). Under Hanafi law, a promise is generally not legally binding unless it is a condition in the contract.
The text says: 'بقي مجرد وعد لا يلزم الوفاء به' (it remains a mere promise that does not require fulfillment).
4
Reflect on the commentator's instruction 'تأمل'
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq ends with 'فتأمل' (so reflect), signaling that this is a careful refinement and that the reader should understand the proof is not absolute but depends on which narration is followed.
This highlights the importance of knowing the ikhtilaf within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والدليل عليه ما في بيوع الذخيرة الخ) قال في النهر : والذي ينبغي حمل ما في الذخيرة على إحدى الروايتين من أنهما لو ألحقا به شرطاً فاسداً لا يلتحق، وعلى أنه لا يلتحق بقي مجرد وعد لا يلزم الوفاء به والله تعالى الموفق .اهـ. فتأمل.
His statement: (The proof for it is what is in Buyu' al-Dhakhira...). He said in al-Nahr: What is appropriate is to interpret what is in al-Dhakhira according to one of two narrations: that if they attached a void condition to it, it does not attach; and on the basis that it does not attach, it remains a mere promise that does not require fulfillment. And Allah is the Guide. End. So reflect.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This is a super-commentary on the proof that was cited earlier from al-Dhakhira regarding the wood purchase. The commentator from al-Nahr (likely Ibn Nujaym, the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) clarifies that the ruling in al-Dhakhira should be understood according to one of two narrations in the Hanafi school. The narration is about whether a void condition attached to a contract actually becomes part of the contract. One view is that it does not attach, so the contract remains pure. The other view is that it does attach but is void. The context of al-Dhakhira is that the buyer said 'carry it to my home' without making it a condition, so it is not a condition at all. The commenter advises that if the condition is not attached, it is just a promise, which is not binding. This refines the earlier proof by showing its basis in ijtihad.

Key Terms
الرواية (al-riwayah): A narration or transmitted opinion within the Hanafi school; there are multiple riwayat from the founders.
الوعد (al-wa'd): A promise; a statement that is not a condition and not legally binding in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary from al-Nahr, what is the status of a statement made after a contract that is not attached as a condition?
A) It is a binding condition.
B) It is a void condition that invalidates the contract.
C) It is a mere promise that does not require fulfillment.
D) It is considered part of the contract.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, post-contract statements are not automatically conditions; they may be non-binding promises depending on the narration adopted.

Conditions in Iqalah: Void vs Suspensive
Rules on conditions in iqalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on conditions in iqalah and apply the distinction between void conditions (which do not invalidate) and suspensive conditions (which invalidate).

Core Idea
Iqalah is rescission, not sale; void conditions do not break it, but suspending it on a condition is invalid.

In Hanafi fiqh, iqalah (mutual rescission of a sale) is treated as a rescission (faskh), not a new sale. This distinction is crucial for determining the effect of conditions. The passage clarifies that certain conditions, like agreeing to rescind for a different price, do not void the iqalah. However, if the iqalah is suspended on a future condition (e.g., 'I rescind if you lend me money'), it is invalid. We will analyze this rule and its practical applications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its nature
Recognize that iqalah is a rescission (faskh), not a new sale (bay'). This is the foundational distinction that drives the rules.
The Hanafi school holds this view; other schools may treat iqalah as a sale.
2
Distinguish void conditions from suspension
Separate conditions that are part of the rescission (e.g., rescinding for a different price) which do not invalidate, from conditions that suspend the rescission on a future event (e.g., 'if you lend me'), which do invalidate.
The text gives examples: rescinding for less than original price is valid; suspending on a loan is not.
3
Note the exception for options
Remember that stipulating an option (khiyar) in iqalah is permissible, as per al-Bazzaziyyah. This is not a suspension but a valid condition.
Options are part of the contract, not external suspensive conditions.
4
Apply the rule to kitabah
Extend the principle to kitabah (contract of manumission): conditions like not leaving the city are valid if they do not suspend the contract itself.
The passage hints that such conditions are valid because they are not suspensive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والإقالة بأن قال أقلتك هذا عن البيع إن أقرضتني؛ كذا ذكره العيني. وفي القنية : لا يصح تعليق الإقالة بالشرط وتقدم أنهما لو تقايلا بأقل من الثمن الأول أو بجنس آخر لم تفسد ووجب الثمن الأول وهو مثال أنها لا تبطل بالشروط الفاسدة، وأما ما ذكر فمثال تعليقها. وفي البزازية بجوز اشتراط الخيار فيها . صحيح قوله : (والكتابة) بأن قال المولى لعبده كاتبتك على ألف بشرط أن لا تخرج من البلد أو اشتراط الخيار للمحتال في كون ذلك من التعليق نظر بل هو شرط لكنه صحيح ليس مما نحن فيه تأمل . قوله : (وهذه واردة على إطلاق المصنف وغيره قال في النهر وجوابه أن هذا من المحتال وعد وليس الكلام فيه اهـ. ومراده من المحتال المحتال عليه لأنه قد تحذف صلته، وهذا الجواب غير ظاهر عن هذا لأن كونه وعداً لا يخرجه عن كونه شرطاً . قوله : (وأما ما ذكر) أي من قول العيني أقلتك البيع إن أقرضتني كذا ومراد المؤلف الاعتراض على العيني بأن المراد بيان ما لا يبطل بالشرط الفاسد، وما ذكره من المثال تعليق بالشرط والتعليق بالشرط لا . كما يصح ذكره في القنية. وذكر المؤلف في آخر باب الإقالة أن فائدة كون الإقالة فسخاً تظهر في خمس مسائل : الثانية منها أنها لا تبطل بالشروط المفسدة ولكن لا يصح تعليقها بالشرط كأن باع ثوراً من زيد فقال اشتريته رخيصاً فقال زيد إن وجدت مشترياً بالزيادة فبعه منه فوجد فباع بأزيد لا ينعقد البيع الثاني لأنه تعليق الإقالة لا الوكالة
His saying: (And rescission) that he says, 'I rescind this sale from you if you lend me'; as mentioned by al-Ayni. And in al-Qunyah: Suspending iqalah upon a condition is not valid. And it has preceded that if they rescind for less than the original price or for another type, it does not become void and the original price is obligatory, and this is an example that it is not invalidated by void conditions. As for what was mentioned, it is an example of suspending it. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: It is permissible to stipulate an option in it. Correct. His saying: (And kitabah) that the master says to his slave, 'I have contracted kitabah with you for a thousand on condition that you do not leave the city or stipulating an option for the creditor (muhtal) — regarding that being a suspension, there is consideration; rather it is a condition, but it is valid and not our topic here. Reflect. His saying: (And these [examples] contradict the absolute statement of the author and others) — he said in al-Nahr: The answer is that this is a promise from the muhtal and the discussion is not about it. And his meaning by muhtal is the muhtal 'alayh (transferee), because its relation may be omitted. And this answer is not apparent because being a promise does not remove it from being a condition. His saying: (And as for what was mentioned) meaning from the saying of al-Ayni, 'I rescind the sale from you if you lend me' — the author intends to object to al-Ayni that the intent is to explain what is not invalidated by a void condition, and what he mentioned is a suspension by condition, and suspension by condition is not valid, as mentioned in al-Qunyah. And the author mentioned at the end of the chapter on iqalah that the benefit of iqalah being a rescission appears in five issues: the second of them is that it is not invalidated by corrupting conditions, but its suspension by a condition is not valid. For example, if he sold an ox to Zayd and said, 'I bought it cheap,' and Zayd said, 'If you find a buyer at a higher price, sell it to him,' and he found and sold at a higher price, the second sale is not concluded because it is a suspension of iqalah, not agency.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage discusses conditions in iqalah (rescission of a sale). The author notes that iqalah is a rescission (faskh), not a new sale. Suspending iqalah on a condition (e.g., 'I rescind if you lend me') is not valid, as stated in al-Qunyah. However, if the parties agree to rescind for a different price or type, it does not void the iqalah; the original price remains due. This shows that iqalah is not invalidated by void conditions (like changing the price), but it cannot be suspended on a future condition. There is also a mention from al-Bazzaziyyah that stipulating an option in iqalah is permissible. The author then discusses a nuance: some situations may appear to be suspension but are actually valid conditions (e.g., a promise). He also notes an objection to al-Ayni's example, clarifying that the example of 'I rescind if you lend' is a suspension, which is invalid, conflicting with the general statement that iqalah is not invalidated by conditions. The author resolves that iqalah is not invalidated by conditions that are part of the transaction (like changing the price), but external conditions that suspend it are invalid.

Key Terms
إقالة (iqalah): Rescission of a sale; mutual agreement to cancel the sale and return the goods/price.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission; annulment of a contract.
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspending a contract or ruling on a future condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is true about iqalah?
A) It is invalidated by any condition.
B) It is invalidated by suspensive conditions but not by void conditions like price changes.
C) It is always valid regardless of conditions.
D) It is treated as a new sale.

Key Takeaway
Iqalah is a rescission, not a sale; void conditions do not break it, but suspending it on a condition makes it invalid.
